Title: It's Time To End Federal Control Of Education And Restore Parental Authority
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">It's Time To End Federal Control Of Education And Restore Parental Authority</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><a href="https://amgreatness.com/2025/05/11/its-time-to-end-federal-control-of-education-and-restore-parental-authority/"><em>Authored by Sam Sorbo via American Greatness,</em></a></p>

<p>For decades, Americans have watched as federal involvement in education expanded, ballooning into a behemoth bureaucracy that imposes top-down mandates while divorcing parents from their rightful role as the primary educators of their children, while failing to achieve academic success for students.</p>

<p><strong>If we are serious about fixing our children’s education, we must restore parental authority and end federal control of education.</strong></p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-15_15-24-52.jpg?itok=1eHtTcqZ" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-15_15-24-52.jpg?itok=1eHtTcqZ"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="142b0d59-af28-4ca4-af1e-2e607b944eae" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="281" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/2025-05-15_15-24-52.jpg?itok=1eHtTcqZ" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p><strong>America’s Founding Fathers never intended for Washington, D.C., to dictate how children in Kansas or Kentucky learn to read, write, and think</strong>. Education was, and should be, a local and parental matter. President Donald Trump rightly stated in Executive Order 13985, <em>Combating Race and Sex Stereotyping</em>, “The experiment of controlling American education through federal programs and dollars…has plainly failed our children, our teachers, and our families.” That failure is clearly documented by the National Assessment of Educational Progress (NAEP), often referred to as “The Nation’s Report Card.” Even before the COVID-19 pandemic, NAEP scores had <a href="https://nces.ed.gov/nationsreportcard">stagnated or declined</a>. Today, nearly <strong>40% of fourth graders</strong> read <a href="https://nationsreportcard.gov/"><strong>below basic level</strong></a>, despite record federal funding. Billions of taxpayer dollars have produced declining literacy.</p>

<p><strong>It’s not just ineffective—it’s indefensible.</strong></p>

<p>Federal education initiatives have repeatedly promised results, especially for low-income students, but have failed to deliver. Programs like Title I and Head Start have cost hundreds of billions of dollars over the years with <a href="https://www.cato.org/">no consistent academic gains</a> to show for them. Similarly, federal control over college grants and loans has inflated tuition and <a href="https://www.newyorkfed.org/">buried young Americans</a> under a mountain of debt.</p>

<p><strong>The evidence is clear: centralized, bureaucratic control undermines education.</strong></p>

<p>As the founder of the “They’re YOUR Kids Foundation,” I work with parents every day who feel helpless. The system fails their children academically and often undermines their values. If we truly want to empower families, we must strip away the federal red tape and hand the reins back to those who know and love their children best: parents.</p>

<p>Representative Barry Moore of Alabama has proposed legislation (H.R. 2691, “Eliminate the Department of Education Act,” <a href="http://congress.gov/">Congress.gov</a>) to eliminate USED and redirect education funding based on what residents in each state pay in federal income taxes. But simply shifting USED’s functions to other agencies, as some proposals suggest, won’t solve the problem—it just moves the bureaucracy around.</p>

<p>That’s why I support the US Parents Involved in Education (USPIE) Blueprint: a five-step plan to close the U.S. Department of Education and return education governance to the states. The <a href="https://uspie.org/">Blueprint</a> is simple, sensible, and long overdue:</p>

<ol><li>
	<p>Return all program management and funding to the states.</p>
	</li>
	<li>
	<p>Repeal laws like the <em>Every Student Succeeds Act</em> (ESSA) that enable federal overreach.</p>
	</li>
	<li>
	<p>Privatize college loan programs through local financial institutions for increased accountability.</p>
	</li>
	<li>
	<p>Eliminate all divisions and spending within USED.</p>
	</li>
	<li>
	<p>Reduce federal tax collection so states retain education funds directly.</p>
	</li>
</ol><p>We have a singular opportunity to implement meaningful change, including a federal tax credit system that empowers parents to direct their own children’s education. Under this proposal:</p>

<ul><li>
	<p>Parents who homeschool or choose private education would receive a <strong>Child Tax Credit</strong> equal to the federal per-pupil expenditure.</p>
	</li>
	<li>
	<p>Federal taxpayers of households with children attending government schools would prompt their per-pupil allocation to be block-granted to their respective states.</p>
	</li>
</ul><p>This model respects choice while avoiding the pitfalls of government entanglement. Voucher programs, while well-intentioned, often bring government regulation with them. The 1980 Supreme Court ruling involving Hillsdale College affirmed that any institution accepting federal funds—even indirectly through student aid—is subject to federal control. [Grove City College v. Bell, 465 U.S. 555 (1984)] That’s the Trojan horse we must avoid.</p>

<p><strong>We must stop pretending we can reform federal education mandates and instead recognize them for what they are: unconstitutional, ineffective, and dangerous to parental rights.</strong></p>

<p>As a mother who homeschooled three children, I know firsthand the value of individualized learning guided by a parent who knows their child’s needs and aspirations. Education is not simply the memorization of facts or test preparation. It is the formation of character, virtue, curiosity, and conviction. That formation is best entrusted to families—not bureaucrats in Washington.</p>

<p>President Trump’s 2025 executive order declared that closing the Department of Education would “restore the proper role of families and local governments in education.” But that can only happen if we also change the funding structure and remove all federal strings. If not, we risk replacing one failed model with another, abandoning the nation’s most precious resource, and ultimately forfeiting our very future.</p>

<p>It’s time to reject the lie that Washington knows best. Parents are not the problem. They are the solution. Local communities, not federal mandates, are best equipped to nurture the next generation of citizens. And education must once again become the deeply personal, values-rooted family journey it was meant to be.</p>

<p><strong>We have a roadmap. We have legislation. And most importantly, we have an awakening of parents across this country who are saying, Enough is enough.</strong></p>

<p>Let’s seize this moment to make education truly free—by making it family-led.</p>
</div>
      <span rel="schema:author" class="field field--name-uid field--type-entity-reference field--label-hidden"><a title="View user profile." href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" lang="" about="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" typeof="schema:Person" property="schema:name" datatype="" class="username" xml:lang="">Tyler Durden</a></span>
<span property="schema:dateCreated" content="2025-05-16T03:00:00+00:00" class="field field--name-created field--type-created field--label-hidden">Thu, 05/15/2025 - 23:00</span>


Title: How Widespread Are Food Intolerances?
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">How Widespread Are Food Intolerances?</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p>In a limited survey by Statista Consumer Insights, between 6 and 17 percent of respondents said they had a food intolerance confirmed by a health professional. </p>

<p><a href="https://www.statista.com/chart/34469/share-of-respondents-with-food-intolerance/"><em>As Statista's Katharina Buchholz reports,</em></a> <strong>the figure was highest in the U.S. and lowest in France. </strong></p>

<p><a href="https://www.statista.com/chart/34469/share-of-respondents-with-food-intolerance/" title="Infographic: How Widespread Are Food Intolerances? | Statista"><img alt="Infographic: How Widespread Are Food Intolerances? | Statista" height="500" src="https://cdn.statcdn.com/Infographic/images/normal/34469.jpeg" style="max-width: 960px;" width="500" /></a> </p>

<p><em>You will find more infographics at <a href="https://www.statista.com/chartoftheday/">Statista</a></em></p>

<p><strong>In four other countries surveyed - the United Kingdom, Germany, Mexico and China - between 10 and 11 percent said this was the case for them.</strong></p>

<p><a href="https://www.statista.com/topics/4274/global-health/">Food intolerances and allergies,</a> like insensitivity to gluten, dairy, sugar or more specific products, have been a hot topic over the last couple of years.</p>

<p><strong>While more and more people cut certain foods out of their diets because of allergies or because they consider them bad nutrition, other accuse those engaging in this behavior of following a fad.</strong> </p>

<p>While awareness around food insensitivities has certainly risen and more people were able to get <a href="https://www.statista.com/topics/799/health/">diagnoses</a> in the field, hyperconsiousness around food, health and fitness are also becoming more widespread - with both areas increasingly harder to distingush from one another.</p>

<p><a href="https://www.nhs.uk/conditions/food-intolerance/">According to the UK's NHS,</a> <strong>common food intolerances include lactose, gluten, histamines and sulphites, </strong>but also caffeine, alcohol and lesser-known salicylates.</p>
</div>
      <span rel="schema:author" class="field field--name-uid field--type-entity-reference field--label-hidden"><a title="View user profile." href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" lang="" about="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" typeof="schema:Person" property="schema:name" datatype="" class="username" xml:lang="">Tyler Durden</a></span>
<span property="schema:dateCreated" content="2025-05-16T02:35:00+00:00" class="field field--name-created field--type-created field--label-hidden">Thu, 05/15/2025 - 22:35</span>


Title: New York To Send 'Inflation Refund' Checks To Eligible Residents
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">New York To Send 'Inflation Refund' Checks To Eligible Residents</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><a href="https://www.theepochtimes.com/us/new-york-to-send-inflation-refund-checks-to-eligible-residents-5858089?utm_source=partner&utm_campaign=ZeroHedge"><em>Authored by Rachel Acenas via The Epoch Times,</em></a></p>

<p>New York Gov. Kathy Hochul on Tuesday announced the state’s first-ever “inflation refund,” a one-time payment to eligible residents.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/image_51.jpg?itok=TXQnygOG" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/image_51.jpg?itok=TXQnygOG"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="af233046-c1d0-48f4-9c3e-6087e5d059e6" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="333" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/image_51.jpg?itok=TXQnygOG" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>Hochul said during a news conference that inflation has driven up costs for New Yorkers, and they should get that money back. The funding, according to the governor, will come from the money the state collected in higher sales taxes because of inflation.</p>

<blockquote>
<p><em><strong>“We collected more in sales tax as a result. Unanticipated revenue. I said, this can go into the state coffers, but why not give it to the residents whose pockets it came out of? They paid more than they ever expected. That’s the whole idea behind an inflation refund.”</strong></em></p>
</blockquote>

<p>Collectively, the one-time payment will put $2 billion back in the pockets of over eight million New York taxpayers, Hochul said. The amount of the payment would be based on filing status and income.</p>

<p>Joint tax filers who earn up to $150,000 will receive a $400 check, while those earning between $150,000 and $300,000 will get $300. Single tax filers with incomes up to $75,000 should expect to receive a $200 inflation refund check, and those earning between $75,000 and $150,000 will get a $150 check.</p>

<p>Hochul first proposed her plan of an inflation refund check last December and secured the funding in the fiscal year 2026 state budget agreement. Her initial plan called for higher refunds, specifically $300 for single filers making $150,000 or less, and $500 for joint filers making up to $300,000.</p>

<p>According to data from the <a href="https://www.bls.gov/regions/northeast/news-release/consumerpriceindex_newyork.htm">Consumer Price Index</a>, the New York area experienced the highest inflation rate in the country from April 2024 to April 2025, with a rate of 3.9 percent. New York’s rate was much higher than the national average, which was 2.3 percent in April 2025. The New York-Newark-Jersey City metro area experienced a 3.9 percent increase in prices, while core inflation reached 4.3 percent.</p>

<p><strong>In announcing the inflation refund plan, the governor signed a large check while announcing the inflation refund. “We got it done, everybody. We got it done,” she told supporters.</strong></p>

<p>Residents who qualify for the one-time payment don’t need to fill out an application or take any type of action, according to a <a href="https://www.governor.ny.gov/news/we-got-it-done-governor-hochul-celebrates-huge-budget-win-put-nearly-5000-back-pockets-working">news release</a> by the governor’s office. Rather, the state will automatically send them a check based on their 2023 tax filing. The checks will be mailed over a period of several weeks beginning in the fall of 2025.</p>

<p><strong>As part of the state budget, Hochul is also giving 1.6 million New York families an annual tax credit of up to $1,000 per child under age four and up to $500 per child from four through sixteen, marking the largest expansion of New York’s child tax credit in its history.</strong> The state budget agreement also includes her plan to cut taxes for more than 75 percent of all tax filers in the state.</p>

<p>United Way of New York City President and CEO Grace Bonilla said in a <a href="https://www.governor.ny.gov/news/we-got-it-done-governor-hochul-celebrates-huge-budget-win-put-nearly-5000-back-pockets-working">statement</a> in response to Hochul’s budget: </p>

<blockquote>
<p><em>“These changes will ease the burden on people who are already facing untenable challenges – forced to choose between feeding their children or paying bills.”</em></p>
</blockquote>

<p>According to United Way’s 2023 True Cost of Living <a href="https://unitedwaynyc.org/true-cost-of-living/">report</a>,<strong> 50 percent of working-age people in New York City are struggling to make ends meet.</strong></p>

<p>New York’s inflation refund checks are similar to California’s Middle Class Tax Refund program. That one-time payment was issued to eligible recipients between October 2022 and January 2023, to provide relief to residents in the state. California’s refund came in the form of a debit card that required activation.</p>
</div>
      <span rel="schema:author" class="field field--name-uid field--type-entity-reference field--label-hidden"><a title="View user profile." href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" lang="" about="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" typeof="schema:Person" property="schema:name" datatype="" class="username" xml:lang="">Tyler Durden</a></span>
<span property="schema:dateCreated" content="2025-05-16T02:10:00+00:00" class="field field--name-created field--type-created field--label-hidden">Thu, 05/15/2025 - 22:10</span>


Title: Water Wars: One-Fifth Of Pakistan's Electricity Comes From Hydro
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Water Wars: One-Fifth Of Pakistan's Electricity Comes From Hydro</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><strong>India has suspended the Indus Waters Treaty with Pakistan, a major water-sharing agreement brokered by the World Bank. </strong>The move came on April 23, within a day of a deadly shooting in Pahalgam, in the Indian-administered part of Kashmir, marking the first time the treaty has been paused since the pact’s inception in 1960. In response, Pakistan stated that an attempt to stop the flow of water would be considered an “act of war”. Tensions mounted between the two <a href="https://www.statista.com/chart/8301/the-countries-holding-the-worlds-nuclear-arsenal/">nuclear-armed nations</a> in the following weeks, breaking out into four days of fighting, before quelling again with a ceasefire mediated by the U.S. announced on Saturday, with both nations pulling back from the brink.</p>

<p><strong><a href="https://www.statista.com/chart/27272/water-conflicts/">Water resources</a> are an important part of the equation right now between the two countries. </strong>The <a href="https://www.statista.com/statistics/1612691/india-and-pakistan-distribution-of-water-according-to-iwt">Indus Waters Treaty (IWT)</a> divides the six main rivers of the Indus basin between the two nations, with the three westerly rivers — Indus, Jhelum and Chenab — supplying Pakistan with water, while the three easterly ones — Ravi, Beas and Sutlej — feed India.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/Water-War-2.3.jpg?itok=OIpylnIP" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/Water-War-2.3.jpg?itok=OIpylnIP"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="6f459356-1753-4d53-8740-ab2dc77828a0" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="281" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/Water-War-2.3.jpg?itok=OIpylnIP" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>According to <a href="https://www.abc.net.au/news/2025-05-14/india-suspends-indus-water-treaty-pakistan-tensions-water-war/105286366">reporting</a> by ABC,<strong> in addition to the suspension of the Indus Waters Treaty, India has also fast-tracked the construction of four new hydropower projects on rivers flowing into Pakistan and refused to share data on river flows with Islamabad.</strong> David Michel, Senior Fellow for the Global Food and Water Security Program at the Center for Strategic and International Studies, explains in an <a href="https://www.csis.org/analysis/can-india-cut-pakistans-indus-river-lifeline">analysis</a> that while India cannot completely stop the water flow to Pakistan in the near term due to its current infrastructure, it can stop the flow of information to its neighbor. He explains: </p>

<blockquote>
<p><em>“The IWT requires the parties to share a good deal of data on project development, river flows, and hydrological conditions. By suspending the treaty, India can also cease data sharing, depriving Pakistan of flood warnings, for example, prospectively hampering the nation’s water management and potentially imperiling Pakistani lives and livelihoods.”</em></p>
</blockquote>

<p>Observers cite concerns over India’s building of dams, including four which are on one of the westerly rivers intended to supply Pakistan, and flag the issue of what would happen to the flow of water to Pakistan if such infrastructure is expanded to enable more storage.</p>

<p><strong>Pakistan is dependent on the rivers of the Indus basin not only for some of its population’s drinking water, but also for agriculture, which accounts for almost a quarter of the country’s GDP, as well as for power.</strong> </p>

<p><a href="https://www.statista.com/chart/34459/pakistans-sources-of-electricity-generation/">As Statista's Anna Fleck shows in the chart below,</a> using <a href="https://www.iea.org/countries/pakistan/electricity">data</a> from the International Energy Agency (IEA) shows, 34.6 TWh of electricity in Pakistan was sourced from hydropower in 2022 (latest available data), all of which comes from the Indus basin. </p>

<p><a href="https://www.statista.com/chart/34459/pakistans-sources-of-electricity-generation/" title="Infographic: One-Fifth of Pakistan's Electricity Comes From Hydro | Statista"><img alt="Infographic: One-Fifth of Pakistan's Electricity Comes From Hydro | Statista" height="501" src="https://cdn.statcdn.com/Infographic/images/normal/34459.jpeg" style="max-width: 960px;" width="501" /></a> </p>

<p><em>You will find more infographics at <a href="https://www.statista.com/chartoftheday/">Statista</a></em></p>

<p><strong>This makes it the second most important energy source for electricity in the country</strong>, following only after natural gas (47 TWh or around 27 percent). </p>

<p>The next biggest energy sources are oil (16.6 percent), coal (15.9 percent and nuclear (15.6 percent).</p>

<p><em>Read more on the </em><a href="https://www.statista.com/topics/13485/india-pakistan-conflict/#topFacts"><em>India-Pakistan conflict 2025</em></a><em> and </em><a href="https://www.statista.com/chart/27272/water-conflicts/"><em>water conflicts in Asia</em></a><em>.</em></p>
</div>
      <span rel="schema:author" class="field field--name-uid field--type-entity-reference field--label-hidden"><a title="View user profile." href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" lang="" about="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" typeof="schema:Person" property="schema:name" datatype="" class="username" xml:lang="">Tyler Durden</a></span>
<span property="schema:dateCreated" content="2025-05-16T01:45:00+00:00" class="field field--name-created field--type-created field--label-hidden">Thu, 05/15/2025 - 21:45</span>


Title: "I Can't Understand My Professor"
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">"I Can't Understand My Professor"</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><em>By Rob Jenkins of <a href="https://www.mindingthecampus.org/2025/05/01/i-cant-understand-my-professor/">Minding the Campus</a></em></p>

<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">My colleague at </span><span style="font-weight: 400;">Minding the Campus</span><span style="font-weight: 400;">, Jared Gould, has </span><a href="https://www.mindingthecampus.org/2025/03/27/foreign-students-price-americans-out-of-their-own-workforce/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">written persuasively</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> on the problem of colleges and universities over-admitting foreign students, who can fill seats that should have gone to American students, drive up costs for everyone, and ultimately take jobs from American workers. </span></p>

<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">In my view, however, a more pressing issue—<strong>although one that is rarely broached, lest the complainant be labeled “xenophobic”</strong>—is that of foreign-born professors, especially those whose command of spoken English is, shall we say, less than optimal.</span></p>

<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">These days, institutions have come to rely more and more on non-native Ph.D.s. Just scan through the faculty roster at any American university and see how many names you can pronounce. This is a problem for some of the same reasons Jared mentions: Not only did many of these professors take grad-school seats from American students, they eventually took jobs that might have gone to American candidates.</span></p>

<p><em><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/cant%20undertstand%20prof.jpg?itok=9F2Sulib" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/cant%20undertstand%20prof.jpg?itok=9F2Sulib"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="ddada6e3-925f-446a-a64b-f0dbb2f1c053" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="374" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/cant%20undertstand%20prof.jpg?itok=9F2Sulib" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></em></p>

<p><span style="font-weight: 400;"><strong>There’s another problem with foreign-born professors, though, on an even more basic level: Students often struggle to understand them in class. </strong>If students literally can’t grasp what the professor is saying, due to a language barrier, how can they learn the material? Often, they resort to essentially teaching themselves, using textbooks, study groups, and online aids.</span></p>

<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The daughter of a good friend is currently in medical school at a large, highly respected Southeastern university. I had a chance to chat with her over the holidays and asked her how it was going. What she said frankly shocked me.</span></p>

<p><span style="font-weight: 400;"><strong>According to her, not a single one of her medical school professors, so far, has been American-born. </strong>All speak with thick accents, although some are clearer than others. Asking questions in class doesn’t help much, because she often can’t understand the answers. And she isn’t alone. Her classmates all have the same problem.   </span></p>

<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">So how are they supposed to learn this information that is presumably so important for doctors to know—information they will be tested over, repeatedly, throughout their years in medical school, culminating in board examinations?</span></p>

<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">This bright young woman, along with her classmates and many other medical students all over the country, has simply taken matters into her own hands, purchasing expensive software that covers the same material. She attends class religiously each day, then goes home and spends eight or ten more hours watching videos. Despite shelling out tens of thousands of dollars on an “elite” medical school education, she is essentially having to teach herself—all because her professors don’t speak clear English.</span></p>

<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">This is just one example of what seems to be a widespread problem. In my 40 years of college teaching and advising, I’ve had dozens of students complain to me that they have one or more professors they can’t understand, particularly in mathematics, engineering, and the hard sciences.</span></p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="https://store.zerohedge.com/rancher-direct-clean-food/" data-image-href="https://store.zerohedge.com/rancher-direct-clean-food/" data-link-option="2" href="https://store.zerohedge.com/rancher-direct-clean-food/"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="1d7c3fc7-867d-4ae7-baa0-cd61d4246985" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="134" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/TBI_Ad_1500x400px_MemorialDay_1%281%29.jpg?itok=1P4CS8m5" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p><strong><span style="font-weight: 400;">How did we get ourselves into this situation, and how can we get out of it?</span></strong></p>

<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The answer to the first question, which also suggests an answer to the second, is that we got here mainly by prioritizing research over teaching—in some cases, by a wide margin. Indeed, some of our most prestigious institutions seem to value research almost exclusively and teaching hardly at all. Almost any tenure-track professor at a Research 1 university will tell you that their annual evaluations and tenure bids are highly focused on research, publishing, and grant procurement, with teaching coming in a distant second, if that. In other words, if a candidate is an accomplished researcher or has the potential to be, schools don’t really care if students can understand them or not.</span></p>

<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The simple solution is for institutions to prioritize teaching, or at least make it equal to research. Honestly, most of what passes for “research” these days is either </span><a href="https://www.chronicle.com/article/diminishing-returns-in-humanities-research/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">derivative naval-gazing</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> or </span><a href="https://www.campusreform.org/article/prof-jenkins-plagiarism-just-tip-iceberg/24832"><span style="font-weight: 400;">unreproducible nonsense</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">; only a relative handful of professors are doing truly groundbreaking work in any field. The rest should be expected to teach more and publish less, and be evaluated accordingly. Departments, too, should be judged primarily on how well students learn in their classes, not on how many journal articles they produce or how much grant money they generate.</span></p>

<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">With a renewed emphasis on teaching, departments might start to care a little more about whether students can actually understand their professors and make that an integral part of the screening process for new faculty. Some institutions already do this, but every candidate for a faculty position should have to give a public presentation that students are encouraged to attend—bribed with food, if necessary—and their opinions solicited.</span></p>

<p><span style="font-weight: 400;"><strong>In that way, perhaps we can eventually move beyond this frankly untenable situation in which even our brightest students sometimes struggle to pick up on important concepts.</strong> We might be pleasantly surprised at how much and how fast they learn once they actually understand what their professors are saying.</span></p>
</div>
      <span rel="schema:author" class="field field--name-uid field--type-entity-reference field--label-hidden"><a title="View user profile." href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" lang="" about="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" typeof="schema:Person" property="schema:name" datatype="" class="username" xml:lang="">Tyler Durden</a></span>
<span property="schema:dateCreated" content="2025-05-16T01:20:00+00:00" class="field field--name-created field--type-created field--label-hidden">Thu, 05/15/2025 - 21:20</span>


Title: New York Tops London As World's Leading Financial Center In 2025
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">New York Tops London As World's Leading Financial Center In 2025</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p>Financial centers are a core pillar of the modern economy, channeling capital, facilitating trade, and driving innovation across the world.</p>

<p>In this graphic, <a href="https://www.visualcapitalist.com/mapped-the-worlds-top-financial-centers-in-2025/">Visual Capitalist's Marcus Lu visualized</a> the world’s top 40 most competitive financial centers, using data from the 37th edition of the <a href="https://www.longfinance.net/publications/long-finance-reports/the-global-financial-centres-index-37/">Global Financial Centres Index (GFCI 37)</a>.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/Global-Financial-Centres-Index_S.jpg?itok=ET-mGm7q" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/Global-Financial-Centres-Index_S.jpg?itok=ET-mGm7q"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="51ec55a3-5a30-4e27-aac8-447d1f97add6" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="510" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/Global-Financial-Centres-Index_S.jpg?itok=ET-mGm7q" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<h2>Data & Methodology</h2>

<p>The GFCI 37 was compiled using 140 quantitative measures from sources like the World Bank, OECD, and UN.</p>

<p>These measures are combined with assessments collected by respondents to the GFCI online questionnaire. In total, the GFCI 37 used 31,314 assessments from 4,946 respondents.</p>

<p>The data we used to create this graphic is listed below.</p>

			<td class="column-3">712</td>
		</tr></tbody></table><h2>Areas of Competitiveness</h2>

<p>The quantitative factors used in the GFCI model are grouped into five areas of competitiveness:</p>

<ul><li>
	<p><strong>Business environment:</strong> Transparency and stability of systems, regulatory complexity</p>
	</li>
	<li>
	<p><strong>Human capital: </strong>Access to skill professionals, investment in education</p>
	</li>
	<li>
	<p><strong>Infrastructure:</strong> Quality of physical and digital infrastructure</p>
	</li>
	<li>
	<p><strong>Financial sector development: </strong>Accessibility to clients, development of digital solutions</p>
	</li>
	<li>
	<p><strong>Reputation:</strong> Trustworthiness of legal and regulatory systems</p>
	</li>
</ul><h2>Regional Insights</h2>

<p>We’ve summarized the main highlights from each GFCI region below.</p>

<h4>North America</h4>

<p>North America has four centers in the top 10: <a href="https://www.visualcapitalist.com/us-cities-by-gdp-map/">New York</a>, San Francisco, Chicago, and Los Angeles. The most improved within North America are Miami and Vancouver, which both climbed over 10 places in the ranking.</p>

<h4>Western Europe</h4>

<p>London is the region’s dominant center, with seven other cities featuring in the top 20. The average rating across Western Europe increased by 2.14%.</p>

<h4>Asia Pacific</h4>

<p>Asia Pacific has six centers in the top 20, with four belonging to China (Hong Kong SAR, Shanghai, Shenzhen, Beijing). Looking elsewhere, Hangzhou, New Delhi, Kuala Lumpur, Ho Chi Minh City, and Manila all rose six or more places.</p>

<h4>Middle East & Africa</h4>

<p>The region’s leading centers are Dubai and Abu Dhabi, with Dubai climbing four places to 12th in GFCI 37. Meanwhile, Tel Aviv, Kuwait City, and Johannesburg each fell more than 10 places.</p>

<h4>Latin America & The Caribbean</h4>

<p>São Paulo rose seven places this year, making it the leading financial center in the region.</p>

Title: Buffett Liquidated Citigroup, Dumped Financial Stocks As US Entered Trade War : Full 13F Breakdown
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Buffett Liquidated Citigroup, Dumped Financial Stocks As US Entered Trade War : Full 13F Breakdown</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p>Warren Buffett already stunned the Berkshire faithful with his "shocking" announcement last weekend that the 94 year old billionaire was, <em>gasp, </em>finally retiring as CEO of the $1 trillion+ conglomerate. Luckily, there were no surprises in Buffett's <a href="https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1067983/000095012325005701/xslForm13F_X02/form13fInfoTable.xml">latest 13F filing </a>published at the close today: while Buffett did not add any new positions in the quarter that preceded Trump’s trade war, he did liquidate two of his previous large holdings, and continued to trim positions in financial stocks while adding to a handful others.</p>

<p>Buffett started off the last year of his tenure as CEO of Berkshire by exiting his once-huge position in Citigroup, while also shrinking his holdings in Capital One Financial and continuing to trim his longtime stake in Bank of America.</p>

<p>While it is still a top 5 position valued at $26.4 billion at the end of Q1, Buffett started selling his BofA stake in July last year, without providing any explanation for the move. He now owns 8.3% of the US lender and is no longer its biggest shareholder, according to data compiled by Bloomberg. </p>

<p>Berkshire also fully liquidated its stake in Brazil’s Nubank, which has grown into one of the world’s biggest digital banks since its 2013 founding. Berkshire bought a $500 million stake before the bank went public in 2021. The stock has gained 46% since. </p>

<p>On the plus side, Buffett added to his stake in Constellation Brands, which now totals 6.6%, or $2.2 billion; he opened the new position in the alcohol distributor in the last quarter of 2024. He also bought more Sirius XM Holdings and Occidental Petroleum, where he is by far the largest holder with 27% of the shares outstanding. In addition, the company requested confidentiality treatment from the Securities and Exchange Commission, meaning Berkshire was allowed to omit one of more holdings in its filing Thursday.</p>

<p>After aggressively selling down his stake in Apple for much of 2023 and 2024, his AAPL shares were untouched in Q1 and still represents the billionaire’s portfolio’s most valuable holding.</p>

<p>Here is a full breakdown of what Berkshire did in Q1. It added to position in:</p>

<ul><li>Occidental Petroleum, +763,017 million shares to 264.9 million shares, or $13.1 billion as of March 31</li>
	<li>Verisign, +18.423 shares to 13.3 million shares or $3.4 billion</li>
	<li>SiriusXM, +2.3 million shares to 119.8 million shares, or $2.7 billion</li>
	<li>Constellation Brands, +6.4 million shares to 12.009 million, or $2.2 billion</li>
	<li>Dominos Pizza, +238,613 shares to 2.6 million shares, or $1.2 billion</li>
	<li>Pool Corp, +865,311 shares to 1.5 million shares, or $466 million</li>
	<li>Heico Corp, +112,401 shares to 1.2 million shares, or $245.2 million</li>
</ul><p>It reduced its positions in:</p>

<ul><li>Bank of America, by 48.7 million shares to 631.6 million shares, or $26.4 billion as of March 31</li>
	<li>Davita, by 953,091 shares to 35.1 million shares, or $5.4 billion</li>
	<li>Liberty Media, by 3.3 million shares to 19.4 million shares or $1.4 billion</li>
	<li>Capital One, by 300K shares to 7.150 million shares, or $1.3 billion</li>
	<li>T-Mobile, by 469K shares to 3.9 million shares, or $1.0 billion</li>
	<li>Charter Communications, by 7500 shares to 1.98 million shares, or $731 million</li>
</ul><p>Buffett largely refrained from making large acquisitions in recent years, instead building a cash pile that reached nearly $350 billion by the end of March. At the conglomerate’s annual meeting this month, the billionaire said the recent market downturn was “really nothing,” pointing to times in Berkshire’s history when his company’s stock lost half of its value in short spans.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/berkshire%20cash%20q1%202025_0.jpg?itok=NiIwkRuX" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/berkshire%20cash%20q1%202025_0.jpg?itok=NiIwkRuX"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="0be68987-2f51-41ba-a441-e12696f05e66" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="301" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/berkshire%20cash%20q1%202025_0.jpg?itok=NiIwkRuX" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>As we <a href="https://www.zerohedge.com/economics/buffett-step-down-berkshire-ceo-year-end-cash-hoard-hits-record-348-billion">reported at the start of May</a>, Buffett will step down as chairman at year-end. He built Berkshire into a business valued at more than $1.1 trillion, with individuals as well as professionals closely watching and sometimes imitating his investment moves.</p>

<p>Shares of Omaha, Nebraska-based Berkshire have gained more than 11% so far this year. The S&P 500 Index has risen less than 1% during the same period.</p>

<p>A full breakdown of Berkshire's holdings is below.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/Berkshire%2013F%20q1%202025.jpg?itok=Vff6Zb2I" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/Berkshire%2013F%20q1%202025.jpg?itok=Vff6Zb2I"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="be0bb753-0320-4145-9bed-80bee739e02b" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="541" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/Berkshire%2013F%20q1%202025.jpg?itok=Vff6Zb2I" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

      <span rel="schema:author" class="field field--name-uid field--type-entity-reference field--label-hidden"><a title="View user profile." href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" lang="" about="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" typeof="schema:Person" property="schema:name" datatype="" class="username" xml:lang="">Tyler Durden</a></span>

Title: Colorado Could Be The Parental Rights Canary In The Coal Mine
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Colorado Could Be The Parental Rights Canary In The Coal Mine</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><em><a href="https://realclearwire.com/articles/2025/05/12/colorado_could_be_the_parental_rights_canary_in_the_coal_mine_1109615.html">Authored by J.P. De Gance via RealClearReligion</a>,</em></p>

<p dir="ltr"><strong>Some may look at the pending Colorado legislation destroying parental rights and wrongly see the last gasps of a dying woke regime.   </strong></p>

<p dir="ltr"><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/686651_jpg_92.jpg?itok=dhQfbwNI" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/686651_jpg_92.jpg?itok=dhQfbwNI"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="359eb5b6-d1f0-4cb6-839a-30b1f3812d43" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="375" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/686651_jpg_92.jpg?itok=dhQfbwNI" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p dir="ltr">The dystopian state house bill, HB 25-1312 or better known as the “Kelly Loving Act,” <strong>allows the Colorado government to remove a child from her parents if parents refuse to go along with her gender dysphoria and self-styled new identity</strong>. It represents the most totalitarian legal destruction of parental rights in American history. </p>

<p dir="ltr">The bill passed the Colorado House and Senate. To understand why this destructive legislation might become Colorado law, we need to look closer at the cultural understructure. </p>

<p dir="ltr"><strong>The most politically powerful defenders of children are married, biological parents. </strong>In 1970, married households with kids under age 18 made up 40 percent of all American households. Today, that number stands at just 17.8 percent of all households. </p>

<p dir="ltr">Colorado sits on the front edge of the demographic cliff with <a href="https://denverite.com/2024/11/07/denver-school-closures-dps-consolidation-proposal-2024/">K-12 schools already starting to shutter</a>. According to the US Census, married households with kids in the state are just 81 percent of the national average at 14.4 percent of all households.   </p>

<p dir="ltr">So, this evil legislation makes some political sense. The less married parents with kids in any electorate district, the more vulnerable parents and kids are to the onslaught of state power. </p>

<p dir="ltr">And given current trends in marriage and fertility rates – our future politics may look a lot more like Colorado’s politics than anyone realizes. This legal threat to parental rights will spread. </p>

<p dir="ltr">Here’s what we know both from the data and common sense.  </p>

<p dir="ltr"><strong>A man not married to the mother of his child is less present in the day-to-day life of his child. </strong>Nearly all unmarried dads are nonresident dads who see their child less than once a week within two years of becoming a nonresident dad. A large portion of these men see their child only monthly or even less. <strong>These children don’t just lack the vital day-to-day influence that only a loving, present father can provide, they lose a powerful advocate and protector – particularly in politics.   </strong></p>

<p dir="ltr">Assuming she hasn’t been captured by gender ideology herself, the financially struggling single mom often becomes a patronage client of the same legislator who is now taking away her parental rights. </p>

<p dir="ltr">It’s a textbook example of divide and conquer.  </p>

<p dir="ltr">Here’s the reality.<strong> Marriage and fertility – either in its vibrance or absence – is a powerful political force in our nation’s politics. It often goes unnoticed by the politically conscious.  </strong></p>

<p dir="ltr">Seeing fertility collapse in Roman antiquity, Octavian focused part of his rule on policy to boost fertility. He failed and Rome struggled to form native-born armies eventually falling to the Barbarians.  </p>

<p dir="ltr">The strength of early Rome’s family and fertility only rebounded through the evangelism of Christian missionaries and the revolutionary power of the Gospel’s teaching on marriage, which produced the greatness of the West. Reproducing such a revival is vital. </p>

<p dir="ltr">Today, many parents and most church leaders are unaware of the hellscape and nihilism facing young people in sex and relationships.  </p>

<p dir="ltr"><strong>A recent study by Date Psychology found that nearly half of young men have never asked a woman out.   </strong></p>

<p dir="ltr"><a href="https://ifstudies.org/blog/what-happens-when-children-are-exposed-to-pornography">The average age of first porn use in the United States is now 12</a>. <a href="https://www.tandfonline.com/doi/full/10.1080/0092623X.2021.1985025?casa_token=pcnT3z3Ifc4AAAAA%3AbELDPJ4ZABh7lVa87gP0x9cfIQk6Fo3rtgxR4DMjIaVItD3FcRXmDS7Hp1UAdtCRGZ_AH2WzSpG1">Choking in consensual sex has become terrifyingly common</a> as porn becomes ubiquitous. The average age of first marriage for women is now far past peek fertility and moves ever closer to the age of the geriatric pregnancy. </p>

<p dir="ltr">Many who lament the current state of play choose to focus all the attention on bashing men – as if society got here merely because of one sex. </p>

<p dir="ltr">Our economy devasted the jobs where men inherently thrived. K-12 pedagogy became hyper feminized causing boys to conclude school was for girls resulting in women now outnumbering men in college admissions by a 50 percent margin.  </p>

<p dir="ltr">Popular media portrays women heroes as unconquerable while fathers are often portrayed as doofuses. Family law continues to skew against husbands.  </p>

<p dir="ltr"><strong>This is all to say there are plenty of contributing factors to our situation. But, what’s the solution?  </strong></p>

<p dir="ltr">Unless one embraces a life of Pauline celibacy, we ought to first recognize the obvious: men and women need one another. We were made for each other, and this reality is designed into our very bodies.   </p>

<p dir="ltr">Adversarial approaches are unhelpful.  </p>

<p dir="ltr"><strong>Equal in dignity, men and women both deserve to be treated as an end in and of themselves and not treated as a means.   </strong></p>

<p dir="ltr">We each must learn to live the radical biblical call of “being subject to one another out of reverence for Christ.” The paradox of Christian marriage is that a life of sacrificial love lived for the other is where health and happiness most reliably flow. </p>

<p dir="ltr">So, an effective, long-term response to legislation like what is making its way into Colorado law, requires us to defend children by getting practical and tactical about renewing healthy marriage at the retail level. </p>

<p dir="ltr"><strong>For churches, this means altering their ministry to proclaim the timeless truths of the Gospel into this moment.  </strong></p>

<p dir="ltr">In all, 85 percent of American churches invest nothing, zero budget dollars, on marriage and relationship ministry. Instead, the local church should be a life-giving oasis providing the civilizational cure.  </p>

<p dir="ltr">Young people need to find within the church an “in real life” community where they can meet a partner outside of either the consumerism of dating apps or the didactics of a Bible study.  While living in a community of believers, they ought to also learn how to prioritize, date and discern a marriageable partner. They ought to hear about why the erectile dysfunction ads constantly run during live sports and be challenged to avoid the poison of pornography.  </p>

<p dir="ltr">The social science supporting marriage is overwhelmingly positive. Married people with children who attend church are among the happiest and healthiest in America. Contrary to popular media accounts, married church goers even report having sex more frequently than their secular peers.  </p>

<p dir="ltr"><strong>The church must embrace becoming the counterculture in a deeply practical way.</strong></p>

<p dir="ltr">Effective political activism is vital to confront immediate threats.</p>

<p dir="ltr">But, increasing healthy marriages in the culture is necessary. It is the only path to defeating the radicals’ assault on children and parental rights. Otherwise, Colorado’s legislation will one day become national legislation. </p>
</div>

Title: As India-Pak Tensions 'Ease', These Are The Countries Holding The World's Nuclear Arsenal
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">As India-Pak Tensions 'Ease', These Are The Countries Holding The World's Nuclear Arsenal</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><strong>India and Pakistan, currently experiencing a ceasefire </strong>after clashes along their disputed border, have caught global attention as the two neighbors are both armed with nuclear weapons. </p>

<p>According to <a href="https://www.sipri.org/media/press-release/2024/role-nuclear-weapons-grows-geopolitical-relations-deteriorate-new-sipri-yearbook-out-now">data</a> from the Stockholm International Peace Research Institute (SIPRI), <strong>each nation owns around 170 nuclear warheads.</strong></p>

<p><a href="https://www.statista.com/chart/8301/the-countries-holding-the-worlds-nuclear-arsenal/">As Statista's Anna Fleck shows in the following chart,</a> India has added 8 nuclear warheads to its arsenal since January 2023, increasing from 164 warheads to 172. North Korea and China also expanded their arsenals in this time period, bringing their total figures to an estimated 50 warheads and 500 warheads, respectively.</p>

<p><a href="https://www.statista.com/chart/8301/the-countries-holding-the-worlds-nuclear-arsenal/" title="Infographic: The Countries Holding The World's Nuclear Arsenal | Statista"><img alt="Infographic: The Countries Holding The World's Nuclear Arsenal | Statista" height="502" src="https://cdn.statcdn.com/Infographic/images/normal/8301.jpeg" style="max-width: 960px;" width="502" /></a> </p>

<p><em>You will find more infographics at <a href="https://www.statista.com/chartoftheday/">Statista</a></em></p>

<p><strong>Currently, there are estimated to be 9,585 <a href="https://www.statista.com/topics/4269/nuclear-weapons/">nuclear warheads</a> in military stockpiles for potential use across nine countries, with Russia and the U.S. accounting for 8,088 of these. </strong></p>

<p>There are also an estimated 2,536 retired warheads that are yet to be dismantled.</p>

<p>The<strong> two European nuclear powers, France and the UK, together have 515 operational nuclear warheads</strong>. </p>

<p>With the exception of North Korea, <a href="https://de.statista.com/infografik/32030/anzahl-der-weltweit-durchgefuehrten-atomwaffentests/">none of the nations in possession of nuclear warheads have tested them since the 1990s</a>.</p>
</div>

<h2>Runs in the family...</h2>

<p>As covered previously in a ZeroHedge <a href="https://www.zerohedge.com/political/epstein-diddy-spotlight-shines-james-comeys-prosecutor-daughter">piece</a> titled "From Epstein To Diddy: Spotlight Shines On James Comey's Prosecutor Daughter", Comey's offspring smell a little swampy as well. From the piece:</p>

<blockquote>
<p>In a thinly covered news story from <a href="https://www.billboard.com/business/legal/maurene-ryan-comey-ghislaine-maxwell-lead-prosecutor-joins-diddy-trial-1235843958/">December</a> that's suddenly relevant again (read on), New York Prosecutor <strong>Maurene Comey </strong>-<strong> </strong>whose father <strong>James Comey</strong> famously refused to prosecute Hillary Clinton for mishandling classified information & then participated in the Russia collusion hoax - joined the prosecution against Combs. The younger Comey has previously worked as lead prosecutor on both the <strong>Jeffrey Epstein and Ghislaine Maxwell cases</strong>, <strong>as well as that of former Epstein cellmate Nicholas Tartaglione.</strong></p>

<p>...</p>

<p>Maurene Comey becamse a US attorney in the Southern District of New York in 2015.</p>

<p>In 2019, when she was just 30-years-old, <strong>Comey became one of the lead prosecutors in the Jeffrey Epstein case</strong> before he was found dead in his jail cell in August 2019.</p>

<p><strong>Two years later, she became one of three <a href="https://www.businessinsider.com/maurene-comey-james-comey-daughter-leading-jeffrey-epstein-case-2019-7">lead prosecutors</a> in the trial of Ghislaine Maxwell</strong>, Epstein's partner in crime and daughter of suspected Mossad operative <a href="https://x.com/basedspinach/status/1895205597718683709">Robert Maxwell</a>. </p>

<p>Before becoming a US attorney, Comey clerked for US District Court chief judge Loretta Preska of the SDNY - who notably oversaw a long-running <a href="https://www.businessinsider.com/virginia-giuffre-lawsuit-led-to-criminal-case-ghislaine-maxwell-epstein-2021-11">defamation case</a> filed by<strong> Epstein victim Virginia Giuffre against Maxwell.</strong></p>

<p><strong>Comey was also involved in the case of</strong> <strong>Nicholas Tartaglione,</strong> a former NYPD officer who was convicted of killing four men in 2016, and who was briefly <strong>Epstein's cellmate</strong> in the Manhattan Metro Correctional Center. Tartaglione claims to have <a href="https://www.nydailynews.com/2019/07/26/jeffrey-epsteins-ex-cop-cellmate-says-he-saved-multimillionaire-sex-offender-from-hanging-source/">helped Epstein</a> after 'finding him unconscious' (and totally not trying to kill him) prior to Epstein's actual death.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/inline-images/230407131213-nicholas-tartaglione.jpg?itok=2iudzxPs" data-link-option="0" href="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/inline-images/230407131213-nicholas-tartaglione.jpg?itok=2iudzxPs"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="833a1ef4-aa89-4fa7-9507-10e94404fc12" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="281" typeof="foaf:Image" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/230407131213-nicholas-tartaglione.jpg?itok=2iudzxPs" alt="" /></picture></a></p>

<p>Two days after Epstein's death, <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/08/12/business/jeffrey-epstein-interview.html#"><em>NY Times</em></a> reporter James B Stewart, who had spent 90 minutes with Epstein a year prior, wrote "The overriding impression I took away from our roughly 90-minute conversation was that <strong>Mr. Epstein knew an astonishing number of rich, famous and powerful people, and had photos to prove it.</strong> He also claimed to know a great deal about these people, <strong>some of it potentially damaging or embarrassing,</strong> including details about their supposed sexual proclivities and recreational drug use.</p>

<p>And so, whether this is just a case of 'it's a small world' or something a little (or a lot) less innocent, <strong>James Comey's daughter is now involved in a second case where high-profile celebrities and politicians may have been secretly filmed engaging in sexual activity with minors.</strong></p>

Title: Montana Becomes Latest State To Ban Lab-Grown Meat 
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Montana Becomes Latest State To Ban Lab-Grown Meat </span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p>On Tuesday, Montana State Governor Greg Gianforte <u><a href="https://news.mt.gov/Governors-Office/Governor_Gianforte_Bans_Lab-Grown_Meat_in_Montana">announced</a></u> that he had <strong>signed a bill into law banning the manufacturing and sale of lab-grown meat</strong>. </p>

<p>"So-called "lab-grown meat" has no place in Montana," Gov. Gianforte wrote on X, adding, "By signing HB 401 into law, <strong>I am proud to defend our way of life and the hardworking Montana ranchers</strong> who produce the best beef in the world."</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">So-called "lab-grown meat" has no place in Montana.<br /><br />
By signing HB 401 into law, I am proud to defend our way of life and the hardworking Montana ranchers who produce the best beef in the world. <a href="https://t.co/INc2WuAvNI">pic.twitter.com/INc2WuAvNI</a></p>
— Governor Greg Gianforte (@GovGianforte) <a href="https://twitter.com/GovGianforte/status/1922359665041564153?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 13, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p><strong>Montana is now the fifth state in the nation</strong> to pass legislation prohibiting lab-cultivated proteins. The push comes after concurrent Biden-era policies that simultaneously created a loophole for safety testing while prioritizing lab-cultivated proteins as "Climate-Friendly" ahead of labeling requirements. </p>

<p>Not exactly a drug, but not necessarily food harvested in nature, in 2019, Congress directed the Food and Drug Administration (FDA) and the United States Department of Agriculture (USDA) to establish a formal agreement delineating each agency's responsibilities for regulating lab-made or "cellular-cultivated" meat.</p>

<p>By early 2021, the Biden administration prioritized lab-made meat products as a "Climate-Smart" Agricultural alternative, promising a fast track to manufacturers Good Meat Inc and the <u><a href="https://finance.yahoo.com/news/bill-gates-backed-lab-grown-195311408.html">Bill Gates-backed Upside Foods.</a></u></p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/E2HT0P1XIAMocuN.jpg?itok=gsrHRJbs" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/E2HT0P1XIAMocuN.jpg?itok=gsrHRJbs"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="455bd431-dcbc-44a3-b70b-de63b426297c" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="500" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/E2HT0P1XIAMocuN.jpg?itok=gsrHRJbs" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p><u><a href="https://www.fda.gov/media/163260/download?attachment">By 2023, the FDA had issued a "No Questions Asked"</a></u> approval for lab-cultivated "chicken cells with characteristics of fibroblasts." </p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-15_15-15-56.png?itok=W9pCtfzO" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-15_15-15-56.png?itok=W9pCtfzO"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="c4dfceac-0b74-4611-a432-a866e83e9aa0" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="281" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/2025-05-15_15-15-56.png?itok=W9pCtfzO" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>While the USDA does not regulate processed food, <u><a href="https://www.fda.gov/food/human-food-made-cultured-animal-cells/formal-agreement-between-fda-and-usda-regarding-oversight-human-food-produced-using-animal-cell">the agreement stipulated</a></u> that the USDA's Food Safety Inspection Service (FSIS) would be handed off regulatory oversight "at the point of harvest." </p>

<p>Bureaucratic translation: The USDA's regulatory role would be limited to "labeling and sanitation." </p>

<p>While sanitation seems fairly straightforward, it's the labeling requirement - which has yet to materialize - that has state lawmakers pumping the brakes.</p>

<p><u><a href="https://www.federalregister.gov/documents/2020/10/07/2020-22140/labeling-of-foods-comprised-of-or-containing-cultured-seafood-cells-request-for-information">Since early 2020, FSIS</a></u> has gone round-after-round with "stakeholders" about what to call this petri-dish creation. <u><a href="https://www.federalregister.gov/documents/2021/09/03/2021-19057/labeling-of-meat-or-poultry-products-comprised-of-or-containing-cultured-animal-cells">During the last round</a></u> of "name the thingamajig" stakeholders warned the FSIS that transparent labeling would "hamper innovation," and "violate the First Amendment."</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-15_15-16-26.png?itok=udQUgrJ6" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-15_15-16-26.png?itok=udQUgrJ6"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="3ed7ab34-6ff6-4dcf-bfb6-df39cd8daf05" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="440" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/2025-05-15_15-16-26.png?itok=udQUgrJ6" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>To-date, the USDA has not fulfilled its regulatory role, according to the delineated agreement. To be fair, the FDA didn't exactly uphold its end of the bargain either with fast-tracked "No Questions" approvals. </p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">Some employees are comparing the lab-grown meat startup, Upside Foods, to Theranos.<br /><br />
“Are we the next Theranos?” asks one former employee. "People are being lied to, but no one is going to die. Ideally.”<br /><br />
"Batches of meat growing in the custom-made bioreactors would frequently… <a href="https://t.co/2kMhz7ZOju">pic.twitter.com/2kMhz7ZOju</a></p>
— Meat Head (@markeatsmeat) <a href="https://twitter.com/markeatsmeat/status/1707074860235538856?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">September 27, 2023</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>Even as whistleblowers were equating lab-made meats to the next Theranos, the <strong>"Big 4" meat packers <u><a href="https://www.agriculturedive.com/news/jbs-begins-work-on-lab-grown-meat-center-in-brazil/694616/">began rapidly investing billions</a></u> to replace ranchers with biotech</strong>.</p>

<p>With the FDA's blessing and zero red tape requiring transparent labeling, companies like JBS, Tyson, and Cargill have quickly begun producing lab-grown beef, cultured chicken, pork, fish, sausages, burgers, meatballs, and other prepared foods.</p>

<p>While some argue that state-level bans harm the free market, local lawmakers see them as part of a larger fight to <strong>preserve Western values</strong>.</p>

<p>"<strong>Agriculture is our state's number one industry, and this bill takes a clear stand to protect our ranchers and our food supply</strong>," Montana State Rep. Braxton Mitchell said. "<strong>We won't let synthetic products with misleading labels undercut the hard work of Montana's farm and ranch families."</strong></p>

<p>*   *   * </p>

<p>We've launched a "Rancher-Direct" e-commerce platform to secure access to clean, American-raised beef sourced from independent ranchers across the country.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="https://store.zerohedge.com/rancher-direct-clean-food/?utm_source=zerohedge.com&utm_medium=article&utm_campaign=store_promo" data-image-href="https://store.zerohedge.com/rancher-direct-clean-food/?utm_source=zerohedge.com&utm_medium=article&utm_campaign=store_promo" data-link-option="2" href="https://store.zerohedge.com/rancher-direct-clean-food/?utm_source=zerohedge.com&utm_medium=article&utm_campaign=store_promo"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="480511d1-6f73-442d-b106-d07fcf378df6" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="186" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/AD3_4.jpg?itok=F2w3lNf1" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>Eat real food. Very simple.</p>

Title: 'Biggest Self-Own In The History Of The Internet': Hillary Clinton Tries To Get Cute Over Qatar
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">'Biggest Self-Own In The History Of The Internet': Hillary Clinton Tries To Get Cute Over Qatar</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><em><a href="https://modernity.news/2025/05/15/hillary-clinton-steps-in-her-own-st-again/?utm_source=feedly&utm_medium=rss&utm_campaign=hillary-clinton-steps-in-her-own-st-again">Authored by Steve Watson via modernity.news</a>,</em></p>

<p>Hillary Clinton can’t help herself when it comes to President Trump, posting on X Wednesday “No one gives someone a $400 million jet for free without expecting anything in return. Be serious,” in reference to Trump’s acceptance of a luxury Boeing 747 from Qatar’s royal family.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/Hillary_jpg_92.jpg?itok=2VOHw1sE" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/Hillary_jpg_92.jpg?itok=2VOHw1sE"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="fd606e96-8ee7-4085-a7ab-3fa426190fff" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="281" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/Hillary_jpg_92.jpg?itok=2VOHw1sE" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>Everyone quickly pointed out the hypocrisy, given the Clinton Foundation’s history of accepting substantial donations from Arab states, including Qatar, during her tenure as Secretary of State.</p>

<p>The Clinton Foundation has received over $40 million from Arab countries like Saudi Arabia and the UAE, and even accepted a $1 million gift from Qatar in 2011 without informing the State Department, despite Clinton’s agreement to disclose such contributions for review.</p>
