Title: Lethal Lidar: Volvo SUV's Infrared Beam Fries Smartphone Camera
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Lethal Lidar: Volvo SUV's Infrared Beam Fries Smartphone Camera</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p>High-powered lidar systems—commonly used in autonomous and semi-autonomous vehicles—emit infrared laser beams to map their environments. While invisible to the human eye, these beams can damage smartphone camera sensors, as one Reddit user recently discovered the hard way. </p>

<p>Reddit user <em><a href="https://www.reddit.com/r/Volvo/comments/1ke98nv/never_film_the_new_ex90_because_you_will_break/?utm_source=embedv2&utm_medium=post_embed&utm_content=whitespace&embed_host_url=https://www.thedrive.com/news/volvo-ex90s-lidar-sensor-will-fry-your-phones-camera">Jeguetelli</a></em> recently shared a video on the <em>r/Volvo</em> subreddit showing a smartphone camera's image sensor being fried after filming the front-mounted lidar sensor on the Volvo EX90—a fully electric, seven-seat luxury SUV that serves as Volvo's flagship entry into the electric vehicle market.</p>

<p>"<strong>Never film the new Ex90 because you will break your cell camera.Lidar lasers burn your camera</strong>," Jeguetelli wrote. </p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-15_14-29-33.png?itok=a8aCAxWN" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-15_14-29-33.png?itok=a8aCAxWN"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="a360209b-63a0-446f-8a4a-ce1ec490fd33" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="303" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/2025-05-15_14-29-33.png?itok=a8aCAxWN" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>Auto blog <em><a href="https://www.thedrive.com/news/volvo-ex90s-lidar-sensor-will-fry-your-phones-camera">The Drive</a> </em>pointed out, "It should be said that the risk here is inherent to lidar technology, and has nothing to do with Volvo's specific implementation on the EX90. In fact, earlier this year, the automaker even issued a warning against directing external cameras at the vehicle's lidar pod for the very reasons discussed."</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">Filming this car's lidar system breaks the phone camera<a href="https://t.co/99rfffYS1l">pic.twitter.com/99rfffYS1l</a></p>
— Interesting things (@awkwardgoogle) <a href="https://twitter.com/awkwardgoogle/status/1922758949071139116?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 14, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>Volvo's website states:</p>

<blockquote>
<p><strong><em>Lidar light waves can damage external cameras</em></strong><em>: Do not point a camera directly at the lidar. The lidar, being a laser based system, uses infrared light waves that may cause damage to certain camera devices. This can include smartphones or phones equipped with a camera.</em></p>
</blockquote>

<p>"<strong>Would this damage your car's backup camera, if a LIDAR equipped car tailgates you?</strong>" one Redditor asked. </p>

<p>Another person said, "<strong>Thank god for Apple Care." </strong></p>

<p>The ongoing debate in the tech world centers on LiDAR vs. cameras—a big divide in the race toward fully autonomous vehicles, especially when comparing Tesla's camera-only approach to rivals embracing LiDAR.</p>

<p><strong>Elon Musk famously called LiDAR a "crutch,"</strong> arguing that camera vision powered by advanced AI is sufficient for FSD.</p>

<p>"In my view, it's a crutch that will drive companies to a local maximum that they will find very hard to get out of." Musk said several years ago, adding, "Perhaps I am wrong, and I will look like a fool. But I am quite certain that I am not."</p>

<p>The Counterargument: Tesla's competitors argue that LiDAR provides critical redundancy and reliability, especially for safety-critical applications like robotaxis.</p>

<p>The proliferation of LiDAR sensors on vehicles should come with a public service warning: avoid pointing smartphone cameras at these devices emitting infrared laser beams—they can permanently damage image sensors.</p>

<p>Also, will LiDAR risk burning camera sensors on Tesla vehicles? </p>
</div>
      <span rel="schema:author" class="field field--name-uid field--type-entity-reference field--label-hidden"><a title="View user profile." href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" lang="" about="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" typeof="schema:Person" property="schema:name" datatype="" class="username" xml:lang="">Tyler Durden</a></span>
<span property="schema:dateCreated" content="2025-05-15T21:35:00+00:00" class="field field--name-created field--type-created field--label-hidden">Thu, 05/15/2025 - 17:35</span>


Title: Dem Lawmaker Facing Calls For Expulsion And Arrest After Allegedly Assaulting ICE Agents Outside Detention Center In NJ
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Dem Lawmaker Facing Calls For Expulsion And Arrest After Allegedly Assaulting ICE Agents Outside Detention Center In NJ</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><em><a href="https://amgreatness.com/2025/05/14/dem-lawmaker-facing-calls-for-expulsion-and-arrest-after-allegedly-assaulting-ice-agents-outside-detention-center-in-nj/">Authored by Debra Heine via American Greatness</a>,</em></p>

<p>Homeland Security Secretary Kristi Noem on Tuesday said the<strong> three Democrat lawmakers who scuffled with Immigration and Customs Enforcement (ICE) agents in New Jersey last Friday committed felonies.</strong></p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/demrep.JPG?itok=2n-qR7Vh" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/demrep.JPG?itok=2n-qR7Vh"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="3287d87d-caeb-4fd8-a667-e3c60f8e61a0" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="288" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/demrep.JPG?itok=2n-qR7Vh" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>New Jersey Reps. Bonnie Watson Coleman, Robert Menendez and LaMonica McIver were part of a mob that protested at the Delaney Hall detention center, a privately run facility under contract with ICE that houses non-citizens awaiting immigration proceedings or deportation.</p>

<p><strong>The lefty protesters were demanding that the center be shut down, <a href="https://nypost.com/2025/05/12/us-news/feds-weigh-assault-charges-for-pols-who-protested-nj-ice-center/">the New York Post</a> reported.</strong></p>

<p>Newark Mayor Ras Baraka (D) was arrested Friday afternoon and charged with trespassing after entering the facility and refusing to leave.</p>

<p>An ugly scuffle ensued as the lawmakers surrounded Baraka in an apparent attempt to shield the mayor from the ICE agents making the arrest.</p>

<p>“<strong>Don’t touch us!</strong>” McIver (in red) screamed over and over as officers tried to break through their blockade.</p>

<p>An online video shows the hefty McIver (in red), a member of the House Homeland Security Committee, throwing punches and shoving law enforcement officers as they tried to regain control.</p>

<p><iframe allow="accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture; web-share" allowfullscreen="" frameborder="0" height="315" referrerpolicy="strict-origin-when-cross-origin" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/IYF0wTbG9Ug?si=kSSmOEi1vbIoiYa0" title="YouTube video player" width="560"></iframe></p>

<p>Watson Coleman said the group of lawmakers had already visited the facility and come out to talk to the mayor when they were the ones allegedly assaulted by ICE agents.</p>

<p>“Since DHS has been lying about this, allow me to correct the record. This scuffle, during which an ICE agent physically shoved me, occurred AFTER we had entered the Delaney Hall premises,” she <a href="https://x.com/RepBonnie/status/1920989902520340582">posted on  X,</a> Friday.</p>

<p>“<strong>We entered the facility, came BACK OUT to speak to the Mayor, and then ICE agents began shoving us. This is not how we entered the facility. We were escorted in by guards, because we have lawful oversight authority to be there</strong>,” she said.</p>

<p>”Tricia McLaughlin, the Department of Homeland Security’s assistant secretary for public affairs, said on CNN Friday that DHS has damning body-cam video of the scuffle that has not yet been released to the public.</p>

<p>“We actually have body camera footage of some of these members of Congress assaulting our ICE enforcement officers, including body slamming a female ICE officer,” McLaughlin said.</p>

<p>“<strong>These members of Congress, this mayor and these protesters are not above the law</strong>,” McLaughlin noted on “Fox & Friends,” Monday.</p>

<p>Noem hinted that more arrests are being considered during an appearance on Fox News, Tuesday night.</p>

<p>“This wasn’t oversight, this was committing felonies. This was going out and attacking people who stand up for the rule of law. And it was absolutely horrible,” Noem told the host Jesse Waters, noting that the acts of violence were committed in defense of violent criminals— rapists, murderers, and members of foreign terrorist organizations victimizing American communities.</p>

<p>“<strong>What are they trying to do? Get these people released back into the country so there can be more Laken Rileys?</strong>” she asked. “I just don’t understand what their point is. They’ve completely lost their minds.”</p>

<p>Noem said it was up to the Department of Justice to decide whether to press charges against the Democrat lawmakers.</p>

<p><iframe allow="accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture; web-share" allowfullscreen="" frameborder="0" height="315" referrerpolicy="strict-origin-when-cross-origin" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/mzGH__XPBM8?si=pFm-7phviNCGKPFb" title="YouTube video player" width="560"></iframe></p>

<p>Rep. Buddy Carter (R-Ga.) introduced a resolution Tuesday to strip the House members of all their committee assignments.</p>

<p><strong>Rep. Marjory Taylor Greene went further Wednesday, saying McIver needs to be expelled.</strong></p>

<p>Greene <a href="https://x.com/RepMTG/status/1922661736718491821">posted a photo on X</a> showing McIver “couldn’t even look up as video played of her assaulting ICE officers” during a Homeland Security hearing Wednesday.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/New-Project-2025-05-14T140619.839_jpg_92.jpg?itok=VzmJCE1z" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/New-Project-2025-05-14T140619.839_jpg_92.jpg?itok=VzmJCE1z"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="0c7c4bd9-9a90-4e59-9a23-ef5e42e5d184" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="348" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/New-Project-2025-05-14T140619.839_jpg_92.jpg?itok=VzmJCE1z" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>“She has zero respect for law enforcement or the rule of law, which is especially disgraceful as we honor law enforcement during Police Week,” the congresswoman added. “This isn’t just grounds for censure or removal from committees. LaMonica McIver should be EXPELLED from Congress.”</p>

<p>During the hearing Wednesday, <strong>Noem again argued that the Democrat lawmakers were not conducting oversight when they fought with ICE agents.</strong></p>

<p>“What happened on May 9 at Delaney Hall was not oversight. It was a political stunt that put the safety of our law enforcement agents, our staff, and our detainees at risk,” she testified.  “This behavior was lawless, and it was beneath this body. Members of Congress are not above the law and cannot illegally break into detention facilities.”</p>

<p><iframe allow="accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture; web-share" allowfullscreen="" frameborder="0" height="315" referrerpolicy="strict-origin-when-cross-origin" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/nzF8w1F4vbs?si=bj9EPGD3otnweEa6" title="YouTube video player" width="560"></iframe></p>

<p>Rep. Alexandria Ocasio-Cortez (D-N.Y.), meanwhile,  criticized the Trump administration over their handling of the incident, <a href="https://thehill.com/homenews/administration/5299452-homeland-security-secretary-accuses-democrats-felony/">the Hill</a> reported.</p>

<p>“If anyone’s breaking the law in this situation, it’s not members of Congress, it’s the Department of Homeland Security,” she said in an Instagram video posted Sunday.</p>

<p>“<strong>It’s people like Tom Homan and Secretary Kristi Noem</strong>,” she added.</p>

<p>“You lay a finger on someone, on Rep. Bonnie Watson Coleman … or any of the representatives that were there, you lay a finger on them, we are going to have a problem,” Ocasio-Cortez added. “Because the people who are breaking the law are the people not abiding by it.”</p>

<p>Via Getty, the peaceful January 6 protester known as “the Lectern Guy,” shared his own thoughts on the fracas over the weekend.</p>

<p>“<strong>United States Representative LaMonica McIver has still not been arrested after assaulting multiple federal officers on video</strong>,” Getty<a href="https://x.com/lecternleader/status/1921552087202017300"> posted on X</a> Sunday. “Within 48 hours of smiling and waving in the Capitol on J6, I was in county jail isolation under 24-hour supervision, charged with 3 crimes, 2 were lies, the other debatable,” he continued.</p>

<p>“They put me in an ankle monitor and told me I was I was a danger to my community. Meanwhile, this animal is still collecting a paycheck from our tax dollars,” Getty added bitterly.</p>

<p><a href="https://wfin.com/fox-political-news/scoop-gop-plans-investigation-into-ice-threats-after-dems-storming-of-facility/">Fox News reported</a> Wednesday that House Judiciary Chairman Jim Jordan (R-Ohio) is opening an investigation into threats facing ICE facilities in the wake of the attack on Delaney Hall Detention Center.</p>

<blockquote>
<p>Fox News Digital was told that Jordan is expected to schedule a hearing for next Tuesday, with former ICE and Department of Homeland Security (DHS) officials expected among the witness panel.</p>
</blockquote>

<p>Republicans leaders, according to Fox, are still discussing what, if any, consequences could be in store for Reps. Watson Coleman, Menendez and  McIver.</p>
</div>

Title: Putin Removes Commander Of Russia's Ground Forces In Another Defense Shake-Up
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Putin Removes Commander Of Russia's Ground Forces In Another Defense Shake-Up</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p>The longtime commander of Russia's ground forces, Army General Oleg Salyukov, has been relieved of his command by order of President Vladimir Putin on Thursday. </p>

<p>Salyukov has led the Ground Forces as 'commander-in-chief' <strong>since 2014</strong>, making his removal a major decision amid what appears an ongoing shake-up of military leadership.</p>
<a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/landforces.jpg?itok=fFfTmzsJ" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/landforces.jpg?itok=fFfTmzsJ"><picture><figure role="group" class="caption caption-img inline-images image-style-inline-images"><img alt="" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="c6fe3e37-b35d-434a-93ac-ce9643b62cc1" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="358" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/landforces.jpg?itok=fFfTmzsJ" typeof="foaf:Image" width="500" /><figcaption><em>Chief of the Russian Land Forces Oleg Salyukov (far left) attends prior year's Victory Day, in Moscow, on May 9, 2024. Reuters</em></figcaption></figure></picture></a>

<p>He just literally oversaw Moscow's Victory Day parade on May 9, and so his removal was likely a highly unexpected development.</p>

<p>As of yet, the Kremlin has offered no specific reason for the top commander's removal. Russia has continued making gains on the battlefield, particularly near Pokrovsk. But the advance has become <strong>a very slow grind</strong>.</p>

<p>Some the latest gains this week in Donetsk are <a href="https://www.aljazeera.com/features/2025/5/15/russia-grabs-a-bit-more-of-ukraine-as-it-heads-into-peace">as follows</a>:</p>

<blockquote>
<p><em><strong>Russian forces captured the settlement of Kotlyarivka, southwest of the embattled area of Pokrovsk, on Monday</strong>, Russia’s Ministry of Defense said.</em></p>

<p><em>The seizure brought Russian forces to within 3.7km (2.3 miles) of the regional border between Donetsk and Dnipropetrovsk in Ukraine. Russian forces also forced their way into the village of Myrolyubivka, east of Pokrovsk, and claimed to have taken the entire settlement.</em></p>

<p><em>On Wednesday, Russia’s Defense Ministry claimed its forces took the community of Mykhailovka, also in Donetsk.</em></p>
</blockquote>

<p>But it could be that Putin is growing impatient, and wants even greater breakthroughs at a moment peace negotiations mediated by the US are gaining steam. This huge figure points to this:</p>

<blockquote>
<p>RUSSIA DEPLOYS 640,000 TROOPS IN WAR AGAINST UKRAINE: MILITARY</p>
</blockquote>

<p>Meanwhile Salyukov's removal comes after a series of major defense ministry shake-ups which stretch well into 2023, which had also seen Sergei Shoigu removal as Defense Minister (and 'promoted' into a top security council role).</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">The commander of Russia's Ground Forces Army General Oleg Salyukov has left his post and has been appointed deputy secretary of the security council under former defense ministry Sergei Shoigu. Salyukov had been the commander of Russia's Ground Forces since 2014.… <a href="https://t.co/KiE3CFtQEf">pic.twitter.com/KiE3CFtQEf</a></p>
— Rob Lee (@RALee85) <a href="https://twitter.com/RALee85/status/1923066267075813376?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 15, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>According to prior <a href="https://www.ifri.org/en/papers/commanders-putins-long-war-purged-reshuffled-and-disgruntled">analysis</a>:</p>

<blockquote>
<p><em><strong>Putin typically prioritizes loyalty over competence, which makes the command structure incapable of addressing sudden shifts in the combat environment</strong>. The recent profound shake-up of and purges in the Defense Ministry have resulted in a serious bureaucratic disorganization of this structure that is crucial for sustaining the war effort. </em></p>

<p><em>The lack of any changes in the General Staff <strong>weakens the ability to learn from experience and compromises the authority of the high command</strong>. Angst and anger among the fighting generals caused by the ineptness of the high command is a major source of political risk, which Putin can neither ignore nor properly address.</em></p>
</blockquote>

<p>Indeed this analysis remains true, and it's hard to imagine someone with more experience than Salyukov - given that he has commanded the country's ground forces for a decade, including through well over three years of a complex Ukraine battlefield.</p>
</div>
      <span rel="schema:author" class="field field--name-uid field--type-entity-reference field--label-hidden"><a title="View user profile." href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" lang="" about="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" typeof="schema:Person" property="schema:name" datatype="" class="username" xml:lang="">Tyler Durden</a></span>
<span property="schema:dateCreated" content="2025-05-15T20:45:00+00:00" class="field field--name-created field--type-created field--label-hidden">Thu, 05/15/2025 - 16:45</span>


Title: VDH: The Real First 100 Days
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">VDH: The Real First 100 Days</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><a href="https://amgreatness.com/2025/05/15/the-real-first-100-days/"><em>Authored by Victor Davis Hanson via American Greatness,</em></a></p>

<p><strong>Pundits are confused about what to make of the first 100 days of the second Trump administration.</strong></p>

<p>Supporters talk of <strong>“flooding the zone,” </strong>believing Trump is making so many changes so quickly that his opposition is reduced to deer-in-the-headlights infancy.</p>

<p>They must be right when the nation suffers daily Democratic pottymouth videos, vandalism of Teslas, infantile meltdowns at congressional witnesses, rioting against federal agents to protect illegal alien felons, protesting on behalf of women beaters, M-13 gangbangers, human traffickers, and assaulters, and visa-holding violent students praising Hamas terrorists.</p>

<p>In contrast, opponents either claim that Trump’s first three months are either directionless chaos or a Hitlerian nightmare or both.</p>

<p><strong>But what is really happening?</strong></p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-15_11-02-36.jpg?itok=Z8_DB-XT" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-15_11-02-36.jpg?itok=Z8_DB-XT"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="7dcd9197-d30c-4f6a-9094-6cf377e59743" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="276" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/2025-05-15_11-02-36.jpg?itok=Z8_DB-XT" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p><strong><u>One</u>, Trump is finally addressing the problems that proverbially “cannot go on forever, and so they won’t go on.”</strong></p>

<p><em>When, if ever, would the left have closed the southern border? After 10, 30, 50 million illegal aliens?</em></p>

<p><em>How many more criminal illegal entrants was the Biden administration willing to allow into American neighborhoods—500,000? 1 million? 3 million?</em></p>

<p><em>How long was the world simply going to ignore the human destruction on the doorstep of Europe?</em></p>

<p><em>Would Biden or Harris have sought a ceasefire? Or would it have taken another 1.5, 3, or even 5 million more dead, wounded, and missing Ukrainians and Russians?</em></p>

<p>Nor did past administrations ever seek a solution to the massive national debt, much less the uncontrollable budget and trade deficits.</p>

<p><strong>All prior presidents passed the day of judgment on to some vague future presidency, assured that their money printing would at least not blow up on their watch.</strong></p>

<p>All moaned that China was piling up huge trade surpluses while denying its own population the usual modern safety net. They knew Beijing’s aim was to use the trillions of dollars in trade surpluses to build a new massive military, a greater arsenal of nuclear bombs, and a new imperial Belt and Road overseas empire.</p>

<p>Yet no administration did anything but greenlight American outsourcing and offshoring while ignoring Chinese trade cheating and technology theft.</p>

<p>Indeed, prior presidencies appeased and enriched China on the foolish belief that such indulgence would lead to Chinese prosperity, and with such Western-style affluence, soon a globalized, democratic, and supposedly friendly China.</p>

<p>In sum, we just witnessed all at once a 100-day, 360-degree effort to address all the existential challenges that we knew were unsustainable but were either afraid or incompetent to address.</p>

<p><strong><u>Second</u>, the administration apparently wants to confront the source of these crises and believes it is the progressive project.</strong></p>

<p>The left maintains real political power not by grass-roots popularity, but rather by unelected institutional clout. The party of democracy uses anti-democratic means to achieve its ends of perpetual control.</p>

<p>It wages lawfare through the weaponization of the state, local, and federal courts.</p>

<p>It exercises executive power through cherry-picked federal district and circuit judges and their state and local counterparts.</p>

<p>The permanent bureaucracies and huge federal workforce are mostly left-wing, unionized, and weaponized by a progressive apparat. Their supreme directive is to amalgamate legislative, judicial, and executive power into the hands of the unelected Anthony Faucis, Jim Comeys, and Lois Lerners of the world—and thus to override or ignore both popular plebiscites and the work of the elected Congress.</p>

<p>Over ninety percent of the media—legacy, network, social, and state—are left-wing. Their mission is not objectivity but, admittedly, indoctrination.</p>

<p><strong>Academia is the font of the progressive project. Ninety percent of the professoriate are left-wing and activist—explaining why campuses believe they are above the rules and laws of the Constitution, the Supreme Court, and the U.S. Congress.</strong></p>

<p>Add into the mix the blue-chip Accela corridor law firms and the globalized corporate and revolving-door political elite.</p>

<p>The net result is clear: almost everything the vast majority of Americans and their elected representatives did not want—far-left higher education, a Pravda media, biological men destroying women’s sports, an open border, 30 million illegal aliens, massive debt, a weaponized legal system, and a politicized Pentagon—became the new culture of America.</p>

<p><strong>So, Trump is not just confronting unaddressed existential crises but also the root causes of why, when, and how they become inevitable and nearly unsolvable.</strong></p>

<p>His answer is a messy, knock-down-drag-out counterrevolution to reboot the country back to the middle where it once was and where the Founders believed it should remain.</p>

<p><strong>His right and left opponents call such pushback chaotic, disruptive, and out of control.</strong></p>

<p>But the counterrevolution appears disorderly and upsetting, mostly to those who originally birthed the chaos; it certainly does not to the majority of Americans who finally wanted an end to the madness.</p>
</div>
      <span rel="schema:author" class="field field--name-uid field--type-entity-reference field--label-hidden"><a title="View user profile." href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" lang="" about="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" typeof="schema:Person" property="schema:name" datatype="" class="username" xml:lang="">Tyler Durden</a></span>
<span property="schema:dateCreated" content="2025-05-15T20:20:00+00:00" class="field field--name-created field--type-created field--label-hidden">Thu, 05/15/2025 - 16:20</span>


Title: Meta Stumbles: Delays Release Of Flagship "Behemoth" AI Model Over Performance Concerns
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Meta Stumbles: Delays Release Of Flagship "Behemoth" AI Model Over Performance Concerns</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p>A new report from <a href="https://www.wsj.com/tech/ai/meta-is-delaying-the-rollout-of-its-flagship-ai-model-f4b105f7">The Wall Street Journal</a> hit the wires late Thursday during the U.S. cash session, revealing that Meta is reportedly delaying the release of its flagship AI model, "Behemoth," due to internal concerns over its performance and mounting questions about its multibillion-dollar splurge in AI investments.</p>

<p>Initially slated for an April release around Meta's inaugural AI conference (LlamaCon) for developers, Behemoth has been pushed to late in the second half of this year.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/GrA2C7PXYAAhjQb.jpg?itok=GSdUvDba" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/GrA2C7PXYAAhjQb.jpg?itok=GSdUvDba"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="55ce317e-8c04-435c-a182-f6b328624682" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="333" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/GrA2C7PXYAAhjQb.jpg?itok=GSdUvDba" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>The delays come as Meta has publicly claimed that Behemoth outperforms competitors like OpenAI and Google on certain benchmarks. People familiar with the delays say Behemoth has faced "training challenges." </p>

<p>Since Meta's first Llama model was released in early 2023, 11 of the 14 original researchers from the company's Fundamental AI Research Team have left.</p>

<p>Meanwhile, Meta disclosed in its latest <a href="https://www.zerohedge.com/markets/meta-soars-after-blowing-away-estimates-hikes-capex-forecast">earnings report</a> that it had raised its capital expenditure forecast to between $64 billion and $72 billion, up from a previous range of $60 billion to $65 billion—a significant portion of that increase earmarked for AI infrastructure.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/meta%20capex_0.jpg?itok=JdGTPKez" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/meta%20capex_0.jpg?itok=JdGTPKez"><img alt="" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="292" src="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/meta%20capex_0.jpg?itok=JdGTPKez" width="500" /></a></p>

<p>This development mirrors delays at other major AI labs, including OpenAI and Anthropic, suggesting that progress in large language models has slowed. </p>

<p>"<strong>Right now, the progress is quite small across all the labs, all the models</strong>," Ravid Shwartz-Ziv, an assistant professor and faculty fellow at New York University's Center for Data Science, told WSJ.</p>

<p>In markets, Meta shares are down a little more than 2% - coming into resistance after a multi-week 37% run. </p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-15_12-30-56_0.jpg?itok=Nd20D8ws" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-15_12-30-56_0.jpg?itok=Nd20D8ws"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="7efbf940-767f-4931-8395-c673b7acaa41" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="339" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/2025-05-15_12-30-56_0.jpg?itok=Nd20D8ws" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>What could possibly go wrong?</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/GibaLvVWEAA2nQN-1.png?itok=VO-q-8vY" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/GibaLvVWEAA2nQN-1.png?itok=VO-q-8vY"><img alt="" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="331" src="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/GibaLvVWEAA2nQN-1.png?itok=VO-q-8vY" width="500" /></a></p>

      <span rel="schema:author" class="field field--name-uid field--type-entity-reference field--label-hidden"><a title="View user profile." href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" lang="" about="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" typeof="schema:Person" property="schema:name" datatype="" class="username" xml:lang="">Tyler Durden</a></span>
<span property="schema:dateCreated" content="2025-05-15T19:56:23+00:00" class="field field--name-created field--type-created field--label-hidden">Thu, 05/15/2025 - 15:56</span>


Title: DHS Reportedly Requests 20,000 National Guard Troops For "Interior Immigration Enforcement"
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">DHS Reportedly Requests 20,000 National Guard Troops For "Interior Immigration Enforcement"</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p>Democrats had no concern for due process when millions of third-world illegal aliens, including violent criminals and terrorists, invaded the U.S. with help from far-left NGOs. But now, as the Trump administration ramps up mass deportations, suddenly, this same army of left-wing lawmakers is screaming "due process" to delay deportations and clog up the courts. Their legal resistance is seen in federal courts, where remnants of the Biden-Harris regime still cling to power through far-left activist judges hell-bent on obstructing the mandate the American people handed Trump: deport criminal illegal aliens.</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">The Left didn’t care about due process while America was being invaded by illegal aliens, so don’t let them fool you now. Their concern is not due process, their concern is preventing deportations — the final step in the due process for illegal aliens. <a href="https://t.co/CZx5TPInCl">pic.twitter.com/CZx5TPInCl</a></p>
— Heritage Foundation (@Heritage) <a href="https://twitter.com/Heritage/status/1912617453948911625?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">April 16, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>A new report from <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2025/05/15/us/politics/national-guard-immigration.html?smid=tw-share" target="_blank">The New York Times</a>, citing officials with direct knowledge of the plans, says the Department of Homeland Security has requested over 20,000 National Guard troops from the Defense Department to support the president's mass deportation plans for criminal illegal aliens. </p>

<p>If approved, this would mark the first time National Guard members have been used for interior migrant enforcement operations in the U.S.</p>

<p>Here's more from the NYT:</p>

<blockquote>
<p><em>Lawyers at the Pentagon were reviewing the request with "interior immigration enforcement," according to a Defense Department official who spoke on the condition of anonymity to describe internal deliberations. It was unclear what role state National Guard members would play and whether they would be involved in rounding up people for deportation, the official said.</em></p>
</blockquote>

<p>The move only suggests that the Trump administration is preparing to ramp up mass deportations and fulfill the mandate the American voter gave him: restore national security through the deportation of criminal illegal aliens. </p>

<p>Last month, on Truth Social, Trump wrote, "I'm doing what I was elected to do, remove criminals from our Country, but the Courts don't seem to want me to do that," adding, "We cannot give everyone a trial, because to do so would take, without exaggeration, 200 years."</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-15_12-32-46.png?itok=c4wY7pIS" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-15_12-32-46.png?itok=c4wY7pIS"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="1a676a21-9d03-44c4-99fd-2a2bf1a30da5" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="482" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/2025-05-15_12-32-46.png?itok=c4wY7pIS" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>Vice President JD Vance called the battle between the Trump administration and leftist activists federal judges a "fake legal process" that is the "ratification of Biden's illegal migrant invasion."</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">Consider that Joe Biden allowed approximately 20 million illegal aliens into our country. This placed extraordinary burdens on our country--our schools, hospitals, housing, and other essential services were overwhelmed. On top of that, many of these illegal aliens committed…</p>
— JD Vance (@JDVance) <a href="https://twitter.com/JDVance/status/1912320489261027374?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">April 16, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>"The judicial process is for Americans. Immediate deportation is for illegal aliens," Deputy Chief of Staff Stephen Miller recently said.</p>

<p>What we're witnessing in the federal courts from far-left judges amounts to a subversion of the popular mandate—an orchestrated campaign of lawfare that, in effect, could be viewed as a soft coup through the judiciary. When these activist judges repeatedly obstruct or delay lawful executive orders backed by a clear electoral mandate, it's no longer about legal oversight—it's about undermining the will of the people. </p>

Title: Schiff Slams Clueless Fed, Says Powell Is Living In A Kind Of "Baghdad Bob World"
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Schiff Slams Clueless Fed, Says Powell Is Living In A Kind Of "Baghdad Bob World"</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><a href="https://www.schiffgold.com/peters-podcast/peter-schiff-the-fed-admits-it-doesnt-know-anything"><em>Via SchiffGold.com,</em></a></p>

<p>In Wednesday’s episode of The Peter Schiff Show, Peter unpacks <a href="https://www.schiffgold.com/key-gold-news/fed-holds-rates-acknowledges-economic-uncertainty">the Federal Reserve’s recent decision to hold rates steady</a>, dissecting Jerome Powell’s latest press conference for its contradictions and disconnect from the economic realities faced by Americans. He also critiques ongoing trade policy blunders and warns that political posturing could lead the U.S. into a major economic downturn.</p>

<p><iframe allow="accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture; web-share" allowfullscreen="" frameborder="0" height="432" referrerpolicy="strict-origin-when-cross-origin" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/-ZdVq2wG0Wg" title="🔴 Trump's Tariffs Will Make China Great Again - Ep 1025" width="768"></iframe></p>

<p>Peter opens by reflecting on the Fed’s latest move and the market’s reaction, pointing out the <a href="https://www.schiffgold.com/peters-podcast/peter-schiff-dont-trust-the-rebound-yet">gap between Powell’s rhetoric and investors’ response:</a></p>

<blockquote>
<p><em>Well as expected [last week], the federal reserve left interest rates unchanged. The fed funds target remains between 4.25 and 4.5%. You know, <strong>I think this was one of the most hawkish press conferences that I’ve seen Powell participate in. </strong>You wouldn’t really know that by the reaction in the stock market. Stock market kind of, you know, just ignored what Powell said. The bond market did get a boost as you would expect.</em></p>
</blockquote>

<p>Noting the mismatch between <a href="https://www.schiffgold.com/guest-commentaries/cracked-shells-how-supply-shocks-not-monopoly-drive-egg-prices">the Federal Reserve’s statements and actual inflation data,</a> Peter takes issue with Powell’s assertion that inflation expectations remain grounded:</p>

<blockquote>
<p><em>First of all, in the prepared remarks, one of the interesting comments– or more lie than comment– is that Powell said that inflation expectations remain well anchored and the Fed’s job is to make sure they stay that way. <strong>Now, I don’t know what world Powell is living in, you know, kind of like the Baghdad Bob world from the Gulf War because inflation expectations left the 2% anchor a long time ago. </strong>I mean, hasn’t Powell been paying attention to any of the Michigan numbers that have been coming out on inflation expectations that show, I think, one year expectations with a six handle and five year expectations have got at least a four handle? So we’re nowhere near 2%. </em></p>
</blockquote>

<p>Peter is quick to highlight how the Fed’s optimistic portrayal of the economy doesn’t match the underlying risks. He questions how Powell can call the current situation “a great place” <a href="https://www.schiffgold.com/exploring-finance/jobs-last-three-months-saw-downward-revisions-of-57k-on-average">when real economic indicators tell a different story:</a></p>

<blockquote>
<p><em><strong>How is Powell describing the economy as being in a great place? How is he saying that inflation is in a great place? How was he saying that the labor market is in a great place?</strong> It doesn’t sound like a great place to me. I mean, a great place would be that the odds of higher inflation are going down, right, not where the odds are going up… That would be a good place, but when you’re admitting that the odds of higher inflation are going up, that’s pretty far from a great place.</em></p>
</blockquote>

<p>Turning from monetary policy to international trade, Peter addresses the <a href="https://www.schiffgold.com/commentaries/heres-why-tariffs-wont-bring-back-manufacturing">persistent uncertainty around trade negotiations with China.</a> He suggests that China would be wise to reduce its reliance on American consumers, who are increasingly unable to afford the goods they import:</p>

<blockquote>
<p><em>But I don’t have a lot of optimism for these China trade talks. And in fact, what <strong>I think the Chinese may finally be doing is the right thing. They’ve been resisting doing the right thing for a long time because there’s always some short-term pain.</strong> Because the biggest mistake that China made, and I’ve been talking about this for decades now, was hitching its cart to our wagon. They tried to service the US consumer, supply the US consumer with goods, without recognizing that the US consumer was broke and really couldn’t afford to pay for the goods.</em></p>
</blockquote>

<p>Peter concludes with a critique of protectionist policy, using a recent proposal by Donald Trump as a case study in economic misunderstanding. He points out the <a href="https://www.schiffgold.com/commentaries/the-trump-tariffs-why-free-trade-is-the-only-way-forward">self-defeating nature of a proposed 100% tariff</a> on foreign-made films—a move that threatens an industry where the U.S. actually excels internationally:</p>

<blockquote>
<p><em>Probably the most ridiculous thing that the president said this week wasn’t even during that interview. It was on a post on Truth Social out of the blue. Trump posts, ‘I’m going to impose a hundred percent tariff on movies filmed outside the United States.’ A hundred percent tariff, right? First of all, the movie industry, Hollywood motion pictures, that’s one of our industries that we have a trade surplus. <strong>We export a lot more movies than we import. So movies, the motion picture industry, Hollywood entertainment, that is not a problem that Donald Trump needs to fix.</strong></em></p>
</blockquote>

<p>Be sure to check out <a href="https://www.schiffgold.com/interviews/schiff-on-mining-network-gold-up-as-easy-credit-weigh-on-the-dollar">Peter’s other analysis from the Mining Network!</a></p>

<p> </p>
</div>

Title: Trump Touts 1.4 Trillion Investment In AI, Tech From UAE In Final Mideast Stop
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Trump Touts 1.4 Trillion Investment In AI, Tech From UAE In Final Mideast Stop</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p>After the several massive announcements and deals to come out of Trump's visit to Saudi Arabia and Qatar, developments during the last leg of the US President's Gulf tour in United Arab Emirates actually seem a bit humdrum by comparison. </p>

<p>But the visuals and spare no expenses official welcome and ceremonial events have certainly been interesting...</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">⚡️Trump arrives in the UAE<br /><br />
(Don’t ask me what’s happening)<a href="https://t.co/dtUsPwF25W">pic.twitter.com/dtUsPwF25W</a></p>
— War Monitor (@WarMonitors) <a href="https://twitter.com/WarMonitors/status/1923021034866798814?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 15, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>Among the more notable statements has been Trump's <strong>touting a 1.4 trillion</strong>... yes that's <em>trillion</em>... <strong>investment in AI</strong> and other tech sectors from the Emirates.</p>

<p>The White House had previewed this longtime in the works deal as related to<strong> artificial intelligence infrastructure, semiconductors, energy and manufacturing</strong>.</p>

<p>Further, Emirates Global Aluminum will "invest in the first new aluminium smelter in the United States in 35 years, which would nearly double US domestic aluminium production."</p>
<a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/inline-images/trumpuae.jpg?itok=KAlh7mmz" data-link-option="0" href="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/inline-images/trumpuae.jpg?itok=KAlh7mmz"><picture><figure role="group" class="caption caption-img inline-images image-style-inline-images"><img alt="" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="29868d70-b2be-42a2-9190-2d200b9ab1a6" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="500" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/trumpuae.jpg?itok=KAlh7mmz" typeof="foaf:Image" width="500" /><figcaption><em>Getty Images</em></figcaption></figure></picture></a>

<p>According to more developments out of <a href="https://www.aljazeera.com/news/liveblog/2025/5/15/donald-trump-live-us-president-signs-multibillion-dollar-deals-with-qatar">the UAE</a>:</p>

<ul><li><em>The White House said that Trump and Qatar’s Emir Sheikh Tamim bin Hamad Al Thani <a href="https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2025/5/14/key-takeaways-from-day-two-of-donald-trumps-tour-of-the-middle-east">signed agreements</a> that would “generate an economic exchange worth at least $1.2 trillion”.</em></li>
	<li tabindex="-1"><em>The <a href="https://www.aljazeera.com/video/newsfeed/2025/5/14/peace-talks-boeing-jets-headline-trump-state-visit-to-qatar">agreements</a> are said to include a $96bn deal with Qatar Airways to buy up to 210 Boeing 787 Dreamliner and 777X aeroplanes, and a statement of intent for $38bn in investments at Qatar’s Al Udeid Airbase and other air defence capabilities.</em></li>
	<li><em>A meeting is scheduled for later today of US, Turkish and Syrian officials to discuss details of Trump’s announced dropping of sanctions against Syria.</em></li>
	<li><em>Trump’s three-country tour of the Gulf state region will conclude in the United Arab Emirates on Thursday.</em></li>
</ul><p>Amid lots of awards ceremonies, accolades, and a state dinner...</p>

Certainly he'll come back to Washington awaiting immense controversy and backlash from the corporate media and his political enemies.</p>

Title: "Everything You Said Was Essentially Dishonest" - RFK Jr. Destroys Dems In First Major Hearing As HHS Secretary
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">"Everything You Said Was Essentially Dishonest" - RFK Jr. Destroys Dems In First Major Hearing As HHS Secretary</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><em><a href="https://www.vigilantfox.com/p/rfk-jr-stuns-critics-in-his-first">Via VigilantFox.com</a></em></p>

<p><strong>RFK Jr. just walked into Congress and took down his biggest critics in one fell swoop.</strong></p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/Gq7XJlaXwAAyEnl.jpg?itok=nRnvEWT_" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/Gq7XJlaXwAAyEnl.jpg?itok=nRnvEWT_"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="ad9d87e4-0f2e-4465-a3cd-737e4c0a8986" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="282" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/Gq7XJlaXwAAyEnl.jpg?itok=nRnvEWT_" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>This was a masterclass.</p>

<p>A dentist congressman came out swinging on fluoride. By the time Kennedy finished, he realized he picked the wrong fight.</p>

<p>Then, a Democrat tried to accuse Kennedy of politicizing children’s health—but he got emotional, broke through the noise, and completely flipped the script on her.</p>

<p>If you watch one thing today, make it this. Kennedy just took the MAHA agenda to the next level.</p>

<p>Right out of the gate in his first major congressional hearing as HHS Secretary, Kennedy laid out a sweeping plan to reshape HHS from the ground up.</p>

<p>Here’s what’s on deck:</p>

<ul><li>
	<p>Ending “gain-of-function experiments and research based upon radical gender ideology”</p>
	</li>
	<li>
	<p>A full-scale crackdown on fentanyl and drug addiction</p>
	</li>
	<li>
	<p>$94 billion toward better food, fitness, and childcare</p>
	</li>
	<li>
	<p>FDA action to remove toxic chemicals from the food supply</p>
	</li>
	<li>
	<p>Slashing wasteful NIH projects</p>
	</li>
	<li>
	<p>Merging mental health and addiction programs for faster, better care</p>
	</li>
	<li>
	<p>Giving local leaders more power to fix problems in their own communities</p>
	</li>
	<li>
	<p>A major upgrade to Head Start, the early education program for low-income children</p>
	</li>
</ul><p><strong>“We intend to make the Trump HHS not just the most effective, but also the most compassionate in U.S. history,”</strong> Kennedy said.</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet" data-media-max-width="560">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">Right out of the gate in his first major congressional hearing as HHS Secretary, Kennedy laid out a sweeping plan to reshape HHS from the ground up.<br /><br />
Here’s what’s on deck:<br /><br />
• Ending “gain-of-function experiments and research based upon radical gender ideology”<br /><br />
• A full-scale… <a href="https://t.co/kptlIiHfet">pic.twitter.com/kptlIiHfet</a></p>
— The Vigilant Fox 🦊 (@VigilantFox) <a href="https://twitter.com/VigilantFox/status/1922717549206147325?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 14, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>Then came a tense back-and-forth with Democrat Rep. Rosa DeLauro, who tried to pin him down on tobacco prevention funding. Kennedy didn’t just answer—he flipped the entire narrative.</p>

<p>DeLauro asked, “Do you commit to following the law, again, fully obligating those funds so that we can help adults who want to quit using tobacco and prevent teens from becoming addicted?”</p>

<p>Kennedy fired back: <strong>“</strong>Allow me to answer that by pointing out the absolute cataclysmic disorganization of this agency. <strong>Under your oversight, for 40 years</strong>, we had nine separate offices of Women’s Health.”</p>

<p>And he didn’t stop there.</p>

<p>“When we consolidate them, the Democrats say we’re eliminating them. We’re not. We’re still appropriating the 3.7 billion, but we’re not keeping all nine. We had eight separate offices for minority health. We eliminated one. <strong>We had 27 HIV offices</strong>.”</p>

<p>DeLauro tried to interrupt—“Okay, let me just. I’m going to—”</p>

<p>But Kennedy kept rolling: <strong>“We had 59 behavioral health programs.”</strong></p>

<p>At that point, DeLauro backed off: “I’m well over time.”</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet" data-media-max-width="680">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">Then came a tense back-and-forth with Democrat Rep. Rosa DeLauro, who tried to pin him down on tobacco funding. Kennedy didn’t just answer—he flipped the entire narrative.<br /><br />
DeLauro asked, “Do you commit to following the law, again, fully obligating those funds so that we can help… <a href="https://t.co/QHceNdH2xu">pic.twitter.com/QHceNdH2xu</a></p>
— The Vigilant Fox 🦊 (@VigilantFox) <a href="https://twitter.com/VigilantFox/status/1922717871051792833?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 14, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>One of the most jaw-dropping moments came when Rep. Mike Simpson, a dentist, tried to challenge Kennedy on fluoride—and instantly regretted it.</p>

<p>“We better put a lot more money into dental education because we’re going to need a whole lot more dentists [if we ban fluoride],” Simpson said.</p>

<p>The rebuttal was too easy for Kennedy.</p>

<p>“We now know that <strong>virtually all the benefit [from fluoride] is from topical</strong>, and we can get that through mouthwashes. We can get through fluoridated toothpastes.”</p>

<p>Then came the line that hit hard:</p>

<p>“The National Toxicity Program issued a report in August, a meta review of all the science that now exists on fluoride, and <strong>showed a direct inverse correlation between fluoride exposure dose and lower IQ</strong>.”</p>

<p>“Which is an issue that we all have to be concerned with. We want high IQ kids right now,” Kennedy added.</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet" data-media-max-width="680">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">One of the most jaw-dropping moments came when Rep. Mike Simpson, a dentist, tried to challenge Kennedy on fluoride—and instantly regretted it.<br /><br />

— The Vigilant Fox 🦊 (@VigilantFox) <a href="https://twitter.com/VigilantFox/status/1922718037091762243?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 14, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>Later, Rep. Steny Hoyer demanded answers on HHS budget cuts—but Kennedy was ready with numbers and a blunt dose of reality.</p>

<p><strong>“We’re spending $2 trillion a year that we don’t have!”</strong></p>

<p>He followed up: <strong>“When you’re spending $2 trillion more than you have, you have to make cuts.”</strong></p>

<p>Hoyer pressed again. Kennedy stayed firm.</p>

<p>“The cuts that were done were cuts that were to duplication, to redundancy, to streamlining,” he said. “We increased our workforce 70% in four years. So we were going <strong>back to the 2019 levels</strong>.”</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet" data-media-max-width="680">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">Later, Rep. Steny Hoyer demanded answers on HHS budget cuts—but Kennedy was ready with numbers and a blunt dose of reality.<br /><br />

— The Vigilant Fox 🦊 (@VigilantFox) <a href="https://twitter.com/VigilantFox/status/1922718153341124823?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 14, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>Then came a moment of visible deflation from Rep. Mark Pocan, who tried—repeatedly—to get Kennedy to endorse vaccines.</p>

<p>“If you had a child today, would you vaccinate that child for measles?” Pocan asked.</p>

<p>Kennedy didn’t bite.</p>

<p>“What I would say is my opinions about vaccines are irrelevant,” he said. “I think what we’re going to try to do is to lay out the pros and cons, the risks and benefits accurately as we understand them.”</p>

<p>Pocan pressed again: “Can you talk about chickenpox?”</p>

<p>Kennedy exposed a reality Pocan didn’t want to hear:</p>

<p>“Again, I don’t want to give advice. I can tell you in Europe, they don’t use the chickenpox vaccine specifically because the preclinical trial shows that <strong>when you inoculate the population for chickenpox, you get shingles in older people, which is more dangerous</strong>.”</p>

<p>Desperate for something, Pocan asked, “Polio?”</p>

<p>“Again, I don’t want to be giving advice,” Kennedy replied.</p>

<p>Pocan backed off with a clear look of disappointment: “That’s fair. No, that’s fair. Like I said, I was not doing it as a gotcha…”</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet" data-media-max-width="680">

Kennedy didn’t bite.<br /><br />
“What I would say is my opinions about vaccines are… <a href="https://t.co/lnpBEIfpGH">pic.twitter.com/lnpBEIfpGH</a></p>
— The Vigilant Fox 🦊 (@VigilantFox) <a href="https://twitter.com/VigilantFox/status/1922718311306957096?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 14, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>One of the most shocking revelations came when Kennedy pointed to corruption inside NIH as the reason we still don’t have a cure for Alzheimer’s.</p>

<p>“For 20 years, because of utter corruption and fraud, we were directing Alzheimer’s research to one hypothesis, and any other hypothesis was shut down,” he said.</p>

<p>“We should have the cure for Alzheimer’s today. <strong>We don’t have it PURELY because of corruption at NIH. And we are going to have it quickly.</strong>”</p>

<p>Rep. Lois Frankel attacked Kennedy’s use of HHS funds, characterizing it as Elon Musk randomly plugging numbers into a computer to make decisions.</p>

<p>Kennedy fired back, taking offense at that false narrative.</p>

<p><strong>“Everything that you said was essentially dishonest,”</strong> he told her.</p>

“Everything that you said was essentially dishonest,” he told her. <a href="https://t.co/ZZP4igMY0C">pic.twitter.com/ZZP4igMY0C</a></p>
— The Vigilant Fox 🦊 (@VigilantFox) <a href="https://twitter.com/VigilantFox/status/1922719206618898456?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 14, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>Later, Kennedy clashed with Rep. DeLauro once more. This time, he let loose.</p>

<p><strong>“Look at our children, they’re the sickest children in the world,”</strong> he said passionately.</p>

<p>Kennedy delivered a direct blow to DeLauro, noting he succeeded where she failed.</p>

<p>“Congresswoman DeLauro, you say that you’ve worked for 20 years on getting food dye out. <strong>Then give me credit!”</strong> he exclaimed. <strong>“I got it out in 100 days.”</strong></p>

<p>He then closed with a call to unity:</p>

<p>“So, let’s work together and do something that we all believe in, which is have healthy kids in our country for God’s sake. <strong>There’s no such thing as Republican children or Democratic children</strong>. There’s just kids, and we should all be concerned with them.”</p>
