<span property="schema:dateCreated" content="2025-05-15T18:45:00+00:00" class="field field--name-created field--type-created field--label-hidden">Thu, 05/15/2025 - 14:45</span>


Title: White House Has Presented Iran With Written Nuke Deal Proposal In Huge First
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">White House Has Presented Iran With Written Nuke Deal Proposal In Huge First</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><strong><u>Update(10:30ET)</u>:</strong> With President Trump and his envoy having arrived in the United Arab Emirates (UAE) for the last leg of the president's Gulf tour, new details of behind the scenes US-Iran negotiations have come to light on Thursday.</p>

<p>In a huge first, the Trump White House has <strong>sent Iran a written proposal toward forging a new nuclear deal</strong>. White House envoy Steve Witkoff has led several rounds of talks, and Axios has revealed that the communication was issued to Tehran last Sunday.</p>

<p>"Iranian Foreign Minister Abbas Araghchi took the proposal back to Tehran for consultations with Supreme Leader Ali Khamenei, President Masoud Pezeshkian and other top officials," writes <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/15/iran-deal-proposal-witkoff-enrichment">Axios</a>.</p>
<a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/irannclr.jpg?itok=1L74-vIx" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/irannclr.jpg?itok=1L74-vIx"><picture><figure role="group" class="caption caption-img inline-images image-style-inline-images"><img alt="" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="cd649d64-ef1c-4763-9017-858bf93606a7" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="281" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/irannclr.jpg?itok=1L74-vIx" typeof="foaf:Image" width="500" /><figcaption><em>Via Associated Press</em></figcaption></figure></picture></a>

<p>It was the Iranian side which <strong>initiated the swap of written proposals</strong> first, as the talks which have been on since April went from 'indirect' to more <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/15/iran-deal-proposal-witkoff-enrichment">'direct'</a>:</p>

<ul><li><em>During the third round of talks in late April, Araghchi gave Witkoff an updated document with Iranian ideas for a nuclear deal. This time, Witkoff took the document.</em></li>
	<li><em>A U.S. team of experts studied it and sent the Iranians a list of questions and requests for clarification. The Iranians replied and added questions of their own, two sources said.</em></li>
	<li><em>Meanwhile, Witkoff and his team prepared a U.S. proposal laying out the Trump administration's parameters for an Iranian civilian nuclear program and requirements for monitoring and verification, the sources said.</em></li>
</ul><p>It appears that thus far both sides have received the other's written proposals positively, and that's what was driving President Trump's "olive branch" comments on Tuesday. He had stressed while speaking in Saudi Arabia that <strong>"this is not an offer that will last forever. The time is right now for them to choose."</strong></p>

<p>President Trump followed up on Thursday by saying from Qatar,  "We're in <strong>very serious negotiations </strong>with Iran for long-term peace," according to AFP.</p>

<p>He said, "We're getting close to maybe doing a deal without having to do this... there (are) two steps to doing this, there is a very, very nice step and there is the violent step, but I don't want to do it the second."</p>

<p>Trump's comments followed an <a href="https://www.nbcnews.com/news/us-news/iran-enriched-uranium-nuclear-deal-trump-rcna206833">NBC News</a> interview with Ali Shamkhani, a top political, military and nuclear adviser to Iranian Supreme Leader Ayatollah Ali Khamenei, who said Tehran is prepared to sign a nuclear deal—provided key conditions are met—in exchange for the lifting of U.S. economic sanctions. </p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">Trump reposted the NBC article indicating Iran is ready to reach a deal (though the details of that deal suggest it would look essentially identical to the JCPOA). <a href="https://t.co/LPDLzqu0nd">pic.twitter.com/LPDLzqu0nd</a></p>
— Gregory Brew (@gbrew24) <a href="https://twitter.com/gbrew24/status/1923005051322212696?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 15, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>NBC News pointed out that Shamkhani's comments "appear to be the clearest public statement yet on Iran's expectations and willingness to reach a deal from the supreme leader's inner circle." </p>

<p>And the fact that written proposals have already been exchanged is yet further confirmation of this positive trend towards peace. Trump has emphasized that Iran can never have a nuclear bomb, but Tehran itself has long said it's not pursuing a nuke, and that its program is only for peaceful domestic energy purposes.</p>

<p>* * *</p>

<p>Brent crude prices fell on Thursday as geopolitical risk premiums eased following President Trump's comments during his Gulf tour, where he signaled that the U.S. is nearing a nuclear deal with Iran. Unlike earlier headlines on AI, defense, and aviation deals with Saudi Arabia and Qatar, Trump's comments suggested a potential breakthrough in U.S.-Iran nuclear talks.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="https://store.zerohedge.com/rancher-direct-clean-food/" data-image-href="https://store.zerohedge.com/rancher-direct-clean-food/" data-link-option="2" href="https://store.zerohedge.com/rancher-direct-clean-food/"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="06de12fd-f045-4655-9540-139bf6e6bf1f" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="287" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/bbq%20stockup_0.JPG?itok=Wd2Gb13b" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>"We're in very serious negotiations with Iran for long-term peace," Trump told reporters in a press pool that AFP News first reported. </p>

<p>Speaking in Doha, Qatar, during his Middle East trip, the president said, "We're getting close to maybe doing a deal without having to do this... there (are) two steps to doing this, there is a very, very nice step and there is the violent step, but I don't want to do it the second way."</p>

<p>An Iranian source told <a href="https://www.reuters.com/world/trump-says-us-is-getting-very-close-nuclear-deal-with-iran-2025-05-15/">Reuters</a> that negotiations with Trump administration officials still needed to bridge some gaps before a final deal could be reached. </p>

<p>Trump's comments followed an <a href="https://www.nbcnews.com/news/us-news/iran-enriched-uranium-nuclear-deal-trump-rcna206833">NBC News</a> interview with Ali Shamkhani, a top political, military and nuclear adviser to Iranian Supreme Leader Ayatollah Ali Khamenei, who said Tehran is prepared to sign a nuclear deal—provided key conditions are met—in exchange for the lifting of U.S. economic sanctions. </p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">With Trump Touring Gulf, Iran Offers Huge Nuclear Concession <a href="https://t.co/NQ4259UIsE">https://t.co/NQ4259UIsE</a></p>
— zerohedge (@zerohedge) <a href="https://twitter.com/zerohedge/status/1922796096553714104?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 14, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">Trump confirms reports that Iran have “sort of agreed to the terms” that they cannot have nuclear capabilities!<br /><br />
Trump confirms he is currently in “very serious negotiations with Iran, for long-term peace”!<br /><br />
Trump also highlights how “many people” want war with Iran, but that he… <a href="https://t.co/rVSkScNRIN">pic.twitter.com/rVSkScNRIN</a></p>
— Clandestine (@WarClandestine) <a href="https://twitter.com/WarClandestine/status/1922920176497942987?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 15, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>NBC News pointed out that Shamkhani's comments "appear to be the clearest public statement yet on Iran's expectations and willingness to reach a deal from the supreme leader's inner circle." </p>

<p>Trump has offered "an olive branch" to Tehran after a multi-month maximum-pressure campaign, including economic sanctions and deploying long-range stealth bombers to America's "<a href="https://www.zerohedge.com/military/stealth-bombers-reportedly-deploying-americas-unsinkable-carrier">unsinkable aircraft carrier</a>" - located in the Indian Ocean - ready to be deployed at a moment's notice.</p>

<p>However, last week, ahead of Trump's Gulf tour, we spotted at least one of these <a href="https://www.zerohedge.com/geopolitical/stealth-bomber-returns-diego-garcia-us-iran-nuclear-talks-head-fourth-round">stealth bombers returning</a> to the U.S. We suggested this may have been an act of goodwill ahead of talks by the U.S. or possibly just a routine flight.  </p>

<p>On Thursday, Brent crude futures fell 3% to $60 a barrel on expectations that a U.S.-Iran nuclear deal would ease sanctions and increase crude oil on international markets.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/bfmA82E_0.jpg?itok=lfhf4u5y" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/bfmA82E_0.jpg?itok=lfhf4u5y"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="6362d6b1-1bd6-4d1f-9878-a3f8f1757d28" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="278" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/bfmA82E_0.jpg?itok=lfhf4u5y" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>"The overnight development of a possible nuclear deal is the sole reason for the morning's weakness. If an agreement is reached, Iran agrees to halt enriching weapon grade uranium and the deal is effectively enforced, which is hard to believe, then the Persian Gulf country's crude oil exports can rise by as much as 1 [million barrels per day]," PVM analyst Tamas Varga told CNBC in an emailed statement. </p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/Snag_1abc566.png?itok=DgbG36Ld" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/Snag_1abc566.png?itok=DgbG36Ld"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="06410f5a-0513-4d48-b7a8-c69582c40598" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="274" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/Snag_1abc566.png?itok=DgbG36Ld" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>"It sounds price negative, but its impact will possibly be mitigated by OPEC+ rolling back on its plan to release barrels back to the market faster than originally planned," he added.</p>

<p>Goldman trader Rich Privorotsky commented on the development: </p>

<blockquote>
<p><em>Staying with geopolitics there are some rather positive stories emanating out of Iran. "Iran is ready to sign a nuclear deal with certain conditions with President Donald Trump in exchange for lifting economic sanctions, a top adviser to Iran's supreme leader told NBC News on Wednesday." Unclear if the U.S. will agree to the terms but they seem fairly broad: "He said Iran would commit to never making nuclear weapons, getting rid of its stockpiles of highly enriched uranium which can be weaponized, agree to only enrich uranium to the lower levels needed for civilian use, and allow international inspectors to supervise the process, in exchange for the immediate lifting of all economic sanctions on Iran." (NBC news) If confirmed I think oil could eventually end up heading back to the recent lows and I would continue to express any cyclical concerns in this space.</em></p>
</blockquote>

<p>Here's the latest commentary from UBS traders:</p>

<blockquote>
<p><em>Oil Equity Resilience Amid Oil Price Drop Oil prices are down, mainly because of a potential deal with Iran. That could mean up to 500kb/d increased supply coming to market very quickly. Oil equities, however, are already underweight for generalists and specialists have already de-grossed, following the OPEC+ surprises so far this year - hence oil equities are proving to be relatively resilient even though the oil price is down.</em></p>
</blockquote>

<p>If Trump secures a nuclear deal with Tehran, it would cap off a week of landmark agreements with Gulf nations—collectively worth trillions—and add to an already bullish news cycle for the president. Also, this would mean continued easing of geopolitical risk premiums in the region, in other words, lower energy prices for Trump to pursue his 'America First' agenda.</p>
</div>
      <span rel="schema:author" class="field field--name-uid field--type-entity-reference field--label-hidden"><a title="View user profile." href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" lang="" about="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" typeof="schema:Person" property="schema:name" datatype="" class="username" xml:lang="">Tyler Durden</a></span>
<span property="schema:dateCreated" content="2025-05-15T18:22:00+00:00" class="field field--name-created field--type-created field--label-hidden">Thu, 05/15/2025 - 14:22</span>


Title: Ukraine Will Never Recognize Occupied Territories As Russia, Zelensky Says From Turkey
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Ukraine Will Never Recognize Occupied Territories As Russia, Zelensky Says From Turkey</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><strong><u>Update(1105ET)</u>: "</strong>We don’t yet know the official level of Russians, but from what we see, <strong>it looks phony</strong>," Zelensky told reporters in Ankara. So despite the Ukrainian leader earlier declaring "I am here" upon landing in Turkey, he is not in fact at the Russia-Ukraine talks in Istanbul.</p>

<p>This <em>'I am here' yet not actually 'there'</em> charade generated some contradictory headlines earlier on Thursday. Zelensky <strong>continues his performative gestures aimed at impressing one man: Trump</strong>. He even explained that he is sending Defense Minister Rustem Umerov to head the Ukrainian delegation for the Istanbul meeting, now likely underway, <strong>out of respect for Trump and the peace process he initiated</strong>. </p>

<p>The Kremlin side meanwhile says it's ready to make <a href="https://www.cnn.com/world/live-news/ukraine-russia-talks-istanbul-turkey-intl">compromises</a>:</p>

<blockquote>
<p data-article-gutter="true" data-component-name="paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="cms.cnn.com/_components/paragraph/instances/cmapfupvp000k3b6mxrxmlap3@published"><em>The head of the Russian delegation in Istanbul, Vladimir Medinsky, told Russian state media RIA that Moscow was “ready for discussions.”</em></p>

<p data-article-gutter="true" data-component-name="paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="cms.cnn.com/_components/paragraph/instances/cmapg7o2m000t3b6ms08rojan@published"><em>“We are ready for discussions, for resuming the Istanbul negotiations;<strong> we are prepared for possible compromises</strong> and their discussion,” Medinsky said, referring to the last known direct talks between Russia and Ukraine that took place in Istanbul in the spring of 2022.</em></p>
</blockquote>

<p data-article-gutter="true" data-component-name="paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="cms.cnn.com/_components/paragraph/instances/cmapgdtf9000y3b6ma4xgwstc@published">But apparently <strong><em>not on the table</em> is the only thing which could actually end this tragic war - territorial concessions</strong>: </p>

<blockquote>
<p data-article-gutter="true" data-component-name="paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="cms.cnn.com/_components/paragraph/instances/cmapgdtf9000y3b6ma4xgwstc@published"><em>Ukraine’s President Volodymyr Zelensky said Kyiv will never recognize parts of Ukraine that are currently occupied as parts of Russia, as he confirmed peace talks are set to go ahead.</em></p>

<p data-article-gutter="true" data-component-name="paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="cms.cnn.com/_components/paragraph/instances/cmapfx7p0000n3b6miuqofcui@published"><em><strong>“In all discussions – and I emphasize this – and this is my unwavering position – we do not legally recognize any of our temporarily occupied territories as Russian. This is the Ukrainian land,”</strong> Zelensky told journalists.</em></p>
</blockquote>

<p>Still, the fact the two sides are even at the same table in Istanbul is a huge development and start.</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">⚡️ Russia delegation has been empowered to negotiate with Ukrainian side — Vladimir Medinsky reacts to the lull in Istanbul talks<br /><br />
'We view these talks as a continuation of negotiations BROKEN by Ukraine 3 years ago <a href="https://t.co/Kacw5hhDRM">pic.twitter.com/Kacw5hhDRM</a></p>
— RT (@RT_com) <a href="https://twitter.com/RT_com/status/1923031629804478876?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 15, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>And again, everything Zelensky is doing appears designed to signal Trump - in order to keep America as Kiev's top weapons backer. "Despite the relatively low level of the Russian delegation, <strong>out of respect for President Trump</strong>, out of respect for the high level of the Turkish delegation and for President Erdogan, we still want to try to take at least the first steps towards a ceasefire, so <strong>I have decided to send our delegation to Istanbul now</strong>," Zelensky said further.</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">Zelensky says he is sending defense minister Umerov for direct talks with the Russians in Istanbul, so that nobody (he means Trump) could accuse Ukraine of not trying to reach peace.</p>
— Yaroslav Trofimov (@yarotrof) <a href="https://twitter.com/yarotrof/status/1923021269399740524?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 15, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>* * *</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="https://store.zerohedge.com/rancher-direct-clean-food/" data-image-href="https://store.zerohedge.com/rancher-direct-clean-food/" data-link-option="2" href="https://store.zerohedge.com/rancher-direct-clean-food/"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="a10c4be6-e482-4b91-a012-6a9eda0c8131" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="287" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/bbq%20stockup.JPG?itok=QN-62S6Z" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>Russian President Vladimir Putin's investment envoy and close aide, Kirill Dmitriev, has praised US President Donald Trump for putting together Russia-Ukraine peace talks in Istanbul, the first such direct dialogue between the warring countries since early 2022.</p>

<p>Trump and his team have <strong>"made the impossible possible" </strong>by bringing Moscow and Kiev to the table. Dmitriev further <a href="https://x.com/kadmitriev/status/1922959414924832829">wrote on X</a> that the Istanbul meeting is happening <strong>"against all odds/fierce resistance"</strong> and that if "not derailed last-minute, this could be a historic step to peace."</p>

<p>Dmitriev also specifically named Vice President J.D. Vance, Trump’s special envoy Steve Witkoff and Secretary of State Marco Rubio - the latter two who are present in Istanbul - as <strong>major contributors to the mediation effort</strong>. The Kremlin had spent the opening years of the conflict blasting the Biden administration for constantly stoking the war and thwarting dialogue, taking Washington-Moscow relations to new historic lows.</p>
<a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/ukrtrky.jpg?itok=EPS6SdEl" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/ukrtrky.jpg?itok=EPS6SdEl"><picture><figure role="group" class="caption caption-img inline-images image-style-inline-images"><img alt="" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="552b32d4-aaa3-4e8a-b860-00dbe6939de8" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="281" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/ukrtrky.jpg?itok=EPS6SdEl" typeof="foaf:Image" width="500" /><figcaption><em>Via Anadolu Agency</em></figcaption></figure></picture></a>

<p>As we <a href="https://www.zerohedge.com/geopolitical/zelensky-istanbul-responds-insult-putin-sending-junior-officials-peace-talks-i-am-here">noted earlier</a>, Ukraine's President <strong>Zelensky is actually in Turkey</strong>, where he's set to meet with President Erdogan - but separately in the <strong>capital of Ankara</strong>, and has boasted that "I am here" and that Putin is not. Zelensky has even called the Russian delegation, largely composed of junior officials, <strong>"phony"</strong>. </p>

<p>President Trump meanwhile, while attending meetings in Qatar, was asked by a reporter why the American leader is not himself present in Turkey for the talks:</p>

<blockquote>
<p><em>"Why would he go if I’m not going?"</em></p>

<p><strong><em>"I wasn’t planning to go and I didn’t think he would if I didn’t."</em></strong></p>

<p><em>"But we have people there. Marco's doing a fantastic job, Marco's there..."</em></p>
</blockquote>

<p data-role="headline">It remains that Putin has little reason or incentive to go, with war analysts widely recognizing that he remains in the driver's seat militarily, and with Ukrainian forces against the ropes.</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">‘Why would he go if I’m not going?’: Trump reacts to Putin sitting out Istanbul talks<br /><br />
“I wasn’t planning to go and I didn’t think he would if I didn’t.” <a href="https://t.co/4YvqvO8gWh">pic.twitter.com/4YvqvO8gWh</a></p>
— Chay Bowes (@BowesChay) <a href="https://twitter.com/BowesChay/status/1922960657747497368?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 15, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p data-role="headline"><strong>Zelensky has until now offered no major concessions</strong>, and issues like permanent control over Crimea and the four eastern territories remain sticking points for Moscow. Thus there are unlikely to be any major breakthroughs in Istanbul, but the <strong>fact that the two sides are even at the table is a big accomplishment</strong>.</p>

<p data-role="headline"><em>Below is an important rundown of what's expected in Istanbul and what's at stake for both sides, excerpted from fresh Responsible Statecraft analysis, <a href="https://responsiblestatecraft.org/ukraine-russia-istanbul-talks/">Istanbul 2.0: know when to hold 'em, know when to fold 'em</a>:</em></p>

<p data-role="headline"><em>* * *</em></p>

<blockquote>
<p data-role="headline"><strong>What has changed since then?</strong></p>

<p>Ukraine will enter the Istanbul talks in a weaker position that it held in 2022.</p>

<p>Western support for Ukraine financially and economically is not as sound as it was then. No big ticket economic aid and assistance has been made available since the G7 agreement of a $50 billion package of loans, in June 2024. While European states scratched together <a cmp-ltrk="Article Links" cmp-ltrk-idx="4" data-mrf-link="https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/live/c89gpg4jpllt" href="https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/live/c89gpg4jpllt" mrfobservableid="3d83b61c-39c3-4844-8e66-7a285da414e5" target="_blank"><u>new economic aid</u></a> to Ukraine in April, this cannot make up for the reduction in US support.</p>

<p>In territorial terms, Russia withdrew from Kyiv as a concession to the first Istanbul talks and lost ground in Kharkiv and in Kherson in late 2022. However, Russia has gone on steadily to gain further territory in the Donbas since the end of 2023. So while both sides have scores on the board, Russia now maintains the military upper hand on the battlefield and that seems unlikely to change. These two factors in particular were behind President Trump’s February assertion that Ukraine has <a cmp-ltrk="Article Links" cmp-ltrk-idx="5" data-mrf-link="https://www.straitstimes.com/world/united-states/trump-says-ukraine-leaders-dont-have-any-cards-in-talks-on-russias-invasion" href="https://www.straitstimes.com/world/united-states/trump-says-ukraine-leaders-dont-have-any-cards-in-talks-on-russias-invasion" mrfobservableid="81ba6eb4-ee73-4ff4-9fbf-477fed315a95" target="_blank"><u>no cards to play</u></a>.</p>

<p data-role="headline"><strong>What has stayed the same?</strong></p>

<p>NATO membership is still off the table</p>

<p>The verified documents shared by the New York Times last June confirmed that Ukraine’s neutrality and non-membership of NATO was the central issue agreed upon in 2022. Ukraine was ready to become a “permanently neutral state” that would never join NATO or allow foreign forces to be based on its soil.</p>

<p>There seems no route for Ukraine to resile from that given its currently weakened negotiating position and President Trump’s stated view that NATO membership for Ukraine is <a cmp-ltrk="Article Links" cmp-ltrk-idx="6" data-mrf-link="https://www.reuters.com/world/trump-not-practical-ukraine-join-nato-get-back-all-land-2025-02-12/" href="https://www.reuters.com/world/trump-not-practical-ukraine-join-nato-get-back-all-land-2025-02-12/" mrfobservableid="6e933750-a559-4750-b74f-8e5616358413" target="_blank"><u>not practical.</u></a> Although Germany’s new foreign Minister, <a cmp-ltrk="Article Links" cmp-ltrk-idx="7" data-mrf-link="https://www.pravda.com.ua/eng/news/2025/05/10/7511618/" href="https://www.pravda.com.ua/eng/news/2025/05/10/7511618/" mrfobservableid="86641df8-c59d-41a8-b440-b27dfa2576f1" target="_blank"><u>Johann Wadephul</u></a> recently repeated the line that Ukraine’s path to NATO is irreversible, most have agreed, privately and publicly, that Ukraine’s path to NATO is a fraught if not impossible one.</p>

<p data-role="headline"><strong>Right now, just having the talks is a huge breakthrough</strong></p>

<p>The Istanbul talks would not be happening had the <a cmp-ltrk="Article Links" cmp-ltrk-idx="8" data-mrf-link="https://responsiblestatecraft.org/tag/trump-administration/" href="https://responsiblestatecraft.org/tag/trump-administration/" mrfobservableid="255b210e-699d-4692-aff0-b367d225ea00">Trump administration</a> not pushed for it so hard. We don’t need to rehash the “did they or didn’t they” debate around why Ukraine abandoned the Istanbul agreement in April 2022. What is clear, is that Ukraine became entrenched, not only in not negotiating with Russia, but in excluding Russia from all discussions on peace in Ukraine from then onward.</p>

<p>Having agreed in principle for Ukraine to accept neutral status Zelensky was pushing his own <a cmp-ltrk="Article Links" cmp-ltrk-idx="9" data-mrf-link="https://www.reuters.com/world/europe/what-is-zelenskiys-10-point-peace-plan-2022-12-28/" href="https://www.reuters.com/world/europe/what-is-zelenskiys-10-point-peace-plan-2022-12-28/" mrfobservableid="52a4e14d-a4ae-4de8-82dd-4425a41568eb" target="_blank"><u>ten point peace plan</u></a>. This included, among other things, Russia withdrawing its troops to the pre-2014 border, i.e. giving up Crimea and the Donbass and creating a Euro-Atlantic Security Architecture, by which he meant Ukraine joining NATO. Peace summits were organized in various countries that explicitly excluded Russia, culminating in the Switzerland event on June 15, 2024.</p>

<p>At this event, President Zelensky was dug in deeper on resisting any engagement with Russia until a full withdrawal of its troops from Ukraine, which was a completely unrealistic proposal. “Russia can start negotiations with us even tomorrow without waiting for anything – if they <a cmp-ltrk="Article Links" cmp-ltrk-idx="10" data-mrf-link="https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2024/6/16/summit-demands-ukraines-territorial-integrity-urges-dialogue-to-end-war" href="https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2024/6/16/summit-demands-ukraines-territorial-integrity-urges-dialogue-to-end-war" mrfobservableid="a4155b80-0e54-465c-80a0-acc4ba982bdd" target="_blank"><u>leave our legal territories</u></a>,” he said.</p>

<p>Even after President Trump was elected, <a cmp-ltrk="Article Links" cmp-ltrk-idx="11" data-mrf-link="https://apnews.com/article/eu-ukraine-russia-nato-trump-support-zelenskyy-276690fb0a334c769b1631a16843a2f4" href="https://apnews.com/article/eu-ukraine-russia-nato-trump-support-zelenskyy-276690fb0a334c769b1631a16843a2f4" mrfobservableid="adf8b76b-2e69-41ff-b042-0a18472ccbeb" target="_blank"><u>European leaders</u></a> clung to the line that “only Ukraine can decide what peace means.”’ I see no circumstances in which a Kamala Harris presidency would have cajoled President Zelensky to enter into negotiations. Tomorrow’s talks wouldn’t be happening unless the Trump administration broke a whole load of Ukrainian and European eggshells to get to this point.</p>
</blockquote>
<a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/anadolump.jpg?itok=f3rOxdAN" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/anadolump.jpg?itok=f3rOxdAN"><picture><figure role="group" class="caption caption-img inline-images image-style-inline-images"><img alt="" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="b7317284-348b-4ae0-b829-9d907dc01008" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="388" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/anadolump.jpg?itok=f3rOxdAN" typeof="foaf:Image" width="500" /><figcaption><em>Source: Anadolu Agency </em></figcaption></figure></picture></a>

<p data-role="headline">And <em>Responsible Statecraft </em>continues:</p>

<blockquote>
<p data-role="headline"><strong>The biggest issue now is territory</strong></p>

<p>Even though he was wrongly derided at the time by mainstream <a cmp-ltrk="Article Links" cmp-ltrk-idx="12" data-mrf-link="https://responsiblestatecraft.org/media/" href="https://responsiblestatecraft.org/media/" mrfobservableid="677c1fe1-4135-4423-a611-ac52fc6c1fac">media</a>, <a cmp-ltrk="Article Links" cmp-ltrk-idx="13" data-mrf-link="https://edition.cnn.com/2025/03/22/europe/witkoff-carlson-trump-russia-ukraine-talks-intl/index.html" href="https://edition.cnn.com/2025/03/22/europe/witkoff-carlson-trump-russia-ukraine-talks-intl/index.html" mrfobservableid="2346bfa4-2f29-4846-9d4c-32b76b884df8" target="_blank"><u>Steve Witkoff</u></a> correctly pointed out in his March interview with Tucker Carlson that the territorial issues in Ukraine will be most intractable. Russia’s decision in October 2022 to formally annex the four oblasts of Kherson, Zaporizhzhia, Donetsk, and Luhansk changed the calculus. However, Russia does not have full territorial control of any of those oblasts, which are cut through the middle by a hotly contested front line.</p>

<p>Resolving the line of control when the war ends is, by some margin, the most problematic challenge. This will be a hugely sensitive topic, and European allies will shoot down any major concessions to Russia, as they did when the idea surfaced that the U.S.might <em>de jure</em> recognise Russia’s occupation of <a cmp-ltrk="Article Links" cmp-ltrk-idx="14" data-mrf-link="https://edition.cnn.com/2025/04/25/world/trump-ukraine-crimea-explainer-intl/index.html" href="https://edition.cnn.com/2025/04/25/world/trump-ukraine-crimea-explainer-intl/index.html" mrfobservableid="56291079-0b2c-4e75-9089-cf4666fe1976" target="_blank"><u>Crimea</u></a>.</p>

<p>The most obvious settlement is a de facto recognition of occupation, a Cyprus-style scenario, that does not stand in the way of Ukraine’s future membership of the European Union. Even that will require detailed agreement on issues around demilitarization of the line of control and enforcing any ceasefire.</p>

<p data-role="headline"><strong>Sanctions are probably tricky, but also tractable</strong></p>

<p>As <a cmp-ltrk="Article Links" cmp-ltrk-idx="15" data-mrf-link="https://responsiblestatecraft.org/lift-sanctions-on-russia/" href="https://responsiblestatecraft.org/lift-sanctions-on-russia/" mrfobservableid="85112044-af09-4c22-bae0-d5ebd31c0d41" target="_self"><u>I have said before</u></a>, there is enormous scope to a plan that allows for the immediate lifting of the bulk of zero-impact measures, phasing out the remainder at points agreed to by both sides. The toughest issue remains the $300 billion in frozen Russian assets, mostly held in Belgium. Russia has shown a <a cmp-ltrk="Article Links" cmp-ltrk-idx="16" data-mrf-link="https://www.brookings.edu/articles/what-is-the-status-of-russias-frozen-sovereign-assets/#:~:text=Reuters%20reported%20in%20February%20that%20Russia%20was%20prepared,some%20of%20the%20money%20goes%20to%20Russian-controlled%20Ukraine." href="https://www.brookings.edu/articles/what-is-the-status-of-russias-frozen-sovereign-assets/#:~:text=Reuters%20reported%20in%20February%20that%20Russia%20was%20prepared,some%20of%20the%20money%20goes%20to%20Russian-controlled%20Ukraine." mrfobservableid="01ee7ccc-02d0-4916-8d02-e7662c7a6d5d" target="_blank"><u>willingness to concede</u></a> this funding to support reconstruction in Ukraine, including those parts that Russia occupies.</p>

<p>But there is texture here. Freeing up those funds for reconstruction would immediately remove the source of interest payments that are meeting Ukraine’s obligations on its $50 billion in <a cmp-ltrk="Article Links" cmp-ltrk-idx="17" data-mrf-link="https://responsiblestatecraft.org/russian-assets-ukraine/" href="https://responsiblestatecraft.org/russian-assets-ukraine/" mrfobservableid="ed969ba1-cdf5-46c3-b1a5-cf44dc73da91" target="_self"><u>debt to the G7</u></a>, agreed to in June 2024. But the more general policy question arises, how much of the freed up funding would be spent in Ukraine itself and how much in Russian-occupied Ukraine, where most of the war damage has occurred? The U.S. must keep the pressure on to ensure the talks stay on track.</p>

<p>A U.S. presence in Istanbul will be vital, to prevent, in particular, Ukraine from bailing on the talks. That’s why sending <a cmp-ltrk="Article Links" cmp-ltrk-idx="18" data-mrf-link="https://www.msn.com/en-gb/politics/government/trump-envoys-witkoff-and-kellogg-to-go-to-turkey-for-russia-ukraine-talks-sources-say/ar-AA1EGS2H?ocid=BingNewsSerp" href="https://www.msn.com/en-gb/politics/government/trump-envoys-witkoff-and-kellogg-to-go-to-turkey-for-russia-ukraine-talks-sources-say/ar-AA1EGS2H?ocid=BingNewsSerp" mrfobservableid="9950f75a-e28f-4fcd-a2d6-b803d1003d5f" target="_blank"><u>Steve Witkoff and Keith Kellogg</u></a> makes sense. The former is trusted by the Russian side while the latter has built relationships in Ukraine. Their presence serves to keep the process moving forward until a deal can be pushed over the line and the fighting can stop.</p>

<p>Bear in mind that the 2022 talks ran for a month and a half and the circumstances have materially changed as I have indicated above. While there has been speculation that <a cmp-ltrk="Article Links" cmp-ltrk-idx="19" data-mrf-link="https://www.msn.com/en-gb/news/world/trump-thinking-of-going-to-turkey-for-proposed-zelenskyy-putin-peace-talks/ar-AA1EEHH9?ocid=BingNewsSerp" href="https://www.msn.com/en-gb/news/world/trump-thinking-of-going-to-turkey-for-proposed-zelenskyy-putin-peace-talks/ar-AA1EEHH9?ocid=BingNewsSerp" mrfobservableid="7e194de6-67c6-4aa6-9527-d1688fd049a0" target="_blank"><u>President Trump</u></a> might drop into Istanbul, I am not sure that this is necessary if President Putin doesn’t himself attend. Knowing the Russians, I assess that Putin will want his own “‘meeting moment” with the U.S. President on terms that the Russian side can better choreograph. Indeed, that may be a prize for Russia’s engagement in the process, given its desire for a more comprehensive reset of relations with the U.S.</p>
</blockquote>
</div>

Title: Trump Admin Urges Supreme Court To Permit DOGE Access To Social Security Records
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Trump Admin Urges Supreme Court To Permit DOGE Access To Social Security Records</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><em><a href="https://www.theepochtimes.com/us/trump-admin-urges-supreme-court-to-permit-doge-access-to-social-security-records-5857423?utm_source=partner&utm_campaign=ZeroHedge&src_src=partner&src_cmp=ZeroHedge">Authored by Matthew Vadum via The Epoch Times</a> (emphasis ours),</em></p>

<p><strong>The Department of Justice urged the Supreme Court on May 13 to let the Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE) have access to Social Security data after lower courts blocked that access.</strong></p>
<a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/image_92%2840%29_0.jpg?itok=mORpFAhS" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/image_92%2840%29_0.jpg?itok=mORpFAhS"><picture><figure role="group" class="caption caption-img inline-images image-style-inline-images"><img alt="" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="ac83fae6-9ca8-449e-becb-a30e6b3b634e" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="333" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/image_92%2840%29_0.jpg?itok=mORpFAhS" typeof="foaf:Image" width="500" /><figcaption><em>The U.S. Supreme Court in Washington on April 3, 2025. Madalina Vasiliu/The Epoch Times</em></figcaption></figure></picture></a>

<p>President Donald Trump <a href="https://www.federalregister.gov/documents/2025/01/29/2025-02005/establishing-and-implementing-the-presidents-department-of-government-efficiency">issued</a> Executive Order 14158 on Jan. 20, implementing DOGE, an advisory body that recommends cost-cutting measures. The order directed the entity to “implement the President’s DOGE Agenda, by modernizing Federal technology and software to maximize governmental efficiency and productivity.”</p>

<p><strong>Solicitor General D. John Sauer argued in the new filing that the lower courts have overreached and are attempting to turn themselves into “the human resources department for the Executive Branch.”</strong></p>

<p>The filing came after Ellen Lipton Hollander, a Maryland-based federal district court judge, issued an <a href="https://storage.courtlistener.com/recap/gov.uscourts.mdd.577321/gov.uscourts.mdd.577321.49.0.pdf">order</a> on March 20 preventing DOGE from viewing Social Security Administration (SSA) records because such access “violates” the federal Privacy Act.</p>

<p><strong>The lawsuit was brought in February by labor unions and retirees represented by the Democracy Forward Foundation.</strong></p>

<p>“The DOGE Team is essentially engaged in a fishing expedition at SSA, in search of a fraud epidemic, based on little more than suspicion. It has launched a search for the proverbial needle in the haystack, without any concrete knowledge that the needle is actually in the haystack,” the judge wrote in granting a temporary restraining order against the federal government.</p>

<p>DOGE’s team at the Social Security Administration has had “unbridled access to the personal and private data of millions of Americans, including but not limited to Social Security numbers, medical records, mental health records, hospitalization records, drivers’ license numbers, bank and credit card information, tax information, income history, work history, birth and marriage certificates, and home and work addresses,” Hollander wrote.</p>

<p><strong>Hollander directed DOGE to delete any personally identifiable data in its possession. </strong>On April 17, Hollander <a href="https://www.theepochtimes.com/us/federal-judge-limits-doge-access-to-social-security-data-5843929">upgraded</a> the temporary restraining order to a preliminary injunction.</p>

<p>On April 30, the U.S. Court of Appeals for the Fourth Circuit voted 9–6 to maintain Hollander’s order while the appeal process continues.</p>

<p>On May 2, the Trump administration <a href="https://www.theepochtimes.com/us/trump-admin-asks-supreme-court-to-allow-doge-access-to-social-security-data-5851531">filed</a> an emergency appeal with the Supreme Court, asking the justices to pause the preliminary injunction.</p>

<p>In the May 13 <a href="https://www.supremecourt.gov/DocketPDF/24/24A1063/358729/20250513153432172_SSA%20v.%20AFSCME%20%20-%20Stay%20Application%20Reply%20-%20Final.pdf">filing</a>, Sauer argued that the district court erred in preventing “the 11 members of the Social Security Administration (SSA) DOGE team—from accessing data ... for purposes that are unquestionably lawful.”</p>

<p>The district court “dictated to the Executive Branch which government employees can access which data and even prescribed necessary training, background checks, and paperwork for data access,” Sauer wrote.</p>

<p>“<strong>When district courts attempt to transform themselves into the human resources department for the Executive Branch, the irreparable harm to the government is clear</strong>,” he wrote.</p>

<p>When the courts “stymie the government’s initiatives to modernize badly outdated systems and combat rampant fraud—leaving those initiatives on a litigation track that may halt them for months or years—the irreparable harm is even clearer.”</p>

<p>Reviewing Social Security Administration data is important because the agency has “one of the largest documented histories of improper payments,” Sauer stated.</p>

<p>In a <a href="https://www.supremecourt.gov/DocketPDF/24/24A1063/358633/20250512154859924_AFSCME%20v%20SSA%20Opposition%20to%20Stay.pdf">brief</a> in opposition filed on May 12, the lead respondent, the American Federation of State, County, and Municipal Employees, said that after years of honoring “its data security obligations,” the Social Security Administration “now seeks to throw open its data systems to unauthorized (and often unvetted) personnel who have no demonstrated need for the personally identifiable information ... they seek.”</p>

<p>The April 17 preliminary injunction should be left in place because it is “narrow and, contrary to the government’s assertions, permits SSA to disclose both anonymized and non-anonymized data to DOGE Team members,” the brief said.</p>

<p><strong>The Supreme Court could rule on the government’s emergency application at any time.</strong></p>

<p><em>Jack Phillips contributed to this report.</em></p>

Title: DEXCORE suits up under surveillance in “Trace” music video, from 2nd album “WE WERE HERE”
Description: <img width="1200" height="640" src="https://jrocknews.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/05/dexcore-trace-artist-photo-edited-1200x640.jpg" class="attachment-large size-large wp-post-image" alt="" decoding="async" srcset="https://jrocknews.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/05/dexcore-trace-artist-photo-edited.jpg 1200w, https://jrocknews.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/05/dexcore-trace-artist-photo-edited-200x107.jpg 200w, https://jrocknews.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/05/dexcore-trace-artist-photo-edited-750x400.jpg 750w" sizes="(max-width: 1200px) 100vw, 1200px" /><p>DEXCORE released their second album WE WERE HERE digitally on May 7. The album was originally due to release on April 23, but due to production issues, the release, both digitally and physically, was postponed. To coincide with the album&#8217;s digital release, the band revealed the music video for the 10th song, Trace. Throughout, the [&#8230;]</p>

Title: Why Is The Secret German Spy Report On The AfD Party Only Filled With Public Statements?
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Why Is The Secret German Spy Report On The AfD Party Only Filled With Public Statements?</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><em><a href="https://rmx.news/article/why-is-the-secret-german-spy-report-on-the-afd-party-only-filled-with-public-statements/">Via Remix News,</a></em></p>

<p>The German domestic spy service, the Office of the Protection of the Constitution (BfV), has released a 1,100-page report on the Alternative for Germany (AfD), which it used to label the party a “confirmed” right-wing extremist party. The report is huge and reads like it was written by Antifa, but that was to be expected. <strong>However, one interesting point is that it contains only public statements, including quotes made by AfD politicians and a lot of<a href="https://x.com/jonasgreindberg/status/1922764456985231822"> memes</a>.</strong></p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/20250515_RMX_02.jpg?itok=AfveXFCG" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/20250515_RMX_02.jpg?itok=AfveXFCG"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="9a680130-db39-4377-b1d6-7a34c383a589" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="281" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/20250515_RMX_02.jpg?itok=AfveXFCG" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p><strong>Why is that?</strong></p>

<p>We already know that the BfV is secretly surveilling AfD members in certain German states, mostly in the east, where the party is “confirmed right-wing extremist” already. This designation allows for the BfV in those states to partake in extraordinary surveillance powers over AfD members, including reading their chats and emails. Presumably, they can also track their browsing history, and perhaps they are even listening in on their conversations at home.</p>

<p>What this means is that the BfV has plenty of statements, memes and content to use based on <em>private statements</em>, but it is purposefully choosing not to use them. After all, a certain number of those AfD members, in private moments, probably also express opinions, post memes, or share thoughts that the BfV would love to include in a secret report on the party, which many hope will eventually justify an outright ban.</p>

<p><strong>Again, why is the BfV not using these private statements?</strong></p>

<p>There are multiple reasons.</p>

<p><strong>For one, a big part of the apparatus of spy agencies is to obtain information, but not release it to the public.</strong> The public may not be able to stomach such personal and private information and the means that were used to obtain it. Since the Edward Snowden revelations, and even before then, we have become acutely aware that we have accepted devices into our lives and homes that can be used to spy on us on a scale never seen before in history. However, even now — even after all this information has been revealed — I believe nearly all of us still cannot quite grasp what this means — nor do we want to.</p>

<p><strong>Yes, we know that AfD members are being spied on across Germany. Their emails are read, their phone calls are recorded. </strong>AI is being used to sort out keywords of interest to the security services. However, nobody really knows how this information is being processed and what it is being used for, or even who is reading it. The spies who control this information have extraordinary power. As a significant portion of them are now far left, at least in Germany, they believe they are acting as a bulwark against the rise of Nazism, and the ends justify the means when it comes to the AfD. There are other psychological motives at work, of course, as spy agencies are on the whole very good at keeping their secrets, not even necessarily because of internal controls, but because the spies are dedicated to their mission. There is, also, the sense of power that comes with being the watcher, and for many spies, this is a powerful intoxicant. They know, while you are in the dark.</p>

<p><strong>In practice, these spies know which AfD members are having affairs, their personal struggles, their health issues, their financial situation, and even their personal browsing history.</strong> In other words, they know their targets better in many cases than even their close friends and family. The spies of the world, not just in Germany, are now in many ways gods and mind readers, seeing through the walls people build up around themselves and accessing their darkest fears and secrets — all due to rapid advances in technology and the rise of smartphones.</p>

<p><strong>Earlier this month, commentator Eva Vlaardingerbroek, the famed Dutch activist reported that she was alerted that her phone was being breached with Pegasus-like spyware, </strong>mainly produced in Israel, which can unlock essentially every aspect of her personal life, including chats, location data, photos, contacts, and so on. With this software, they can even record her in real time, including personal conversations in her home, as well as turn on her camera to record her in her most personal moments.</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">After having been alerted that the deep state is spying on me through mercenary spyware, I've been feeling like there is someone standing in the room with me at all times.<br /><br />
Now, I'm not naive: exposing the wicked ways of the establishment is quite literally at the core of my… <a href="https://t.co/16dXkeJMAq">pic.twitter.com/16dXkeJMAq</a></p>
— Eva Vlaardingerbroek (@EvaVlaar) <a href="https://twitter.com/EvaVlaar/status/1920160052239089964?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 7, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p><strong>This software, and software like it, has been used on thousands of people, including journalists, politicians, and activists, sometimes with deadly results. </strong>It is not just the right, but far-left activists have also been targeted, including human rights activists. It is also unclear how long Vlaardingerbroek may have been targeted in such a manner. Previous versions of Apple iOS may have not been able to detect this software on her phone. In short, much of her personal life may already be in a database somewhere waiting to be used by intelligence.</p>

<p>Vlaardingerbroek is not in the AfD or even German, but she has backed the party, and she and people like her are most certainly the target of intelligence operatives in countries across Europe.</p>

<p>The point is that this software and the means for surveilling people are very unsettling.<strong> In a privacy-minded country like Germany, revealing the scale of surveillance being used against the AfD may be a scandal within itself, and could taint the entire report, which at the end of the day, should be used to justify a ban of the AfD.</strong></p>

<p>There may have been voices in the BfV who were calling to use secretly recorded data in the report as well, but the agency also knew this report would eventually be leaked and made public. The agency does not appear to want to divulge who they are surveilling, what information they have about them, and how they obtained this information.</p>

<p>Another important consideration is also to be taken into account. The BfV decided it did not need to include this secret information in the report because it is likely confident that it can get what it wants using public statements alone. It can still keep the scale of its surveillance secret and get the ban it desires — at least that is the gamble the agency is making.</p>

<p><strong>Surveillance is everywhere, it is being practiced by the left, the right, and many foreign governments are also active in the West, collecting data on targets.</strong> So, this is not a uniquely German issue by any means. However, if the establishment in Germany becomes truly desperate, there is probably a secret report waiting that includes far more information and personal details than many Germans want to believe is possible.</p>

<p><a href="https://rmx.news/article/why-is-the-secret-german-spy-report-on-the-afd-party-only-filled-with-public-statements/"><em>Read more here...</em></a></p>
</div>

Title: Detection and Mitigation of Lateral Movement in Cloud Networks
Description: <h2 style="text-align: left;">How Hackers Bypass Lateral Movement Detection (And How to Stop Them)</h2>
<p>Detecting lateral movement has emerged as a crucial cybersecurity challenge today. Attackers who breach network perimeters follow a five-step process. They start with reconnaissance, move to their original compromise, spread laterally, establish persistence, and finally achieve their objectives. This systematic approach lets them quietly move through systems while they hunt for sensitive data and expand their control.</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">Security teams must understand hackers' techniques to spot lateral movement quickly. Attackers commonly use pass-the-hash attacks, remote execution, privilege escalation, Kerberoasting, and targeted phishing campaigns. Traditional security measures struggle to stop these sophisticated lateral movement techniques. Most organizations only spot breaches after attackers have caused substantial damage.</p>

Title:  鲍威尔：将重新评估2020版货币政策框架的“关键部分”，长期利率可能走高，“供应冲击”或成新常态 
Description:  <p>在周四的讲话中，美联储主席鲍威尔明确表示正在重新评估其货币政策框架的“关键部分”，包括通胀目标和就业“缺口”的处理方式。随着经济和政策不断变动，长期利率可能会走高。</p>
<p>鲍威尔表示，较高的实际利率可能反映了未来通胀可能比2010年代间歇期更加波动的可能性，称“供应冲击”将“更频繁且可能更持久”，这对经济和央行来说是一个困难的挑战。然而，华尔街日报知名记者、“新美联储通讯社”Nick Timiraos认为，这实际上与美联储目前设定利率的方式关系不大。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/f817ea45-3ed7-4d23-adac-fbdaf141ac95.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="553" data-wscnw="737"/></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements">
<h2 id="3e99817d">2020年框架已不适用</h2>
</div>
<p>当地时间周四，鲍威尔在美联储托马斯·劳巴赫(Thomas Laubach)研究会议上表示，美联储正在调整其货币政策框架，以应对2020年疫情后通胀和利率前景的重大变化。</p>
<p>他表示，2020年制定的政策框架是基于当时持续低利率和低通胀的环境，但当下经济条件已发生显著变化。</p>
<blockquote>
<p>我们将确保新的共识声明能够适应广泛的经济环境和发展。</p>
</blockquote>
<p>特别值得注意的是，鲍威尔明确指出“零利率下限约束不再是基础情景。”他表示，2020年疫情之后，通胀调整后的“实际”利率上升，可能会影响美联储当前框架的要素。</p>
<blockquote>
<p>较高的实际利率可能反映出通胀在未来可能比21世纪10年代危机间期更加不稳定的可能性。</p>
</blockquote>
<h2 id="1d9eca57">重新评估“缺口”概念：不再过度关注就业</h2>
<p>2020年框架将美联储的就业目标重点放在所谓的“缺口”上——即失业率过高的时期。这一变化实际上减少了美联储提前加息以冷却劳动力市场和防止通胀压力出现的做法。</p>
<p>鲍威尔周四解释说，这一调整并非永久放弃预防性政策举措或忽视劳动力市场紧张状况。</p>
<blockquote>
<p>它表明，表面上的劳动力市场紧张本身不足以触发政策反应，除非委员会认为如果不加以控制，将导致不受欢迎的通胀压力。</p>
</blockquote>
<h2 id="ce4778e">重新考虑“灵活平均通胀目标”</h2>
<p>2020年框架审查后，美联储采用了“灵活平均通胀目标”方法，允许通胀在长期低于2%后适度超过2%一段时间。批评者认为，这一框架过于针对当时的低利率、低通胀环境，并不适用于疫情后的经济状况。</p>
<p>对此，鲍威尔在演讲中表示：</p>
<blockquote>
<p>在我们的讨论中，与会者已表示他们认为重新考虑关于“缺口”的表述是合适的。在上周的会议上，我们对平均通胀目标也有类似的看法。</p>
<p>实际利率上升也可能反映出，未来通胀可能会比2010年代两次危机之间的时期更加波动。</p>
</blockquote>
<p>尽管框架正在修订，但鲍威尔重申了2%通胀目标的重要性：</p>
<blockquote>
<p>锚定预期对我们所做的一切至关重要，今天我们仍然完全致力于2%的目标。</p>
</blockquote>
<h2>长期利率可能走高，“供应冲击”或成新常态</h2>
<p>鲍威尔特别警告道：</p>
<blockquote>
<p>我们可能正在进入一个供应冲击更频繁、更持久的时期——这对经济和央行来说都是一个艰巨的挑战。</p>
</blockquote>
<p>这些关于“供应冲击”的言论与鲍威尔最近几周发表的警告相似，他曾多次提到政策变化可能使美联储陷入支持就业和控制通胀之间的艰难平衡。虽然鲍威尔在今天的讲话中没有提到特朗普的关税，但他最近已经指出，关税可能会减缓经济增长并推高通胀。</p>
<p>鲍威尔还表示，框架审查将关注沟通方式：</p>
<blockquote>
<p>在冲击更大、更频繁或更分散的时期，有效沟通要求我们传达围绕我们对经济和前景理解的不确定性。</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Timiraos分析认为，<strong>此次评估不太可能影响美联储目前设定利率的方式。</strong>鲍威尔表示，新框架将在“未来几个月”完成，这可能意味着他将在怀俄明州杰克逊霍尔(Jackson Hole)举行的美联储年度研讨会上概述这一政策。</p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  美国4月PPI同比上涨2.4%低于预期，环比-0.5%，降幅创下五年来最大! 
Description:  <p>周四，美国劳工统计局公布数据显示，美国4月PPI环比下降0.5%，降幅创下五年来最大，预期上涨0.2%，前值从-0.4%上修至0%，核心PPI环比下降0.4%，预期上涨0.3%，前值从-0.1%上修至0.4%。</p>
<p>PPI环比意外下降，主要原因是利润率下滑，这表明企业在一定程度上吸收了关税上涨带来的冲击。</p>
<p>美国4月PPI同比2.4%，好于预期的2.5%，前值2.7%，核心PPI同比3.1%持平预期，较前值3.3%小幅放缓。</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements">
<h2 id="eb84d88c">企业陷入定价两难困境</h2>
</div>
<p>数据表明，美国制造商和服务提供商目前正在避免将更高的美国进口关税传递给下游。尽管生产商正在感受到进口材料和其他投入品的激进关税带向，但对消费者的影响仍然温和。</p>
<p>商业领导者正在苦恼如何在不断变化的政策环境中最大程度地降低更高关税的影响。亚特兰大联邦储备银行最新的商业通胀预期调查显示，不到五分之一的企业表示，他们能够完全转嫁10%的成本增加。</p>
<p>一些企业一直在吸收部分额外成本，以避免在消费者对经济已感到不安的时期需求回落。消费者信心已经下滑，而周四发布的另一份报告显示，零售销售几乎没有增长。</p>
<p>汽车制造商Stellantis NV正在对其车辆提供折扣，而现代汽车公司则将价格保持稳定至6月。这些定价行动表明，一些最大的汽车制造商正试图缓解人们对进口汽车关税将使价格上涨数千美元的担忧。</p>
<p>同时，其他零售商预计购物者将经历更高的价格。沃尔玛在交付了一个销售和收入增长强劲的季度后，警告称关税和日益动荡的经济环境意味着该零售商预计将从本月开始提高一些价格。</p>
<p>对于正在提高价格的公司而言，这样做的风险是可能导致销售额下降。然而，不这样做则会对利润率构成风险。许多公司也在寻求其他方式削减成本或努力提高生产率。</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements">
<h2 id="370a67bb">食品、能源成本继续下降</h2>
</div>
<p>PPI报告显示，4月不含食品和能源的商品价格环比上涨0.4%，食品价格连续第二个月下降，鸡蛋成本下降超过39%，能源成本连续第三个月下降。</p>
<p>最终需求服务价格下降0.7%，为2009年有数据以来的最大降幅。超过40%的降幅归因于机械和车辆批发利润率的下降。</p>
<p>PPI一些组成部分用于计算美联储首选的通胀指标PCE物价指数。由于投资组合管理和机票价格下滑，这些类别大多转弱：医疗保健类别则有所上涨。</p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  沃尔玛Q1销售额增长2.5%略低于预期，CFO警告关税价格上涨可能从本月开始 | 财报见闻 
Description:  <p>美国经济的“晴雨表”沃尔玛第一季度净销售额增长2.5%至1656亿美元，略低于预期。美国可比销售增长4.5%，超过分析师预期的3.94%。</p>
<p>尽管销售表现强劲，但CFO警告，<strong>关税导致的价格上涨可能从本月开始。</strong>公司维持了2026财年的年度销售和利润预测不变。</p>
<p>15日，沃尔玛公布了截至4月30日的季度业绩：</p>
<blockquote>
<ul>
<li>沃尔玛一季度净销售额1656亿美元，同比增长2.5%（剔除汇率影响后增长4.0%），预估1660.2亿美元。</li>
<li>经营利润达71.4亿美元，同比增长4.3%。</li>
<li>毛利率为24.2%，上升12个基点。</li>
<li>第一季度GAAP每股收益0.56美元，调整后每股收益0.61美元，高于分析师平均预期的0.58美元。</li>
</ul>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/c5598e5c-f9aa-4261-805a-9322d4fd43d2.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="1171" data-wscnw="1457"/></p>
</blockquote>
<p>核心业务表现：</p>
<blockquote>
<ul>
<li>全球电商增长22%，主要受店内提货、配送和第三方平台的推动，电商对美国区可比销售的贡献率达到约350个基点。</li>
<li>美国市场可比销售额增长4.5%，这主要得益于健康及保健和杂货的强劲增长。</li>
<li>Sam&#39;s Club同店销售增长6.7%，交易量增长4.8%。会员收入增长9.6%，会员数量、续约率和Plus会员均实现稳健增长。</li>
<li>全球广告收入增长50%（包括新收购的VIZIO），美国本土的Walmart Connect广告业务增长31%（不含VIZIO）。</li>
</ul>
</blockquote>
<p><strong>沃尔玛维持了2026财年的年度销售和利润预测不变。</strong>公司继续预计截至2026年1月的财年调整后每股收益在2.50美元至2.60美元之间，年销售额增长在3%至4%之间。同时，预计第二季度合并净销售额增长在3.5%至4.5%之间，高于市场预期的3.46%。</p>
<p>作为美国最大的集装箱货物进口商，沃尔玛的财报一直被视为了解美国消费者健康状况和关税政策经济波动影响的重要窗口。沃尔玛CEO Doug McMillon在财报电话会议中直言：</p>
<blockquote>
<p>&#34;我们将尽最大努力保持低价，但考虑到关税的规模，即使是本周宣布的降低后的水平，考虑到零售业利润微薄的现实，我们也无法吸收所有压力。&#34;</p>
</blockquote>
<p>CFO John David Rainey在接受采访时表示：</p>
<blockquote>
<p>“目前零售业的经营环境充满挑战，价格上涨如此之快。历史上没有先例能与如此高、如此快的价格上涨相比。关税增加的幅度如此之大，零售商无法自行吸收这些成本。”</p>
</blockquote>
<h2>美国区：核心市场展现超强韧性</h2>
<p>作为公司最重要的市场，<strong>沃尔玛美国区表现强势，销售额达1122亿美元，同比增长3.2%，可比销售增长4.5%。</strong>尤为突出的是，健康与保健以及杂货类别表现出色，促使美国区运营利润增长7.0%至57亿美元。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/48cb0259-b1d0-4008-b696-f3818e00dfe8.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="450" data-wscnw="1457"/></p>
<p>沃尔玛比其他零售商更有能力应对各种挑战。<strong>公司的全球供应链使其能够从多个地区采购产品，而其规模意味着它可以与供应商谈判更好的交易条件。</strong></p>
<p>作为低价格的代名词，沃尔玛通常在经济困难时期表现良好，<strong>因为人们会倾向于寻求优惠。</strong>其数字化运营也给沃尔玛带来了优势。该零售商正通过其取货和配送服务吸引更多顾客，并吸引更多高收入购物者购买杂货、感冒药和婴儿产品等。</p>
<p>沃尔玛国际业务销售额298亿美元，按固定汇率计算增长7.8%，但运营利润下降17.5%至12.6亿美元。这一下滑主要是由于公司对Flipkart、Walmex和加拿大市场的战略性增长投资所致。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/e01d097f-6f67-4c3f-a776-01422ede3ffd.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="177" data-wscnw="870"/></p>
<h2>挑战与展望：经济不确定性下的前景</h2>
<p><strong>除了传统的零售业务外，沃尔玛正加速发展高利润率的数字业务</strong>，包括广告、会员服务和电商平台。这些业务不仅增长迅速，而且利润率远高于传统零售业务。</p>
<p>分析指出，美国消费者信心4月份连续第四个月下滑，表明消费者购买谨慎；与此同时，美国GDP在第一季度三年来首次收缩，引发了对经济衰退的担忧。在这种环境下，<strong>沃尔玛以日常低价策略销售必需品和杂货的定位虽然给公司带来了竞争优势，但也使其利润率维持在较低水平。</strong></p>
<p>CFO John David Rainey强调，鉴于当前经济环境的动态性和短期结果预测范围过于宽泛，公司选择不为第二季度提供特定的运营利润增长和EPS指引，但预计第二季度净销售额将增长3.5%-4.5%。</p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  恒瑞医药启动港股全球招股，近五年港股最大医药IPO来袭 
Description:  <p>2025年5月15日，A股创新药龙头企业恒瑞医药（600276.SH）正式启动H股全球公开发售，计划发行224,519,800股H股（假设超额配售权及发售量调整权未行使），发行价区间定为每股41.45-44.05港元。若全额行使超额配售权及发售量调整权，发行H股最高达296,927,200股，最高募资额可达130.8亿港元，这将成为近五年港股医药企业IPO最高募资额。</p>
<h2><strong>发行细节：时间紧凑，豪华基石团队加持</strong></h2>
<p>据了解，恒瑞医药H股香港公开发售将于5月20日结束，预计于22日前确定最终发行价，最快或于5月23日正式登陆港交所主板，实现&#34;A+H&#34;两地上市。此次发行由摩根士丹利、花旗及华泰国际担任联席保荐人。</p>
<p>值得关注的是，恒瑞医药此次IPO吸引了一众&#34;豪华基石投资天团&#34;的参与，包括新加坡政府投资公司（GIC）、景顺（Invesco）、瑞银全球资产管理集团（UBS-GAM）、高瓴资本、博裕资本等。据招股书，基石投资者按发售价认购或促使其指定实体认购可购入的若干数目的发售股份，以发行价中端计算，总金额逾41亿港元（5.33亿美元），认购金额占比达发行规模的43.04%（假设超额配售权及发售量调整权未行使）。</p>
<p>这些投资巨头的加持不仅彰显了国际资本对恒瑞医药的信心，也将在未来业务发展中起到重要作用。GIC作为全球最大主权财富基金之一，其国际视野和资源网络将有助于恒瑞拓展全球市场；景顺和UBS-GAM作为全球资产管理巨头，将提升恒瑞在国际投资者中的认可度；高瓴资本和博裕资本在医疗健康领域的深厚经验和产业资源，则有望为恒瑞的创新研发和商业化提供支持。</p>
<h2><strong>为何登陆港股？国际化战略的关键一步</strong></h2>
<p>赴香港上市对于恒瑞医药而言极为重要，是其出海战略的关键一步。首先，香港资本市场的国际投资者基础广泛，有助于提升公司在全球医药行业的品牌影响力。其次，本次上市可进一步优化资本结构并开拓新的融资渠道，为公司多元化融资提供助力。再者，上市有助于公司拓展海外业务和国际研发合作，增强国际布局，进一步实现海外市场的突破，提升公司的全球竞争力。</p>
<p>恒瑞医药的财务表现持续强劲。2024年，公司实现营业收入279.85亿元，同比增长22.63%；归属于上市公司股东的净利润63.37亿元，同比增长47.28%。2025年一季度，公司继续保持强劲增长势头，实现营业收入72.06亿元，同比增长20.14%；归属于上市公司股东的净利润18.74亿元，同比增长36.90%。公司研发投入同样可观，2024年累计研发投入82.28亿元，占销售收入比重达到29.40%，自2011年至今累计研发投入达460亿元。</p>
<h2><strong>折价19.3%发行</strong></h2>
<p>以恒瑞定价区间最高的44.05港元每股计算，对比过去十日的A股平均股价，H股发行价存在19.3%的折让。即使如此，恒瑞此次定价相较石药、中国生物制药等H股上市老牌药企，仍有明显的估值溢价。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/e9ec0841-95e7-42bf-8e28-3075d0049770.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="670" data-wscnw="1096"/></p>
<p>据wind数据，相较于过往医药行业6家募资额较大的A+H上市公司平均27.4%的折价，仍然映射出资本市场对于医药龙头的认可，同时也体现了恒瑞医药对自身价值的信心以及对未来市场发展的积极预期。</p>
<p>所得募集资金在扣除发行费用后，将用于研发计划；在中国和海外市场建设新的生产和研发设施，及扩大或升级在中国的现有生产设施；营运资金及其他一般企业用途等。</p>
<p>在全球创新药竞争日益激烈的背景下，恒瑞医药借助港股上市扩大国际影响力，进一步巩固其在中国创新药企业中的领军地位，同时加速国际化进程。对于中国创新药企业而言，这将是一个标志性事件，或将为更多有国际化雄心的中国药企提供借鉴。</p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p>

Title: Revolutionize textile recycling | Science
Description: The rapid rise in textile waste worldwide has brought growing attention to the environmental consequences of fast fashion. In 2015, the global textiles and clothing industry generated an estimated 92 million metric tons of waste (1), and projections suggest that this figure could increase by at least 50% by 2030 under a business-asusual scenario (2). Unsustainable waste management practices, such as landfilling, have exacerbated environmental challenges, contributing to the release of micro- and nanoplastics as well as per- and polyfluoroalkyl substances (PFAS) into ecosystems (3, 4). The textile industry urgently needs sustainable interventions that will promote a circular economy.

class="bbc-j1srjl" style="padding-bottom:56.26%;overflow:hidden"><img src="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/660/cpsprodpb/0439/live/6cf66250-3126-11f0-8947-7d6241f9fce9.jpg.webp" srcset="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/70/cpsprodpb/0439/live/6cf66250-3126-11f0-8947-7d6241f9fce9.jpg.webp 70w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/95/cpsprodpb/0439/live/6cf66250-3126-11f0-8947-7d6241f9fce9.jpg.webp 95w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/144/cpsprodpb/0439/live/6cf66250-3126-11f0-8947-7d6241f9fce9.jpg.webp 144w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/183/cpsprodpb/0439/live/6cf66250-3126-11f0-8947-7d6241f9fce9.jpg.webp 183w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/240/cpsprodpb/0439/live/6cf66250-3126-11f0-8947-7d6241f9fce9.jpg.webp 240w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/320/cpsprodpb/0439/live/6cf66250-3126-11f0-8947-7d6241f9fce9.jpg.webp 320w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/660/cpsprodpb/0439/live/6cf66250-3126-11f0-8947-7d6241f9fce9.jpg.webp 660w" alt="中國一家空氣氣炸鍋工廠的女工" loading="lazy" style="aspect-ratio:2835 / 1595" class="bbc-139onq"></div></div><div class="bbc-6cb6xm"><div class="bbc-1nw71o6"><a href="https://www.bbc.com/zhongwen/articles/cvg7lx4lnyeo/trad" data-static-ati-click="https://a1.api.bbc.co.uk/hit.xiti?s=598342&amp;s2=38&amp;p=zhongwen.articles.cgr5ng92l5zo.trad.page&amp;atc=PUB-[article]-[midarticle-mostread]-[]-[]-[zhongwen.articles.cgr5ng92l5zo.trad.page]-[]-[]-[]&amp;type=AT" class="bbc-7tw9s9">中美貿易戰「停火」：中國工廠復工的時機，還是尋找新巿場的喘息空間？</a></div></div></div></li></ul><p tabindex="-1" id="end-of-recommendations" class="bbc-10a2avq eveec6k0">End of 熱讀</p></div></section><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">在5月10日中美在日內瓦經貿會談拉開帷幕前，市場已形成明確預期：持續緊張的兩國經貿關係將迎來緩和，雙方會通過互相降低關稅打破此前超過100%的畸高稅率局面——美國可能將對華加徵關稅回調至「對等關稅」 剛提出時34%的水平，再疊加因芬太尼問題加徵的20%，總稅率或維持在54%；中國則可能同步將對美關稅降至34%。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">然而5月12日公佈的《中美日內瓦經貿會談聯合聲明》帶來超出預期——美國不僅撤回了4月2日之後實施的多輪累計91%的報復性關稅，還將4月2日設定的34%「對等關稅」 中的24%暫停執行90天，實際生效的 「對等關稅」 暫時降至10%。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">作為回應，中國同步調整稅委會公告，將對美加徵關稅從34%下調至10%，同樣暫停 24%的關稅措施。這意味著在90天緩衝期內，兩國關稅水平被大幅拉低至 「對等 10%」 的基準線，顯著緩解了此前劍拔弩張的貿易對峙氛圍。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">這就形成了中美關稅從「145%驟降至10%」的印象。但如果仔細測算，實際關稅其實非常高。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">除了基準層面保留10% 的 「對等關稅」 外，爭議層面則延續了以芬太尼問題為由加徵的20%關稅，這使得特朗普上任後，對華關稅新增了30%。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">但這還沒算特朗普第一任期所加關稅，當時他依據 「301 條款」 加徵的四輪關稅（前三輪25%、第四輪7.5%），但不是針對所有商品。美國智庫彼得森國際經濟研究所（PIIE）測算，2020年初美國對華平均加權關稅稅率為19.3%，但伴隨中國對美出口佔比下降以及出口商品類別調整，到2024年底加權平均關稅為10.7%。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">這意味著，美國對華目前關稅大致為40.7%；投行高盛測算，再綜合各類調整及半導體等行業的關稅豁免美國對華實際有效關稅稅率為39%。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">這也處在特朗普第一任期從未達到的高關稅水平。高盛認為，大幅39%的對華關稅，將拖累中國經濟增速減少0.8的百分點。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">在非關稅領域同樣也不是「壁壘全消」，中方暫停或取消了4月出台的7類中重稀土出口管制，但繼續維持2月實施的鎢、碲、鉍等關鍵礦物出口限制，以及2024年12月針對鎵、鍺、銻等兩用物項的管制措施。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">此外，美方「小額包裹」的關稅此前從「豁免」變為120%，5月14日聯合聲明後將變為54%，改為按價值或按件徵收（5月25美元 / 件，6 月起50美元 / 件），雖未直接影響大宗商品貿易，卻增加了跨境電商等細分領域的運營成本。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">ING銀行大中華區首席經濟師宋林向BBC中文表示，關稅降至目前水平，足以讓貿易基本回歸正常狀態——在這一水平，出口商、進口商和消費者將共同分擔關稅影響，整體商業活動有望恢復。回顧今年第一季度，20%-30%關稅水平下，對美出口同比增長約5%，儘管存在貿易提前囤貨的因素。</p></div><figure class="bbc-1qn0xuy"><div class="bbc-j1srjl" style="padding-bottom:56.22%"><img src="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/640/cpsprodpb/4444/live/ee4f08d0-317f-11f0-96c3-cf669419a2b0.jpg.webp" srcset="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/240/cpsprodpb/4444/live/ee4f08d0-317f-11f0-96c3-cf669419a2b0.jpg.webp 240w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/320/cpsprodpb/4444/live/ee4f08d0-317f-11f0-96c3-cf669419a2b0.jpg.webp 320w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/480/cpsprodpb/4444/live/ee4f08d0-317f-11f0-96c3-cf669419a2b0.jpg.webp 480w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/624/cpsprodpb/4444/live/ee4f08d0-317f-11f0-96c3-cf669419a2b0.jpg.webp 624w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/800/cpsprodpb/4444/live/ee4f08d0-317f-11f0-96c3-cf669419a2b0.jpg.webp 800w" sizes="(min-width: 1008px) 760px, 100vw" alt="青島港的貨車" loading="lazy" width="900" height="506" style="aspect-ratio:900 / 506" class="bbc-139onq"><p class="bbc-1276odk" role="text"><span class="bbc-m04vo2">圖像來源，</span><span lang="en-GB">Getty Images</span></p></div></figure><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><h2 id="關鍵產品芯片還是芯片" tabindex="-1" class="bbc-1mewxu4 eglt09e0">關鍵產品：芯片，還是芯片</h2></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">中美之間的貿易，芯片是討論焦點——一方面，美國對中國半導體的關稅，並沒有隨著這次談判而顯著下調；另一方面，美國對中國實施嚴格的高端芯片禁令，而中國對美國產品有需求，尤其是高科技產品，但面對美國的禁運，無法有效實施。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">此前，特朗普已經豁免了半導體、智能手機、筆記本電腦等品類加徵的「對等關稅」。不過，2025年2月至3月，美國以芬太尼問題為由對中國加徵20%的關稅，疊加自2025年1月開始對華半導體徵收的50%關稅，目前美國對華半導體徵收的關稅達到70%。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">2018年其從中國進口半導體芯片價值38.8億美元，佔美國半導體芯片整體進口額的10.33%；2024年已經降至20.9億美元，份額降至4.49%。因此，2025年以來升至70%關稅的邊際影響相對有限。70%的稅率還在進一步壓低這一份額，今年3月，從中國進口的半導體金額約佔美國整體半導體進口額的3%-4%，相比去年同期未發生顯著變化。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">而受到影響的，不少是美國企業，比如AMD、英特爾、美光、三星等外資企業在中國完成部分工序回運美國加工、銷售，面臨著不小的額外成本支出。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">一位在深圳從事芯片業務的貿易商向BBC中文表示，過去幾年，中國輸美的芯片量已經很少了，以前中國在中低端芯片、傳感器，有成本優勢，美國在高端芯片有技術優勢，現在這兩種優勢都被打斷，沒法發揮出來。「未來90天內生意繼續做，馬照跑，就是訂單不一定會很激進，一個怕訂單太大風險太大，後續付款項也會有問題；一個怕下單太多，本地的需求下行而堵庫存。」</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">雖然對華芯片關稅還居高不下，但美國高端芯片的出口禁令正在鬆動。背後是特朗普和拜登的不同策略傾向——特朗普執著於貿易平衡，降低貿易赤字，拜登則執著於建「小院高牆」，聯合盟友圍堵中國。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">今年1月13日，即將卸任的美國前總統拜登發佈《人工智能擴散規則》，限制部分高算力的先進GPU的出口，而且限制範圍從過去的個別實體或國家，擴大到全世界，即無論出口到全球哪個國家，都將需要美國的許可，只是待遇不同——將全球劃分為：第一層級的17個國家及台灣可無限制獲得AI芯片；第二層級的約120個國家須遵守芯片數量上限；第三層級則將中國、俄羅斯、伊朗、朝鮮等列為禁區，完全禁止進口這些高端器件。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">該計劃原本會在5月15日正式生效，但就在中美談判後第二天，美國商務部下屬的工業與安全局（BIS）的副部長傑弗里·凱斯勒（Jeffery Kessler）表示，已指示BIS執法人員不要執行《人工智能擴散規則》，因為他不僅會扼殺美國的創新，還會給企業增加繁重的監管負擔，還可能將許多國家降為次級地位，破壞美國與這些國家的外交關係。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">該部門還公告稱，已經啓動程序，著手廢除這一規則，並將在未來發佈新的替代規則。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">路透社援引知情人士稱，廢棄這一分層模式，轉而採用基於政府間協議的全球許可制度，若以政府對政府的模式取代現有等級體系，更契合特朗普總統「與個別國家單獨達成交易」的整體貿易思路，也便於美國將出口美國設計的AI芯片作為其他談判的籌碼。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">美國商務部長霍華德·盧特尼克在3月一次公開場合亦明確表示，希望將出口管制議題納入雙邊貿易談判。</p></div><figure class="bbc-1qn0xuy"><div class="bbc-j1srjl" style="padding-bottom:56.22%"><img src="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/640/cpsprodpb/06b6/live/55c19410-3180-11f0-8947-7d6241f9fce9.jpg.webp" srcset="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/240/cpsprodpb/06b6/live/55c19410-3180-11f0-8947-7d6241f9fce9.jpg.webp 240w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/320/cpsprodpb/06b6/live/55c19410-3180-11f0-8947-7d6241f9fce9.jpg.webp 320w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/480/cpsprodpb/06b6/live/55c19410-3180-11f0-8947-7d6241f9fce9.jpg.webp 480w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/624/cpsprodpb/06b6/live/55c19410-3180-11f0-8947-7d6241f9fce9.jpg.webp 624w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/800/cpsprodpb/06b6/live/55c19410-3180-11f0-8947-7d6241f9fce9.jpg.webp 800w" sizes="(min-width: 1008px) 760px, 100vw" alt="集裝箱和中國國旗" loading="lazy" width="900" height="506" style="aspect-ratio:900 / 506" class="bbc-139onq"><p class="bbc-1276odk" role="text"><span class="bbc-m04vo2">圖像來源，</span><span lang="en-GB">Getty Images</span></p></div></figure><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><h2 id="示範效應印歐日都有強硬表態" tabindex="-1" class="bbc-1mewxu4 eglt09e0">示範效應：印歐日都有強硬表態</h2></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">中美在日內瓦經貿會談結束後，國際社會的目光迅速聚焦於談判成果對全球貿易格局的後續。作為美國傳統盟友的日本與歐盟，以及新興經濟體印度，分別以不同姿態回應這場牽動世界經濟神經的博弈。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">在亞洲，日本展現出謹慎而強硬的姿態。在中美發布聯合聲明的當天，日本首相石破茂在日本眾議院預算委員會會議上說，不能接受在不包含汽車領域的情況下與美方達成協議，也不會為了汽車產業而犧牲農業、以擴大進口美國大米作為談判籌碼。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">由於日本是美國的忠實盟友，這使得石破茂相對強硬的表態，引發關注和討論。日本財務省數據顯示，2024年日美貿易逆差達600多億美元，其中汽車及零部件佔逆差總額的 62%。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">與此同時，美國總統特朗普在中美聯合聲明發佈數小時後，迅速將貿易戰的矛頭轉向歐洲。同樣是在中美髮布聯合聲明的當天，特朗普在白宮記者會上突然將矛頭轉向歐盟，宣稱「 歐盟在貿易上的做法比中國更惡劣」，並威脅將對歐盟汽車啓動 「301 調查」。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">這一言論立即引發歐盟委員會的強烈反應。歐盟委員會貿易發言人奧洛夫·吉爾（Olof Gill）表示，歐盟堅決反對任何不合理的貿易壁壘和單邊關稅措施，強調歐盟將採取一切必要手段保護自身企業和消費者的利益。他指出，歐盟始終主張通過對話和談判解決分歧，反對單邊主義，但絕不會容忍不公平的貿易做法。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">而在南亞次大陸，印度一直被美國視作在該區域制衡中國的盟友，但在特朗普的關稅攻擊中同樣「中槍」。中美聯合聲明發佈數小時後，印度常駐世界貿易組織（WTO）代表向爭端解決機構提交文件，擬對部分美國商品加徵報復性關稅，以此回應美國以「保障措施」為由對印度鋼鋁產品徵收的25%關稅。印度強調，這一反制措施旨在通過「實質等效」的貿易調整，平衡美方舉措造成的經濟損失。彭博社形容，這是印度首次提出反制美關稅政策的舉措。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">前美國財政部長勞倫斯·薩默斯（Lawrence Summers）在接受媒體採訪時表示，「很明顯，特朗普先眨眼了」，並認為中國在未改變核心政策的情況下迫使美國妥協，這一案例可能鼓勵其他國家在貿易談判中採取更堅定的立場。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">華盛頓戰略與國際研究中心（CSIS）專家菲利普·A·勒克（Philip A. Luck ）表示，美國政府曾警告貿易報復將帶來後果，但中國的反制使其實際關稅水平降回去了，這削弱了美國政府「能夠通過不斷升級獲勝」的立場，損害了美國的信譽。缺乏一致性和持續執行的威脅式貿易政策不僅無效，反而適得其反，危害美國的戰略目標和普通民眾利益。若未來政府為恢復信譽而盲目執行威脅，後果難料。</p></div></main><p><strong><a href="https://blockads.fivefilters.org">Adblock test</a></strong> <a href="https://blockads.fivefilters.org/acceptable.html">(Why?)</a></p>

Title: 俄烏三年多來首次會談：澤連斯基難見普京，前線士兵對割地可能感痛心

e1p3vdyi0">俄烏三年多來首次會談：澤連斯基難見普京，前線士兵對割地可能感痛心</h1></div><figure class="bbc-1qn0xuy"><div class="bbc-j1srjl" style="padding-bottom:56.26%"><img class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">但普京並未出現在克里姆林宮公布的名單中，這意味着他不會出席週四的談判。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">2019年12月以來普京與澤連斯基未有親身會晤。兩國上一次進行直接談判是在2022年3月，地點也是伊斯坦布爾，那時莫斯科剛對烏克蘭發動全面入侵不久。</p></div><section aria-label="廣告 2" aria-hidden="true" role="region" data-e2e="advertisement" e17g058b0">美國預計將派出高層代表團出席此次談判。美國國務卿盧比奧（Marco Rubio）於週三抵達土耳其，預計將於週四與北約外長們會面。</p></div><figure class="bbc-1qn0xuy"><div class="bbc-j1srjl" style="padding-bottom:56.43%"><img https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/320/cpsprodpb/5a2b/live/66777630-315d-11f0-8947-7d6241f9fce9.png.webp 320w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/624/cpsprodpb/5a2b/live/66777630-315d-11f0-8947-7d6241f9fce9.png.webp 624w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/684/cpsprodpb/5a2b/live/66777630-315d-11f0-8947-7d6241f9fce9.png.webp 684w" sizes="(min-width: 1008px) 760px, 100vw" alt="上週日，普京在深夜提出15日於土耳其伊斯坦布爾與烏克蘭進行和平談判。" loading="lazy" width="684" height="386" style="aspect-ratio:684 / 386" class="bbc-139onq"><p class="bbc-1276odk" role="text"><span class="bbc-m04vo2">圖像來源，</span><span lang="en-GB">EPA</span></p></div></figure><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><h2 id="前線戰事仍在持續" tabindex="-1" class="bbc-1mewxu4 eglt09e0">前線戰事仍在持續</h2></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">烏克蘭無人機正在東部城市波克羅夫斯克（Pokrovsk）郊區上空盤旋，這裡是烏克蘭交戰最激烈的前線之一。現場畫面透過螢幕即時傳送，一條巨大的煙柱正在升騰。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">幾秒前，烏克蘭的火炮襲擊了俄軍陣地，BBC記者看到俄軍士兵在行動，正試圖向通往波克羅夫斯克的關鍵道路推進。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">至少有一名俄軍士兵在襲擊中受傷，甚至可能喪命。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">現場畫面令人不寒而慄，也凸顯出這場由俄羅斯發動的戰爭的血腥代價。迄今為止，已有數十萬人喪生，正如美國總統特朗普所形容，這是一場「永無止境的血腥屠殺」。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">記者所在的是一棟鄉村房屋，現已改建成烏克蘭陸軍第155機械化旅的指揮中心，距離前線炮兵陣地僅有數英里。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">螢幕上顯示民宅與建築被夷為平地，這樣的破壞程度遠超記者六個月前所見。這些都是過去數月，烏軍為捍衛波克羅夫斯克而浴血奮戰的證明，這裡是頓涅茨克（Donetsk）的重要交通樞紐。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">儘管一再目睹停火希望破滅，即使是向來懷疑的士兵們，本週也開始對這場戰事出現審慎樂觀。美國、歐洲、土耳其等方的外交努力，促使俄羅斯與烏克蘭三年多來首次展開直接對話。</p></div><figure class="bbc-1qn0xuy"><div class="bbc-j1srjl" style="padding-bottom:56.25%"><img src="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/640/cpsprodpb/c1c0/live/466f3440-30cc-11f0-96c3-cf669419a2b0.jpg.webp" srcset="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/240/cpsprodpb/c1c0/live/466f3440-30cc-11f0-96c3-cf669419a2b0.jpg.webp 240w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/320/cpsprodpb/c1c0/live/466f3440-30cc-11f0-96c3-cf669419a2b0.jpg.webp 320w, width="4032" height="2268" style="aspect-ratio:4032 / 2268" class="bbc-139onq"></div></figure><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">37歲的尤里（Yurii）在俄羅斯全面入侵前，曾在科技公司工作。他說：「他們（俄羅斯與烏克蘭）必須開始對話。我們這些士兵都希望戰爭結束。但要記住，戰爭不是我們開始的，所以我們也無法單方面終止。」</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">他抬頭望向螢幕，又發現俄軍士兵在移動。他與同袍迅速計算出座標，並通報給炮兵單位。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">記者從指揮中心出發，行駛泥濘的鄉間小路、穿越一片遼闊的田野前往炮兵陣地。泥土塊飛濺，車輛在濕滑路面上顛簸搖晃。車輛必須全速前進，以減少受到無人機攻擊的風險。自2023年大量部署以來，無人機大幅提高了俄烏雙方的傷亡率。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">戰爭科技也持續演進。現在又出現一種新威脅——在飛行過程中會釋放光纖纜線的無人機。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">「我們無法偵測或干擾這類無人機，所以現場可能潛藏著比我們預想更多的無人機。」尤里說。</p></div><figure class="bbc-1qn0xuy"><div class="bbc-j1srjl" style="padding-bottom:94.37%"><img src="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/640/cpsprodpb/1706/live/b875b9a0-3190-11f0-8519-3b5a01ebe413.png.webp" srcset="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/240/cpsprodpb/1706/live/b875b9a0-3190-11f0-8519-3b5a01ebe413.png.webp 240w, height="1206" style="aspect-ratio:1278 / 1206" class="bbc-139onq"></div></figure><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><h2 id="割地求和「讓人心痛」" tabindex="-1" class="bbc-1mewxu4 eglt09e0">割地求和「讓人心痛」</h2></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">記者駛入被樹木與灌木遮掩的炮兵陣地時，士兵們已開始裝彈了。這是來自法國製造名叫「凱撒」（Caesar）的自走炮，自戰爭爆發以來，烏軍已部署數十門，法國也在努力提高產量。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">「我被它的精準度驚訝，而且我們可以轉換使用多種彈藥。最重要的是，它部署速度快，遠比我過去使用的蘇聯製的古老裝備有效得多。」科扎克說。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">烏軍士兵發射了四輪炮彈，每一發都震耳欲聾。周圍不時傳來敵軍炮彈落下的聲音。戰鬥仍在激烈進行。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">「如你所聽，敵軍的攻勢一波接一波。我們需要大量彈藥來壓制他們。我們希望國際夥伴能盡可能多地供應彈藥，否則我們一旦必須挑選優先與非優先目標，敵人就會得手。」科扎克說。</p></div><div dir="ltr" class="bbc-19j92fr ebmt73l0"><p dir="ltr" class="bbc-w2hm1d e17g058b0">記者問這些士兵，他們對於外界認為烏克蘭應做出讓步、甚至割地求和的看法。</p></div><figure class="bbc-1qn0xuy"><div class="bbc-j1srjl" style="padding-bottom:56.25%"><img src="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/640/cpsprodpb/dcc7/live/d9c5c5b0-30e0-11f0-8519-3b5a01ebe413.jpg.webp" srcset="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/240/cpsprodpb/dcc7/live/d9c5c5b0-30e0-11f0-8519-3b5a01ebe413.jpg.webp 240w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/ws/480/cpsprodpb/dcc7/live/d9c5c5b0-30e0-11f0-8519-3b5a01ebe413.jpg.webp 480w,
