<blockquote>
<p>“我们很早以前就学到了一课，把所有东西都放在一个地方风险太大。”</p>
</blockquote>
<p>此外，库克还表示，苹果正在从美国采购玻璃和Face ID模块，同时从12个州购买190亿块芯片。</p>
<p>他预估，关税将导致公司第三财季(4-6月)将额外增加9亿美元(约合65.4亿元人民币)成本，他暗示未来几个季度这一数字可能会更高。苹果拒绝透露是否会涨价，或者是否把成本转嫁给消费者。</p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  海湖庄园协议魅影！新台币之后，下一个是韩元？ 
Description:  <p data-pm-slice="1 1 []">特朗普政府外汇政策转向冲击亚洲货币市场，韩元可能是下一个大幅走强的主角。</p>
<p data-pm-slice="1 1 []">据追风交易台消息，野村证券在5月14日的报告中表示，目前韩元有升值潜力。根据野村模型，韩元被低估了约 12%，在新兴市场和G10货币中属于 “最被低估” 的之一（仅次于新台币和日元）。若韩国国家养老金（NPS）提高外汇对冲比例，则对韩元的需求将大大上升。投资者应密切关注韩美外汇磋商进展及即将到来的&#34;7月经贸方案&#34;，做好美元/韩元可能迅速下行至1300水平的准备。</p>
<h2 data-pm-slice="1 1 []">从贸易战到货币战？</h2>
<p>据<a href="https://www.cnfin.com/hs-lb/detail/20250514/4233163_1.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">新华财经</a>14日报道，一位韩国政府官员表示，<strong>韩国财政部副部长崔智英于5月5日会见了美国财政部负责国际金融事务的助理部长Robert Kaproth，双方就美元兑韩元市场进行了讨论。</strong>两人是在意大利米兰举行的第58届亚洲开发银行（ADB）年会期间会面的。</p>
<p>这引发了市场猜测，即特朗普政府可能倾向于美元走弱，并将汇率问题作为即将到来的贸易谈判的重要内容。</p>
<p data-pm-slice="1 1 []">野村证券认为，韩美关于汇率讨论的报道进一步支持了韩国央行行长李柱烈此前的言论，即美国对亚洲国家施加了货币升值压力。而韩国财政部长崔相穆已经强调，<strong>韩国将针对贸易问题准备一份 “7月方案”。</strong></p>
<p data-pm-slice="1 1 []">在亚洲范围内，日本财务大臣加藤可能与贝森特会面讨论汇率问题的报道，也提升了市场对亚洲货币升值的预期。尽管加藤可能反驳市场关于美国施压日本让日元升值的言论，但如果有迹象表明汇率是贸易讨论的一部分，亚洲货币升值的风险将呈现不对称性。</p>
<h2 data-pm-slice="1 1 []"><strong>韩元升值有其基本面因素</strong></h2>
<p data-pm-slice="1 1 []">野村认为，尽管美国施压可能是推动韩元升值的主要因素，基本面方面也存在支持韩元升值的理由。</p>
<p data-pm-slice="1 1 []">野村基本均衡汇率（FEER）、购买力平价（基于 CPI 的 PPP）、实际有效汇率（REER）和经生产率调整的实际有效汇率（REER）模型均显示韩元持续被低估，<strong>整体上韩元被低估了约 12%。</strong></p>
<p data-pm-slice="1 1 []"><strong>韩元也是新兴市场和 G10 货币中被低估最严重的货币之一，亚洲地区另外两种被严重低估的货币是新台币和日元。</strong></p>
<p data-pm-slice="1 1 []">与此同时，韩国国家养老金服务（NPS）可能增加外汇对冲。NPS 可轻松将其海外投资的战略外汇对冲比例提升至 10%。<strong>截至2025年2月，其海外投资额为4970亿美元，这意味着可能有497亿美元的潜在外汇出售。</strong></p>
<p data-pm-slice="1 1 []">野村警告，<strong>需要警惕外国投资抛售 / 汇回或外汇对冲的风险。如果韩元大幅升值的预期增强，可能存在其他加强韩元的资金流入来源。</strong></p>
<p data-pm-slice="1 1 []">据野村估计，截至2025年5月9日，韩国散户的海外投资总额为1390亿美元，且已有迹象表明，由于美国例外论褪色和对美元走弱的担忧，他们正在抛售海外资产（主要是股票）。</p>
<p data-pm-slice="1 1 []">另一个风险是，资产管理规模达1.3 万亿美元（截至2024年底，约合180.2万亿韩元）的资管行业，其外国持股约为 1530 亿美元（21.4 万亿韩元），实际资金管理者可能增加外汇对冲（卖出美元），这可能进一步推高韩元。</p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  吉利汽车Q1营收、净利双双创新高，新能源业务爆发 | 财报见闻 
Description:  <p>吉利汽车Q1营收、净利润同比均实现增长，其中净利润更是大增超两倍，汽车销量创历史新高，新能源业务全面爆发。</p>
<p>5月15日，吉利汽车公布一季度财报显示，</p>
<blockquote>
<p>营收72.95亿元，同比增25%，去年同期582.25亿元；</p>
<p>税前利润为66.83亿元人民币，同比增长324%；</p>
<p>归母净利润56.72亿元，同比增264%，去年同期15.60亿元；</p>
<p>毛利总额大幅提升至114亿元，毛利率达15.8%。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/6d557caf-26b1-489f-bf43-d40c0dad51a6.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="708" data-wscnw="675"/></p>
</blockquote>
<p>吉利汽车在公告中表示，Q1销量创下历史最高，新能源业务强劲增长，规模效应突显，带来盈利能力大幅提升。</p>
<p>与此同时，作为吉利汽车集团重要组成部分，极氪汽车今天公布财报显示，亏损显著收窄。本月早些时候，吉利宣布计划将高端电动汽车品牌<span style="color: #1482f0;"><a style="color: #1482f0;" href="https://wallstreetcn.com/articles/3746621" target="_blank" rel="noopener">极氪私有化</a></span>。</p>
<p>截止发稿，吉利汽车港股上涨0.42%，报19.22港元/股，今年迄今，吉利汽车累计涨幅近30%。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/14386d5d-01e1-45cb-80cb-aaa4ef60289d.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="408" data-wscnw="804"/></p>
<h2>新能源业务全面爆发，盈利能力大幅改善</h2>
<p>财报显示，一季度，吉利汽车销量达到70.38万辆，同比增长48%，创下历史新高。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/8d402121-628d-4121-a494-cc6269565ffe.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="181" data-wscnw="650"/></p>
<p>新能源业务表现尤为亮眼，吉利新能源产品（含吉利、领克、极氪）一季度销量达33.9万辆，其中银河品牌销量达到26万辆，同比增长214%。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/fcd7a823-d264-4a64-a836-d8b346300e73.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="896" data-wscnw="674"/></p>
<p>根据吉利汽车公告，新能源业务盈利能力全面改善，规模效应开始显现，这是推动整体净利润大幅提升的关键因素之一。</p>
<p>财报还显示，一季度研发费用达33.28亿元，同比增加24.6%，显示其持续加码技术投入。</p>
<h2>极氪表现强势，扭亏为盈成为新增长点</h2>
<p>作为吉利汽车的重要子公司，极氪在一季度交出了一份出色的答卷。据Auto有范儿， 5月15日，极氪科技发布2025年一季度财报。据财报披露：</p>
<blockquote>
<p>极氪科技一季度总营收达220亿元。其中，整车销售收入191亿元，同比增长16.1%；一季度整车毛利率16.5%，同比上升3.4个百分点；综合毛利率攀升至19.1%，创历史最高；第一季度极氪科技净亏损大幅收窄，同比降低超60%。</p>
</blockquote>
<p>这表明极氪有望走出此前的亏损周期，为吉利汽车集团贡献更多利润。</p>
<p>本月早些时候，吉利宣布计划将高端电动汽车品牌极氪私有化，一年前在纽约上市的极氪目前估值约为64亿美元。</p>
<h2>完成领克收购，战略布局更加清晰</h2>
<p>财报显示，吉利汽车在今年二月完成了对领克汽车的控股权收购。</p>
<p>通过此次交易，吉利与沃尔沃共同持有的领克由之前的合营企业转变为吉利汽车的非全资子公司。</p>
<p>收购完成后，极氪通过其子公司浙江极氪持有领克51%股权，而吉利汽车另一附属公司持有49%股权。</p>
<p>这一战略性收购使吉利能够进一步整合资源，增强在豪华和高端市场的竞争力，同时加强与沃尔沃的协同效应。</p>
<h2>面临的挑战：流动负债和未来增长持续性</h2>
<p>尽管业绩亮眼，财报显示吉利汽车仍面临一些挑战。</p>
<p>财报显示，截至3月31日，公司流动负债净值为112.51亿元，这一数字较去年年末的108.18亿元有所增加。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/14e22560-5c70-44ae-b291-f7cdbc3cfa00.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="403" data-wscnw="629"/></p>
<p>不过，公司董事会认为这不会对持续经营能力产生重大影响，理由是公司业务持续产生稳定现金流、与多家金融机构保持良好关系且有备用融资安排，同时管理层已制定改善流动性的具体计划。</p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  油价大跌3%！伊朗称愿与美国达成协议 
Description:  <p>市场担忧伊朗可能达成核协议，地缘政治缓和继续推动石油供应前景宽松。周四，国际油价短线走低，WTI原油和布油均跌超3%。</p>
<p>据<a href="https://www.thepaper.cn/newsDetail_forward_30821068" target="_blank" rel="noopener">澎湃新闻</a>，伊朗最高领袖哈梅内伊的一位高级顾问14日向美媒透露，伊朗准备在一定条件下与美国总统特朗普签署核协议，以换取解除经济制裁。据媒体报道，特朗普15日称，<strong>与伊朗达成协议的距离非常接近。</strong></p>
<p>受此消息影响，布伦特原油价格跌破每桶65美元，此前一天已下跌0.8%。西德克萨斯中质原油（WTI）交易价格报60.78美元/桶。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/15dc2053-5126-4fb5-b8a5-63a909a61538.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="1070" data-wscnw="1577"/></p>
<p>油价下跌也受到美国原油库存增加的影响。政府数据显示，<strong>美国原油库存增幅创下自3月以来之最，终结了此前连续四天的上涨行情。</strong></p>
<h2>伊朗核协议预期引发油价下跌</h2>
<p>据参考消息援引路透社5月14日报道，伊朗最高领袖哈梅内伊的顾问阿里·沙姆哈尼在美国全国广播公司14日发布的采访中表示，伊朗愿与美国达成协议，以换取美国解除对伊经济制裁。</p>
<p>今年以来原油价格下跌超过13%。美国生产商表示，预计在年底前油价不会有太大变化。<strong>如果伊朗供应增加，可能会加剧今年晚些时候的潜在供应过剩。</strong></p>
<p>此前，<a href="https://wallstreetcn.com/articles/3747100?keyword=OPEC" target="_blank" rel="noopener">石油输出国组织（OPEC）</a>及其盟友上个月开始恢复自2022年以来暂停的供应。根据周三发布的月度报告，该组织4月份仅增加了25000桶/日的产量，远低于此前计划的138000桶/日。该联盟将在6月1日的会议上考虑进一步增产。</p>
<p>Chaos Ternary Futures Co. 旗下研究机构的分析师Zhou Mi表示：</p>
<blockquote>
<p>“原油仍处于中长期下跌趋势，<strong>OPEC+增产和地缘政治缓和继续推动供应前景宽松。</strong>” </p>
</blockquote>
<p>他认为，关税紧张关系缓解可能暂时提振燃料需求，进而提高炼油利润率，从而限制原油的下跌空间。</p>
<p>值得关注的是，<strong>汽油正在显露出强劲迹象。</strong>纽约即期价差（即两个最近到期合约之间的差价）接近五个月来的最高点。这种“现货升水”现象（即近期价格高于远期价格）被视为对需求的利好信号。</p>
<p>国际能源署（IEA）是消费国的重要顾问机构，其发布的供需预测比OPEC的预测更受石油交易者的关注。 <strong>IEA将于周四晚些时候发布最新的供需预估，</strong>市场将密切关注该报告，以研判原油供需的未来走向。</p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  一周两次上调中国股市目标价！高盛：沪深300还有17%上涨空间 
Description:  <p style="text-align: left;">贸易缓和带动市场反弹，高盛一周内两次上调中国股市目标价，重回4月2日前预测水平。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">据追风交易台消息，由于关税谈判情况超预期，截止5月14日，中国股市已完全收复4月2日前的跌幅，MSCI中国、沪深300和恒生科技指数较4月初高点上涨2-4%。</p>
<p>相应地，<strong>高盛维持对中国股票的超配评级，将中国股市12个月目标价调整至4月2日前预测水平，MSCI中国和沪深300指数目标分别为84和4600点，隐含11%和17%的上行空间。</strong>此前，高盛经济学家上调了美国和中国GDP增长预期。</p>
<p>值得一提的是，这是高盛在不到一周内第二次上调指数目标，此前在4月初因相互加征关税曾两次下调目标价。</p>
<p><img class="wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/9e38dd6b-8d89-4c2d-8a75-9c104b6baaee.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="473" data-wscnw="577" data-wscnsize="48130"/></p>
<h2 style="text-align: left;">关税降低带动市场回暖，股市收复4月2日来失地</h2>
<p>据<a href="https://wallstreetcn.com/articles/3746912?keyword=%E5%95%86%E5%8A%A1%E9%83%A8" target="_blank" rel="noopener">商务部</a>，12日，中美各取消了共计91%的加征关税，暂停实施24%的反制关税。这一降幅超出市场预期，中国股市已完全收复4月2日来13%的跌幅。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">高盛表示，截至5月14日收盘，中国股市已完全收复4月2日后的跌幅，中国离岸市场股票和在岸市场分别收复了13%和7%的跌幅。MSCI中国、沪深300和恒生科技指数现在较4月初高点上涨2-4%。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">从板块表现看，硬件科技、工业和消费板块领涨，新兴市场出口商和国内受益者主题表现突出。相比之下，医疗保健、美国出口商和政府支出相关标的表现落后。<strong>年初至今，中国离岸市场仍是全球表现最好的股票市场之一，涨幅达17%，而MSCI新兴市场（不含中国）和发达市场指数分别上涨6%和3%。</strong></p>
<h2 style="text-align: left;">经济增长预期上调，股市目标调整4月2日前水平</h2>
<p style="text-align: left;">鉴于关税降幅超预期以及过去一个月美国金融环境宽松，高盛经济研究团队做出了几项预测调整：</p>
<blockquote>
<ol>
<li>
<p style="text-align: left;">美国方面：将2025年增长预期上调0.5个百分点至1%（环比年率），同时将12个月内衰退概率降至35%。美联储降息时间推后，预计将从12月FOMC会议开始，以每隔一次会议25个基点的节奏进行三次降息，而非此前预测的7月开始连续降息。</p>
</li>
<li>
<p style="text-align: left;">中国方面：将2025年和2026年实际GDP增长预期上调，同时货币和财政政策的宽松程度可能略低于此前预期。</p>
</li>
</ol>
</blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>高盛预计，MSCI中国和沪深300指数在未来12个月分别达到84点和4600点（较此前预测的78点和4400点有所上调），几乎与4月初的预期完全一致，分别存在11%和17%的潜在上涨空间。</strong></p>
<p>高盛认为，互联网与服务行业将受益于消费复苏与数字化转型加速。同时，在政策宽松周期下，优质区域银行与头部房企估值修复可期。在政策刺激受益领域，基建产业链包括建材、工程机械以及新能源汽车等有望巩固发展势头。</p>
<p>围绕结构性增长主题，高盛建议关注精选AI产业链，如算力基础设施（GPU服务器、光模块）、垂直场景应用（智能驾驶、工业软件）等；新兴市场出口商，如拓展东盟、中东市场的制造业龙头；以及股东回报提升主题相关的高股息国企改革标的、股份回购力度加大的消费白马等。</p>
<p> </p>

Title:  德鲁肯米勒一季度：减持谷歌、亚马逊、特斯拉，买入台积电和AppLovin 
Description:  <p>华尔街传奇投资者、有“史上最伟大的赚钱机器”之称的斯坦利·德鲁肯米勒（Stanley Druckenmiller）在2025年第一季度的投资组合调整中动作频频。</p>
<p>根据提交给美国证券交易委员会（SEC）的文件，德鲁肯米勒旗下的Duquesne Family Office<strong>在一季度完全清仓了37只股票，减持了包括谷歌、亚马逊和特斯拉在内的多只科技股，还削减了对美国航空公司的押注，</strong>似乎已经平仓了大量与American Airlines Group股票挂钩的看涨期权。</p>
<p>与此同时，<strong>Duquesne在本季度共新增12只股票，包括台积电和AppLovin的股份，</strong>还增持了包括Teva Pharmaceutical Industries Ltd在内的几只医疗股。同时增加了对 Coupang的投资，该公司目前已成为Duquesne的主要持仓之一。</p>
<p>截至2025年第一季度，德鲁肯米勒投资主要集中在9个行业：医疗保健、科技、消费周期性、工业、能源、消费必需品、金融服务、基础材料和通信服务。医疗保健和科技行业占据了投资组合的主导地位。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/09a826c7-a804-485b-aea9-bde151eb8f43.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="632" data-wscnw="870"/></p>
<h2>重仓“新宠”：DocuSign、CCC智能解决方案与EQT公司</h2>
<p><strong>德鲁肯米勒在本季度共新增12只股票</strong>，其中最大的新增持仓是Docusign Inc，购入107.47万股，价值8748万美元，占投资组合的2.86%，表明他看好数字签名和文档管理市场。</p>
<p>第二大新增持仓为CCC Intelligent Solutions Holdings Inc，购入559.5万股，价值5052万美元，占投资组合的1.65%。第三大新增持仓是EQT Corp，购入85.93万股，价值4592万美元，占投资组合的1.5%。</p>
<h2>“加码”巨头：Teva和台积电成增持重点</h2>
<p>截止第一季度，德鲁肯米勒最大持仓为Natera Inc（一家基因检测公司），占比15.72%，其他主要持仓包括：Teva Pharmaceutical Industries Ltd占7.47%、Coupang Inc占6.67%、Woodward Inc占6.55%和Philip Morris International Inc占5.73%。</p>
<p>与此同时，德鲁肯米勒大幅增持了台积电的股票，增加了49.13万股，使总持股量达到59.88万股，增幅高达456.93%，总价值9940万美元。</p>
<h2>清仓大戏：37只持仓“灰飞烟灭”</h2>
<p>德鲁肯米勒在本季度完全清仓了37只股票。</p>
<p>最引人注目的撤资包括Skechers USA Inc的全部107.48万股，对投资组合造成1.94%的负面影响；以及SLM Corp的全部252.03万股，对组合产生1.87%的负面影响。</p>
<h2>战略缩减：科技股持仓重大调整</h2>
<p><strong>值得注意的是，德鲁肯米勒在科技领域做出了一系列重大调整，减持了包括谷歌、亚马逊和特斯拉在内的多只科技股。</strong></p>
<p>他还减持了Seagate Technology Holdings PLC134.46万股，这使得该公司在其投资组合中的份额下降了85.97%，影响组合比例3.12%。该股票在本季度的平均交易价格为94.51美元，过去3个月回报率6.74%，今年迄今为25.49%。</p>
<p>另一个显著减持是United Airlines Holdings Inc 67.51万股，减持比例高达64.68%，对投资组合影响1.76%。该航空股在季内平均交易价格为94.43美元，但表现不佳，过去3个月下跌26.59%，今年至今下跌21.17%。</p>
<h2>投资组合总体概览：医疗保健领域占据主导</h2>
<p><strong>截至2025年第一季度，德鲁肯米勒投资主要集中在9个行业：医疗保健、科技、消费周期性、工业、能源、消费必需品、金融服务、基础材料和通信服务。</strong>医疗保健和科技行业占据了投资组合的主导地位。</p>

Title:  美日协议，七月底前没戏？ 
Description:  <p>石破茂政府遭遇严峻挑战。国内选举压力下，日本政府或寻求与美达成一份“更好的”协议，美日或无法在7月参议院选举前达成协议。</p>
<p>根据<a href="https://www.news.cn/world/20250512/356c2ae86b9a4c21a27bf98bb31dc120/c.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">新华网报道</a>，日本首相石破茂12日表示，不能接受在不包含汽车领域的情况下与美方达成协议，也不会为了汽车产业而牺牲农业、以扩大进口美国大米作为谈判筹码。希望日美关税谈判能在确保日本国家利益的基础上取得成果。</p>
<p><strong>日美目前已举行两轮关税谈判，日方持续要求美方重新审视关税措施，但美方一直坚持不能在汽车、钢铁等产品上给予日本“特殊待遇”。</strong></p>
<p>作为美国在亚洲的盟友，日本渴望避免与华盛顿的关系恶化，日本首相石破茂最初的首要任务是抢在其他国家之前坐到美国的谈判桌上。</p>
<p>但来自商界领袖和石破茂所在自民党成员的压力迫使他重新考虑，拒绝任何危及汽车行业或威胁国内农民的协议。</p>
<p><strong>汽车是美日贸易争端的“主战场”。2024年汽车占日本对美贸易顺差的81%。</strong>行业分析认为，本财年，美国关税对日本车企营业利润的影响将达到2万亿日元（约合137亿美元），尽管这种影响可以通过提价等措施来抵消。</p>
<p><strong>石破茂目前领导着一个脆弱的执政联盟，他担心一份一边倒的协议将加深执政党自民党的危机。在日本官员们看来，7月底日本参议院选举之前达成协议的可能性不大。</strong></p>
<p>如果贸然妥协，达成对美有利协议，7月份的参议院选举可能会对石破茂政府造成进一步的损害：一份向美国农产品进口敞开闸门的协议，将被日本国内农业游说团体视作“背叛”，进而影响整个自民党的选情。</p>
<p>目前尚不清楚日本对白宫有多大的影响力。东京在安全方面依赖华盛顿，其2024-2025财年对美商品贸易顺差达630亿美元。特朗普政府指责日本故意压低日元汇率，这进一步加剧了谈判的复杂性。</p>
<p>目前日本最有力的提议可能是增加购买美国农产品、扩大美国汽车的市场准入以及投资阿拉斯加液化天然气管道项目。</p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p>

Title: Why new Starbucks dress code prompted a reported 2,000 baristas to strike
Description: <p>Hundreds of<a href="https://www.axios.com/2024/12/20/starbucks-union-strikes" target="_blank"> Starbucks</a> workers have walked off the job at over 100 U.S. stores this week in a strike that's protesting <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/12/starbucks-dress-code-baristas-green-aprons" target="_blank">a new dress code</a> that went into effect this week.</p><p><strong>The big picture: </strong>Axios' Kelly Tyko notes the <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/03/03/starbucks-menu-changes-march-4-spring-drinks-launch" target="_self">Seattle-based coffee giant</a> is trying to revitalize the brand amid <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/01/mcdonalds-restaurants-fast-food-recession-starbucks" target="_blank">sluggish sales</a> by returning to its roots with a new design Starbucks says provides "simplified color options that allow our iconic green apron to shine." But the change sparked outrage with the baristas union.</p><hr><ul><li>Starbucks and the union, Starbucks Workers United, still haven't reached an agreement on a contract despite <a href="https://www.axios.com/2024/02/27/starbucks-union-negotiations-collective-bargaining" target="_blank">beginning negotiations</a> in February last year — something the union pointed to in a Bluesky <a href="https://bsky.app/profile/sbworkersunited.org/post/3lp62mbnkpc2u" target="_blank">post</a> on the strike that began Sunday.</li><li>"We're not just angry over a shirt color," said the Wednesday post. "Starbucks is a MASSIVE company without focus. They refuse to staff our stores properly, give guaranteed hours to workers, pay us a living wage, or provide stipends to pay for this arbitrary dress code.  We need fair union contracts NOW."</li></ul><p><strong>Driving the news: </strong>Starbucks said in its <a href="https://about.starbucks.com/stories/2025/updating-our-dress-code-for-a-more-consistent-coffeehouse-experience/" target="_blank">announcement</a> that its "more defined color palette includes any solid black short and long-sleeved crewneck, collared, or button-up shirts and any shade of khaki, black, or blue denim bottoms" and it's "making a new line of company branded t-shirts available to partners, who will receive two at no cost."</p><ul><li>The company said it wants to "create a sense of familiarity for our customer."</li></ul><p><strong>What they're saying: </strong>A striking barista said in a <a href="https://bsky.app/profile/sbworkersunited.org/post/3lp7sqegmgs24" target="_blank">video</a> posted Thursday to the union's Bluesky account that Starbucks "made a big decision about our jobs without bargaining with us, and this time it's a new restrictive dress code, one that we're paying for out of pocket." </p><ul><li>Wearing black "doesn't make the customer experience any better" and "policing" what workers wear doesn't address being short-staffed or dealing with long lines while there are pay concerns, said the worker, who was not identified in the post.</li><li>"They think they can tell us how to dress, expecting us to spend money on new shoes or pants just to be in compliance with the new dress code while we're already stretched thin and struggling to pay our bills," she said.</li></ul><p><strong>The other side: </strong>As the strike expanded with the union reporting over 2,000 workers walked out Thursday, Starbucks said in a statement "more than 99% of our stores are open today serving customers — and have been all week," per <a href="https://apnews.com/article/starbucks-dress-code-baristas-strike-3a39bbf41247d2090afa9b487ccf3d97" target="_blank">AP</a>.</p><ul><li>"It would be more productive if the union would put the same effort into coming back to the table that they're putting into protesting wearing black shirts to work."</li></ul><p><strong>Flashback: </strong><a href="https://www.axios.com/2024/12/24/starbucks-strike-baristas-workers-united-union" target="_blank">Starbucks strike expands on Christmas Eve</a></p><p><a href="https://www.axios.com/2024/12/24/starbucks-strike-baristas-workers-united-union" target="_blank">
</a></p>

Title: Watch: How experts stumbled upon a priceless document in a university library
Description: A manuscript, once considered an unofficial copy of Magna Carta, is now believed to be genuine and ''one of the world's most valuable documents''.

Title: The DoD Audit Conundrum: Accountability Over Accounting
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">The DoD Audit Conundrum: Accountability Over Accounting</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><em><a href="https://realclearwire.com/articles/2025/05/13/the_dod_audit_conundrum_accountability_over_accounting_1109852.html">Via RealClearPolitics</a>,</em></p>

<p><strong>The Department of Defense (DoD) has failed every audit since 2018, costing taxpayers over $1 billion each year, marked by "disclaimers of opinion," along with thousands of formal “notices of findings and recommendations” (NFRs) from the auditors</strong>. The DoD Inspector General’s <a href="https://comptroller.defense.gov/Portals/45/Documents/afr/fy2024/DoD_FY24_Agency_Financial_Report.pdf">FY 2024 Agency Financial Report</a> documented 28 material weaknesses and more than $1 trillion in asset discrepancies, leading auditors to issue their seventh consecutive disclaimer.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/pentago.JPG?itok=l4Xdk2ue" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/pentago.JPG?itok=l4Xdk2ue"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="455b7195-6a36-4792-a59b-53f4eda35fcd" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="336" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/pentago.JPG?itok=l4Xdk2ue" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>Audits of the DoD’s financial statements, guided by Federal Accounting Standards Advisory Board (FASAB) rules based on private-sector Generally Accepted Accounting Principles (GAAP), assess the DoD’s $850 billion budget using the profit-driven reporting mechanisms of balance sheets and income statements. This approach is suitable for private-sector, profit-seeking businesses like Boeing, IBM, and General Motors, but not for the DoD, a public-sector, taxpayer-funded federal agency whose primary purpose is to defend the homeland, not generate profits. </p>

<p><strong>This mismatch stems from the 1990 <a href="https://www.gao.gov/assets/gao-20-566.pdf">Chief Financial Officers (CFO) Act</a>,</strong> which, although well-intended, has unfortunately caused Congress and the public to prioritize financial health over military accountability. Rather than seeking auditor opinions, Congress and taxpayers should look for answers to questions like: Did $5 billion buy 55 F-35 jets? Did $18 billion deliver five ships? Did $330 billion in Operations and Maintenance obligations ensure wartime readiness?</p>

<p>The complete inability of GAAP-based financial accounting and reporting to address such questions or explain the causes of ongoing inefficiency and waste, <strong>such as the Navy’s $1.8 billion wasted on cruiser modernization (<a href="https://www.gao.gov/products/gao-25-106749">2024 GAO audit)</a>, highlights GAAP’s irrelevance for an agency that spends, not earns.</strong></p>

<p>Instead, the DoD should implement a budgetary audit process focusing on the Statement of Budgetary Resources (SBR), incorporating managerial cost accounting as outlined in the Statement of Federal Financial Accounting Standards (SFFAS) 4, and utilizing AI-driven forensic analysis through the DoD’s <a href="https://www.ai.mil/Initiatives/Analytic-Tools/#:~:text=Advana,data%2Dbased%20decision%2Dmaking.">Advana data analytics platform</a>.</p>

<p>This transition would better synchronize audits with the DoD’s Planning, Programming, Budgeting, and Execution (PPBE) process, ensuring that the $850 billion enhances security, not just balances the books.</p>

<h2>The Problem: Scale and Systemic Flaws</h2>

<p>The DoD’s complexity dwarfs private-sector firms. The <a href="https://comptroller.defense.gov/Portals/45/Documents/afr/fy2022/DoD_FY22_Agency_Financial_Report.pdf">FY 2023 DoD Agency Financial Report</a> revealed that the DoD employed 2.1 million service members and 778,000 civilians across 4,600 global sites, managing $851.7 billion in discretionary funds—half of U.S. discretionary spending—and $3.8 trillion in assets, 70% of the government’s total.</p>

<p>Tracking these resources across 4,500 financial systems makes monitoring obligations and matching them to appropriations difficult; <strong>at least 232 are critical for <a href="https://www.gao.gov/assets/gao-02-29.pdf">internal controls</a> over data entry, transaction processing, and reporting—an auditing nightmare.</strong></p>

<p>For example, the <a href="https://www.fiscal.treasury.gov/files/reports-statements/financial-report/2022/gao-audit-report-2022.pdf">2022 GAO Audit</a> found discrepancies in 61% of $3.5 trillion in assets, and the <a href="https://comptroller.defense.gov/Portals/45/Documents/afr/fy2022/DoD_FY22_Agency_Financial_Report.pdf">2024 DoD Financial Agency report</a> found 28 material weaknesses, showing weak internal accounting controls, like failing to reconcile Fund Balances with Treasury (FBwT)—akin to a checkbook not matching a bank statement.</p>

<p>Issues include outdated systems, manual data entry, and training gaps. A  <a href="https://www.gao.gov/assets/820/817960.pdf">2023 GAO report </a>noted that 18 out of 22 financial systems faced workforce shortages, hindering modernization. Further, multi-year programs like aircraft development blur committed versus available funds, complicating audits. The result? Seven years of disclaimers, with headlines claiming the DoD “can’t pass an audit” and wastes taxpayer money.</p>

<p><strong>But is the DoD truly failing its fiduciary responsibility, or is it trapped in a flawed GAAP-based process irrelevant to its purpose?</strong> Cultural and political pressures, like Congress’s demand for “clean audits” to signal fiscal responsibility, perpetuate this misalignment, distracting from the real question: Are funds delivering security?</p>

<h2>Why GAAP and FASAB Fail the DoD</h2>

<p>GAAP, and by extension FASAB, measures profitability and equity for revenue-generating businesses. Boeing’s $66 billion revenue and $13 billion loss fit this model, but the DoD’s $850 billion budget is all outflows—$5 billion for F-35s, $145 billion for R&D, $330 billion for operations and maintenance, with no income to tally.</p>

<p><strong>FASAB’s directed balance sheets show $3.5 trillion in assets and a “net cost” of $821 billion spent in FY2022, mimicking GAAP’s business-focused standards.</strong> However, 37% of unverifiable assets, according to a <a href="https://www.fiscal.treasury.gov/files/reports-statements/financial-report/2022/gao-audit-report-2022.pdf">GAO Independent Auditor report</a>, aren’t a “loss” but record-keeping issues. In particular, material weaknesses contributing to $2.4 trillion or 61% in <a href="https://www.defense.gov/News/News-Stories/Article/Article/3219566/dod-makes-audit-progress-but-much-more-needs-to-happen-official-says/">untracked assets</a> and $14 billion in “missing” parts, flagging “ bookkeeping “control gaps, not “mission” gaps. </p>

<p>Former Navy Comptroller Russ Rumbaugh made this point in a recent <a href="https://breakingdefense.com/2024/08/navy-comptroller-erp-software-will-finally-enable-a-clean-audit-big-data-analytics/">interview:</a>  <em>“DoD is very accountable, it’s just not auditable,” </em>Rumbaugh told the conference. <em>“We know where the things that go ‘boom’ are, we know where the dollars get spent, [but] to answer those questions [to the satisfaction of auditors], we have to go ask a bunch of stove-piped systems.”</em></p>

<p>The DoD’s <a href="https://broadbandusa.ntia.doc.gov/resources/federal/federal-permitting/department-defense-dod#:~:text=DOD%20is%20the%20United%20States,at%20over%204%2C790%20sites%20worldwide.">4,800 sites</a> and <a href="https://comptroller.defense.gov/Portals/45/Documents/defbudget/FY2025/FY2025_Weapons.pdf#:~:text=The%20FY%202025%20President's%20Budget%20request%20for,Navy%2C%20and%2018%20with%20the%20Air%20Force.">2,000+ budget line items</a> for RDT&E and Procurement alone defy GAAP’s clean ledgers, asking “Is it financially healthy?” when the real question is, “What did the taxpayer get?”</p>

<h2>A Better Approach: Managerial Cost Accounting</h2>

<p>A budgetary review process using managerial cost accounting organizes financial data to help DoD leaders allocate resources efficiently—a cost-benefit approach, not a balance sheet. In a <a href="https://christopherhanks.substack.com/p/a-proposal-to-emphasize-managerial">published paper</a>, <em>A Proposal to Emphasize Managerial Cost  Accounting in the Department of Defense</em>, <a href="https://www.dau.edu/sites/default/files/2024-07/No.%202%20Issue%2051.pdf">Dr. Christopher Hanks</a>, a former RAND analyst, argues that the DoD has neglected this tool, which is “unappreciated and underused.”</p>

<p>He argues that<strong> the Statement of Federal Financial Accounting Standards 4 (<a href="https://files.fasab.gov/pdffiles/handbook_sffas_4.pdf">SFFAS 4</a>) mandated by Congress tracks costs to outputs and is a better approach to evaluating the DoD budget, </strong>ensuring funds align with goals. For example, $82 billion in aid for Ukraine can be traced to emergency laws and evaluated for outcomes.</p>

<p>Unlike GAAP, this approach monitors obligations (commitments), <strong>ensuring compliance with appropriations and justifying variances, not chasing asset-liability matches</strong>. Instead, it should assess how budget approvals are documented. Are controls preventing overspending? Are goods being produced efficiently and providing the intended capabilities? This shift better aligns with Congress’s mandate to spend effectively, not mimic private-sector accounting.</p>

<h2>Aligning Managerial Cost Accounting to DoD’s Budget Process</h2>

<p>The DoD uses a detailed, although cumbersome, process to develop its annual budget. It goes through several steps: aligning the president’s and defense secretary’s security strategy through planning, developing proposed funding for programs that support it, converting those programs into budget requests, and executing it, or what is referred to as the <a href="https://www.dau.edu/acquipedia-article/planning-programming-budgeting-execution-process-ppbe">Planning, Programming, Budgeting, and Execution (PPBE)</a> process.</p>

<p><strong>This process was first introduced in the 1960s by Secretary of Defense Robert McNamara,</strong> who brought this business-like budgeting process from Ford Motor Company to the DoD. It has undergone several adjustments and improvements, creating an arduous but, for the most part, effective method. However, it routinely receives scrutiny and is the subject of recent reform and questionable overhaul requests.</p>

<p>For instance, the recent congressionally directed <a href="https://ppbereform.senate.gov/finalreport/">PPBE Reform Commission</a> has called for stronger, more responsive connections between strategy and spending within the PPBE process. However, the commission's primary goal is to offer recommendations for the PPBE process that meet Congress’s demand for a “clean audit opinion.”</p>

<p>While the commission made several strong recommendations to enhance the PPBE process,<strong> it neglected to tackle the elephant in the room: the way the DoD conducts audits.</strong> Instead, it reinforced a business-oriented audit approach, focusing on better managing financial statements rather than recognizing that imitating them is the issue.</p>

<p>Integrating SFFAS 4 into PPBE is a better reform solution – tracking obligations to capabilities (e.g., $145 billion in R&D for 10 hypersonic missiles) and ensuring that funds deliver results. Changing the term “<em>costs</em>” to “<em>obligations</em>” (both measured in dollars) allows SFFAS 4 to more effectively support PPBE reform by addressing the question, “Does $850 billion of approved obligation authority in the DoD’s budget, executed as planned, fulfill the president’s security strategy?”</p>

<h2>AI-Driven Forensic Approach for Execution</h2>

<p>One of the primary challenges in achieving a clean audit is reconciling how the DoD distributes funds. Thousands of systems, hundreds of checkbooks, and various financial systems create an almost insurmountable bookkeeping task.</p>

<p><strong>Until recently, manual efforts by thousands of auditors—costing $4 billion in audit remediation since 2018—were necessary to examine DoD finances </strong>as if the DoD were a business struggling to reconcile billions in obligations and payments due to chaotic financial systems, poor bookkeeping, and internal control challenges—essentially trying to fit a square peg (accounting) into a round hole (accountability).</p>

<p>With the advent of AI and a more forensic accounting approach to execution, it has become possible to scour the DoD’s 4,500 financial systems to trace obligations, detect fraud and waste, and confirm legal transactions. Using the Advana platform, <strong>AI-driven forensic accounting can trace questionable spending</strong>, such as <a href="https://media.defense.gov/2024/Aug/12/2003521744/-1/-1/1/DODIG-2024-114.PDF">the DoD Inspector General’s 2023 report</a> that found “47 (or 80 percent) of the 59 contracts reviewed, DoD contracting officers did not obtain sufficient documentation to support their positive determination of financial responsibility…”</p>

<h2>What needs to change</h2>

<p>Is a traditional business audit suitable for the DoD, which does not generate revenue but relies on an annual influx of capital? Like most federal government agencies, the DoD depends on approved budgets from Congress to continue existing and operating. Like all businesses, it does not rely on sales to customers and profits for investors to assess its financial health.</p>

<p>What needs to change is a more practical approach to assessing the budget, one that seeks accountability in the utilization of capital rather than a strict audit of expenditures. Did the obligations effectively support the mission and achieve the intended outcomes? Were the obligations used efficiently, effectively, and correctly accounted for?</p>

<p>Furthermore, <strong>can the organization monitor every dollar of its commitments to ensure alignment with strategic objectives and compliance with legal requirements?</strong> Can internal controls effectively reduce fraud, waste, or abuse, and can this assessment inform next year's budget request by considering anticipated challenges and new initiatives?</p>

<p>This approach to the DoD audit situation is not merely a cultural shift; it signifies a new method for assessing how efficiently and effectively taxpayer funds are utilized by the DoD and how they support future funding needs.</p>

<h2>How It Works</h2>

<ul><li>SFFAS 4 for PPB tracks costs to capabilities: The $44 billion for F-35s allocates $30 billion to aircraft, $10 billion to spares, and $4 billion to training, aligning with national defense goals. It measures unit costs (e.g., cost per jet) and ensures funds are cost-effective and provide the intended capability.</li>
	<li>AI Forensics for Execution: AI using Advana analytics verifies obligations traced to laws, enhancing accountability—did $5 billion produce 55 F-35s? It flags waste, like $80 million in misallocated funds, by analyzing hundreds of DoD “checkbooks” across systems. A well-funded AI pilot could recover billions and trace them to obligations.</li>
	<li>Restoring Advana’s Role:  Advana, mandated by the 2018 NDAA, has drifted into logistics and readiness but should refocus on its initially intended “audit” role. Additional funding could integrate SFFAS 4 and AI, streamlining financial tracking and quickly paying for itself within a few years.</li>
</ul><h2>Recommendations</h2>

<ul><li>Amend the 1990 CFO Act by limiting the requirement for financial-statement audits at the DoD to the Statement of Budgetary Resources (SBR) alone.  Clean auditor opinions on SBRs will reflect, among other things, solutions to reconciling DoD’s checkbook problems and ensure that intended deliverables (e.g., $4 billion = ships) are tied to appropriations.</li>
	<li>Revise the FASAB mandate to prioritize SFFAS 4 managerial obligation accounting to support budgeting and AI forensics for execution, replacing GAAP/FASAB’s financial focus with a more accountable approach to DoD’s budget.</li>
	<li>Mandate SFFAS 4 in PPBE: The FY2026 NDAA should lock SFFAS 4 into budgeting, splitting $145 billion R&D into traceable costs (e.g., 10 hypersonic missiles that produce intended capability), not vague assets.</li>
	<li>nbsp;       Fund AI Forensics: Launch a DoD Inspector General AI pilot, testing, for example, $50 billion in procurement. Scale it to $850 billion, flagging obligations like “F-35 spares and parts to meet future operations and maintenance requirements.”</li>
	<li>Reintegrate Advana: Refocus Advana on audit readiness with proper funding, incorporating SFFAS 4 and AI to trace funds. Train financial staff and associate managers to support implementation.</li>
</ul><h2>Conclusion</h2>

<p>The DoD’s audit failures stem from applying GAAP’s profit lens to a spender’s mission. Seven disclaimers, over $1 trillion in asset discrepancies, and 28 weaknesses prove FASAB’s flaws. SFFAS 4 and AI forensics offer a fix: $18 billion = 5 ships, $5 billion = 55 F-35s, traceable to law, not ledgers.</p>

<p>Amending the CFO Act, mandating SFFAS 4, and funding AI and Advana will deliver accountability. Despite challenges like training and resistance, a phased approach ensures feasibility. Congress and taxpayers deserve answers to “What’d we get?” not “Where’s the receipt?” This shift makes $850 billion count.</p>

<p><em>Major General Don McGregor (USAF, ret.) is a combat veteran and an F-16 fighter pilot. While serving as a General Officer in the Pentagon, he was the National Guard Director of Strategy, Policy, Plans, and International Affairs, advising a four-star Joint Chiefs of Staff member. He is an expert in defense strategy, policy, planning, and global security and has been published in several defense news outlets. He holds a B.A. in Computer Science from the University of Minnesota and a master’s degree in Diplomacy and International Conflict Resolution from Norwich University.  General McGregor would like to acknowledge Dr. Christopher Hanks, a defense analyst and working capital funds expert, for his review and beneficial suggestions regarding the content. </em></p>
